# Critical Minerals Explorer Fact-Checking

# Samarium

## **1\) US & allies ‚Äî current production (mined REO and what that implies for Sm)**

**United States (Mountain Pass, CA)**

* ‚úÖ *There is one operating rare‚Äëearth mine in the U.S.*

* üîé **Numbers:** In **2024**, U.S. mine output was **\~45,000 t REO (in mineral concentrates)**, per USGS. MP Materials separately reports a **record 45,455 t REO** and **1,294 t NdPr oxide** produced in 2024; it also **began commercial NdPr metal** and **trial magnet** production late 2024\. [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)[MP Materials](https://investors.mpmaterials.com/investor-news/news-details/2025/MP-Materials-Reports-Fourth-Quarter-and-Full-Year-2024-Results/default.aspx)

* ‚ö†Ô∏è **Important nuance:** Saying U.S. ‚Äúsamarium production is essentially this REO output‚Äù is **incorrect**. Mountain Pass is **Ce/La/Nd/Pr‚Äëdominant bastn√§site**; Sm occurs only as a **minor fraction** of TREO and is **not** produced as a separated Sm oxide/metal at scale today in the U.S. (MP‚Äôs initial separation focus is NdPr). Treating the whole REO tonnage as ‚Äúsamarium‚Äù overstates U.S. Sm supply by **\~two orders of magnitude**. [MP Materials](https://investors.mpmaterials.com/investor-news/news-details/2025/MP-Materials-Reports-Fourth-Quarter-and-Full-Year-2024-Results/default.aspx)[U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)

**Australia**

* ‚ö†Ô∏è Your figure ‚Äú\~0.016 Mt REO in 2022‚Äù (16 kt) is *not representative of Australia‚Äôs current mine output*. According to USGS, **Australia mined \~113,000 t REO in 2024** (and \~116,000 t in 2023\) ‚Äî an order of magnitude higher ‚Äî dominated by Lynas‚Äô Mt Weld. Browns Range remains **pilot-scale** (hundreds of tonnes of RE carbonate in some years), not 2‚Äì3 kt/year. [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)

**Canada**

* ‚úÖ *No sustained commercial REE mine production at present.* USGS lists **no Canadian mine output** in 2023‚Äì2024. (Vital Metals‚Äô small Nechalacho effort was curtailed; Canada‚Äôs main activity today is **processing R\&D** such as the **Saskatchewan Research Council (SRC) Rare Earth Processing Facility**.) [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)[Annual Reports](https://www.annualreports.com/HostedData/AnnualReportArchive/n/ASX_NTU_2019.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**EU/Norway**

* ‚ö†Ô∏è *Corrections:*

  * **Kaunisvaara** is **an iron‚Äëore mine** in Sweden (operating since 2018 under Kaunis Iron). It is **not** a past REE mine. [Kaunis Iron](https://www.kaunisiron.se/en/our-operations/mines/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **Mining:** As of 2024‚Äì2025, **no EU or Norwegian REE mines** are in commercial production. However, **Rare Earths Norway (Fen carbonatite)** has announced a JORC‚Äëcompliant **inferred resource \~559 Mt @ 1.57% TREO (\~8.8 Mt TREO)** ‚Äî a *resource*, not a producing mine. Any mining is **years away**. [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/rare-earths-norway-says-its-ree-discovery-is-europes-largest/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **Processing exists in Europe:** **Solvay (France)** supplies **\~4,000 t/yr** separated RE oxides; **REEtec (Norway)** targets **\~720 t/yr NdPr** starting 2025\. That‚Äôs processing, not mining. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[TechMet Ltd](https://www.techmet.com/assets/reetec/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Japan**

* ‚úÖ *No domestic REE mines; reliant on imports.* (Japan focuses on mid‚Äë/downstream tech and recycling.) [USGS](https://www.usgs.gov/data/chemistry-data-rare-earth-carbonate-minerals-mountain-pass-rare-earth-element-deposit?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Bottom line (current):**  
 The U.S. mines \~45 kt REO (mostly LREE, Sm is minor); Australia is the allied mining heavyweight at \~113 kt REO; Canada/EU/Norway/Japan have **no mining** at scale yet. Don‚Äôt equate REO tonnage with ‚ÄúSm production.‚Äù [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)

---

## **2\) US & allies ‚Äî 2030 demand for Sm (order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude check)**

* **Where Sm is used:** chiefly **SmCo permanent magnets** (high‚Äëtemperature/defense/aerospace, specialty motors) and **burnable poisons in reactors** (Sm‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ has been used, e.g., in Belgium‚Äôs BR2 program). [researchportal.sckcen.be](https://researchportal.sckcen.be/files/270154/CR_report.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Market size clues:** A reputable industry report puts **North America‚Äôs SmCo magnet demand at \~475 t in 2024**, trending to \~575 t by 2033\. [IMARC Group](https://www.imarcgroup.com/north-america-samarium-cobalt-magnets-market?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Converting magnets ‚Üí Sm metal:**

  * **SmCo‚ÇÖ** magnets are **\~36 wt% Sm**. [Stanford Magnets](https://www.stanfordmagnets.com/smco-magnets-composition-series-and-types.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **Sm‚ÇÇCo‚ÇÅ‚Çá** magnets are generally **\~25 wt% Sm** (typical). [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samarium%E2%80%93cobalt_magnet?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * So **475 t of SmCo magnets ‚âà 120‚Äì170 t of Sm metal** (25‚Äì36% range) for **North America alone** in 2024\. Extrapolating to the **U.S.+EU+Japan** suggests **‚Äúa few hundred tonnes of Sm metal per year‚Äù** for allied markets by 2030 is **plausible** ‚Äî but still **small compared with NdFeB** markets. (Nuclear Sm demand exists but is modest relative to magnets.) [IMARC Group](https://www.imarcgroup.com/north-america-samarium-cobalt-magnets-market?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Stanford Magnets](https://www.stanfordmagnets.com/smco-magnets-composition-series-and-types.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samarium%E2%80%93cobalt_magnet?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Policy targets:** The EU‚Äôs **CRMA** aims by **2030** to **process 40%** and **recycle 25%** of strategic raw materials domestically (and **mine 10%**), but there is **no specific ‚Äú30% magnet‚Äù onshoring target in U.S. law** that I can source. Your ‚ÄúU.S. 30% magnet supply onshore by 2030‚Äù line should be **removed or re‚Äësourced**. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/companies-forging-rare-earths-industry-eu-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Takeaway:** Your magnitude (‚Äúfew √ó10¬≤ to \~10¬≥ t Sm‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ/yr by 2030 for allies‚Äù) is **reasonable** as a **broad range**, but please frame it as a **range with caveats** and cite actual market tonnage where available (e.g., NA \~475 t SmCo in 2024). [IMARC Group](https://www.imarcgroup.com/north-america-samarium-cobalt-magnets-market?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **3\) US & allies ‚Äî 2030 supply outlook (what‚Äôs realistic)**

* **U.S.:** Mountain Pass likely remains the backbone (order‚Äëof‚Äë**\~45 kt REO/yr** based on recent actuals). MP is now producing **NdPr oxide** and **NdPr metal** and piloting magnet output in Texas, but there is **no announced Sm separation line**. Treating the full 45 kt REO as ‚Äúfuture Sm supply‚Äù would be **incorrect**; **Sm is a small minor** in its LREE concentrate. [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)[MP Materials](https://investors.mpmaterials.com/investor-news/news-details/2025/MP-Materials-Reports-Fourth-Quarter-and-Full-Year-2024-Results/default.aspx)

  * **Ramaco ‚ÄúBrook Mine‚Äù (WY):** AP confirms a **$533M** plan to recover critical minerals from coal‚Äërelated materials, but **no credible public tonnage** supports ‚Äúa few Mt of REO concentrate.‚Äù That claim should be **deleted** or clearly labeled **speculative** until bankable studies are published. [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2024/mcs2024-rare-earths.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Canada:** The **SRC Rare Earth Processing Facility** in Saskatchewan is a **processing demonstration** (NdPr oxide and eventually metal), not a mine; capacities are **pilot/early‚Äëcommercial** scale. Upstream Canadian REE mines for 2030 remain **uncertain**. Your ‚Äúfew kt/yr REO by 2030‚Äù for Canada is **possible** but **unproven**; cite project‚Äëspecific NI 43‚Äë101s when available. [Annual Reports](https://www.annualreports.com/HostedData/AnnualReportArchive/n/ASX_NTU_2019.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia:** In addition to Mt Weld, **Iluka‚Äôs Eneabba refinery (WA)** is under construction; third‚Äëparty and company materials indicate **\~23,000 t/yr separated REO capacity** when complete, including **\~4 kt/yr NdPr and \~0.75 kt/yr Dy+Tb** in some planning cases. First product is targeted in the **mid‚Äëto‚Äëlate 2020s** (variously 2026‚Äì2027 in recent updates). This materially expands allied **processing** capacity (not mine tonnage). [Fluor](https://www.fluor.com/projects/iluka-rare-earths?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[The Australian Mining Review](https://australianminingreview.com.au/issue/2025/04/rare-earths-revolution-ilukas-eneabba-refinery/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Listcorp](https://www.listcorp.com/asx/ilu/iluka-resources-limited/news/eneabba-rare-earths-refinery-update-presentation-3127414.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Company Announcements](https://company-announcements.afr.com/asx/ilu/9c42bb53-e936-11ed-9428-f6ba9bacc4fd.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **EU/Norway:** Mining by 2030 is **uncertain**. REN‚Äôs **Fen** resource (8.8 Mt TREO) is promising but **still an inferred resource**; permitting/build‚Äëout will likely push first production into the **2030s**. Processing: **Solvay \~4,000 t/yr** separated REOs is active; **REEtec \~720 t/yr NdPr** is ramping. These help **NdPr** more than **Sm** specifically. [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/rare-earths-norway-says-its-ree-discovery-is-europes-largest/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[TechMet Ltd](https://www.techmet.com/assets/reetec/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**What that means for Sm volumes in 2030:**  
 Even if allied mine **REO** output (U.S.+Australia+Canada) surpasses **\~150‚Äì170 kt REO/yr**, the **Sm share** of that stream is **small** (often **\~1‚Äì2% of TREO** in LREE‚Äëdominant deposits; exact ratios vary by ore and circuit). Without **dedicated midstream circuits** to **separate and refine Sm**, **available Sm‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ** will remain **‚Äúhundreds of tonnes per year‚Äù scale** for allied users ‚Äî **not** multi‚Äëkilotons ‚Äî and still **tight relative to defense/aerospace pull**. (This is an inference from deposit chemistry and today‚Äôs separation focus; it aligns with the small scale of the SmCo magnet market compared with NdFeB.) [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)

**Edit to your text:** The line ‚ÄúSumming announced projects suggests allied capacity on the order of 100‚Äì200 kt/yr LCE ‚Ä¶ for Sm‚Äù doesn‚Äôt apply (that LCE framing is lithium‚Äëspecific). For samarium/REE, replace with a **Sm‚Äëspecific** statement emphasizing **minor‚Äëelement recovery** and **separation bottlenecks**, not bulk REO tonnage.

## **4\) ‚ÄúReferences for volumes‚Äù ‚Äî accuracy check**

* **MP Materials 2024 production:** Good source, but update the figures to **45,455 t REO** and **1,294 t NdPr oxide**; note **NdPr metal and trial magnet production commenced**. [MP Materials](https://investors.mpmaterials.com/investor-news/news-details/2025/MP-Materials-Reports-Fourth-Quarter-and-Full-Year-2024-Results/default.aspx)

* **Australia production:** Replace the 2017‚Äì2022‚Äëvintage ‚Äú\~16 kt‚Äù line with **current mine production**: **Australia \~113,000 t REO (2024)** per **USGS MCS 2025**. Browns Range is **pilot**; avoid citing it as 2‚Äì3 kt/yr. [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)

* **‚ÄúNorway 8.8 Mt REO reserve‚Äù:** It‚Äôs a **JORC inferred resource** of **8.8 Mt TREO** at **Fen**, not a reserve and **not yet a mine**. Clarify this. [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/rare-earths-norway-says-its-ree-discovery-is-europes-largest/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **SRC (Canada):** The **facility is demonstration‚Äëscale**; I could not substantiate ‚Äú40 t/month‚Äù or ‚Äú10 t/month‚Äù claims in SRC‚Äôs official releases; instead cite SRC‚Äôs facility description (NdPr separation and metal pilot capability). [Annual Reports](https://www.annualreports.com/HostedData/AnnualReportArchive/n/ASX_NTU_2019.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **5\) Discovery, extraction, separation & remediation ‚Äî technical notes**

Most of your technology descriptions are **directionally correct**, but tighten the sourcing and remove a few over‚Äëconfident claims:

* **Exploration geophysics:** Radiometrics, gravity, and magnetics are indeed standard for REE targeting; treat vendor blogs as *illustrative*, not definitive sources. Consider citing a government/GS document (e.g., GA/USGS) for best practice. (Your MAJR Resources links are acceptable as examples.)

* **Hyperspectral ‚ÄúNd feature‚Äù:** Hyperspectral can map REE‚Äërelated alteration; keep claims conservative unless you cite a peer‚Äëreviewed case that specifically resolved Nd/Sm features in the field.

* **Processing:**

  * **Flotation of bastn√§site/monazite** and **acid baking/caustic digests** are standard.

  * **SX:** Your D2EHPA example is supported (near‚Äëquantitative Ce/La/Nd extraction from monazite tailings leachates in staged systems). [MDPI](https://www.mdpi.com/2075-163X/12/8/948?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **Sm metal production:** Industrially, Sm is produced via **molten‚Äësalt electrolysis of SmCl‚ÇÉ in LiCl‚ÄìKCl** or **metallothermic reduction under vacuum** with **condensation (distillative) purification** ‚Äî the general routes you describe are consistent with the literature. [SpringerLink](https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s12613-020-2112-2?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Sci-Hub](https://moscow.sci-hub.box/1325/d37cb8a3160a145332cd3187a57d8571/10.1016%40j.electacta.2011.07.059.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Environmental practice:** MP‚Äôs site is **net‚Äëzero discharge** and **recycles ‚âà95% of process water**; that example is correctly framed. [MP Materials+1](https://mpmaterials.com/sustainability/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **6\) Bottleneck ‚Äî is your conclusion right?**

* **Yes ‚Äî the key bottleneck is midstream separation/refining (and magnets), not geology.** China still dominates **separation and magnet manufacturing**. The West is adding capacity (**Solvay France \~4 kt/yr separated REOs; REEtec Norway \~720 t/yr NdPr; MP begins NdPr metal & trial magnets; Iluka‚Äôs Eneabba refinery** coming) but Sm‚Äëspecific lines remain **limited**, so **Sm‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ/Sm metal availability** in allied markets will **stay tight** without targeted separation trains and magnet alloy capacity. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[TechMet Ltd](https://www.techmet.com/assets/reetec/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MP Materials](https://investors.mpmaterials.com/investor-news/news-details/2025/MP-Materials-Reports-Fourth-Quarter-and-Full-Year-2024-Results/default.aspx)[Fluor](https://www.fluor.com/projects/iluka-rare-earths?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **7\) A corrected 2025 baseline & 2030 view (concise)**

* **2024 mining (REO, mined):** **U.S. \~45 kt; Australia \~113 kt; Canada/EU/Norway/Japan \~0.** (Mining only.) [U.S. Geological Survey Publications+1](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)

* **Processing (selected):** Solvay (FR) **\~4 kt/yr separated REO**; REEtec (NO) **\~720 t/yr NdPr (start‚Äëup)**; MP (US) **NdPr oxide/metal \+ trial magnets**; Iluka (AU) refinery **\~23 kt/yr separated REO capacity** under construction. **Sm separation remains niche.** [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[TechMet Ltd](https://www.techmet.com/assets/reetec/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MP Materials](https://investors.mpmaterials.com/investor-news/news-details/2025/MP-Materials-Reports-Fourth-Quarter-and-Full-Year-2024-Results/default.aspx)[Fluor](https://www.fluor.com/projects/iluka-rare-earths?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Sm demand marker:** **North America \~475 t SmCo magnets in 2024** ‚áí **\~120‚Äì170 t Sm metal**; allied markets in 2030 likely **a few hundred tonnes of Sm metal** (or **\~300‚Äì500 t Sm‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ**) annually, with defense/aerospace a sticky, temperature‚Äëcritical niche. [IMARC Group](https://www.imarcgroup.com/north-america-samarium-cobalt-magnets-market?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Stanford Magnets](https://www.stanfordmagnets.com/smco-magnets-composition-series-and-types.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samarium%E2%80%93cobalt_magnet?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **2030 supply risk:** Even if allied REO mining rises, **Sm output depends on separation circuits** that currently **prioritize NdPr/Dy/Tb**. Expect **continued import dependence for Sm** unless **Sm‚Äëfocused SX lines** and **SmCo alloy/magnet plants** are built and fed. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Kaunisvaara is iron ore (not REE):** [Kaunis Iron](https://www.kaunisiron.se/en/our-operations/mines/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

### **Final verdict**

* Your **overall conclusion** ‚Äî that the **bottleneck is midstream separation/refining (and magnets), not geology** ‚Äî is **correct**.

* The **biggest fixes** are: (i) don‚Äôt equate **REO tonnage with Sm output**; (ii) update **Australia** to \~**113 kt REO** (2024) and note Browns Range‚Äôs **pilot** status; (iii) correct **EU/Norway** (no mining yet; **Fen** is a resource); (iv) replace the **U.S. ‚Äú30% magnet‚Äù** policy claim with the **EU CRMA** targets or remove; and (v) **strike** the unsubstantiated ‚Äúfew Mt REO‚Äù claim for Ramaco.

## **Executive takeaways (what changes)**

* **Global scale:** Your ‚Äú\~30 t/y global production‚Äù is broadly right, but **South Africa‚Äôs mine output was \~17‚Äì18 t (not \~27 t)** in 2023‚Äì24. Johnson Matthey (JM) reports **global primary rhodium supply 21.8 t** in 2023, **secondary (recycled) 8.9 t**, **total 30.7 t**; South Africa‚Äôs mine share was **17.4 t** (‚âà80% of primary). [matthey.com](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)

* **North America today:** You materially **understate North American mine output.** JM shows **North American primary rhodium supply \~0.6 t in 2023** and **\~0.5 t in 2024** (US \+ Canada). Natural Resources Canada (NRCan) data imply **\~3,000 oz (\~0.093 t) of Canadian rhodium** in 2023, so **the United States contributes the remainder (\~0.4‚Äì0.5 t)**‚Äînot ‚Äúzero.‚Äù [matthey.com](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)[mmsd.nrcan-rncan.gc.ca](https://mmsd.nrcan-rncan.gc.ca/prod-prod/ann-ann-eng.aspx)[Natural Resources Canada](https://natural-resources.canada.ca/minerals-mining/mining-data-statistics-analysis/minerals-metals-facts/platinum-facts?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Demand & recycling:** Your 2030 demand ranges are plausible directionally, but **your allied supply estimate (3‚Äì5 t/y including recycling) is too low.** JM notes **\~9.2 t** of rhodium came from recycling globally in 2024 and that **\~43% of recycled rhodium came from vehicles first sold in North America**‚Äîalready ‚âà**4 t** tied to the NA fleet **today**. That means allied supply (mined \+ recycled) is likely **well above 3‚Äì5 t** barring a structural collapse in scrappage. [matthey.com+1](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)

* **Process flow:** The statement that new North American projects (e.g., Marathon) may use **HPAL/pressure oxidation instead of smelting/flotation** is **incorrect**. Marathon‚Äôs NI 43‚Äë101 FS specifies a **conventional crush‚Äìgrind‚Äìflotation Cu‚ÄëPGM concentrate** flowsheet (concentrate then smelting/refining), not HPAL. [International Mining](https://im-mining.com/2021/03/03/gen-mining-reports-positive-fs-marathon-palladium-copper-project-including-use-woodgrove-direct-flotation-reactors/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Wheaton Precious Metals](https://www.wheatonpm.com/portfolio/development-projects/marathon/default.aspx?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Key bottleneck:** Your main conclusion‚Äîthat **geology (lack of a large allied orebody) and dependence on imports/recycling, not ‚Äúmissing lab tech,‚Äù is the choke point**‚Äîis sound. USGS confirms **only one US company** mines PGMs and JM shows **SA dominates primary supply.** [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-platinum-group.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[matthey.com](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)

# Rhodium

## **Detailed fact check**

### **US & allies ‚Äì current production**

* **United States:**  
   *Claim:* ‚ÄúThe United States reported no rhodium output in 2023.‚Äù  
   *Check:* JM‚Äôs regional table shows **North America primary rhodium supply \~0.6 t in 2023, \~0.5 t in 2024**. NRCan‚Äôs breakdown puts Canada near **0.093 t** (see below), leaving **\~0.4‚Äì0.5 t** attributable to the US (rhodium in Stillwater/East Boulder concentrates). In other words, **US rhodium output is small, but not zero.** [matthey.com](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)[mmsd.nrcan-rncan.gc.ca](https://mmsd.nrcan-rncan.gc.ca/prod-prod/ann-ann-eng.aspx)  
   USGS also notes **one company in Montana mined and processed PGMs** in 2024‚Äîconsistent with that interpretation. [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-platinum-group.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)  
   Sibanye‚ÄëStillwater reports **425,842 oz 2E (Pt+Pd) in 2024**, with smelting/refining at its **Columbus, MT** complex, and confirms the tailings/backfill practices you mention. [Sibanye-Stillwater](https://www.sibanyestillwater.com/business/americas/pgm-operations-americas/stillwater-east-boulder/)

* **Canada:**  
   *Claim:* ‚Äú\~3,000 oz Rh (‚âà0.093 t) in 2023.‚Äù  
   *Check:* NRCan ‚ÄúPlatinum facts‚Äù gives Canada‚Äôs 2023 total PGM output (\~702,000 oz) and shows **rhodium \~0.4%** of Canadian PGM production, which is ‚âà**3,000 oz**. This aligns with your number. (The NRCan page shows the 0.4% split; the ‚ÄúPlatinum group quantity produced‚Äù table shows **23,210,854 g of PGMs** in 2024p; 0.4% of that order of magnitude maps to \~3,000 oz.) [Natural Resources Canada+1](https://natural-resources.canada.ca/minerals-mining/mining-data-statistics-analysis/minerals-metals-facts/platinum-facts?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[mmsd.nrcan-rncan.gc.ca](https://mmsd.nrcan-rncan.gc.ca/prod-prod/ann-ann-eng.aspx)  
   Note: Lac des Iles is now **Impala Canada** (acquired in 2019), not ‚ÄúNorth American Palladium.‚Äù (That naming update doesn‚Äôt affect your quantity.) [blog.gorozen.com](https://blog.gorozen.com/blog/the-hidden-revival-of-platinum-and-palladium)

* **Australia / EU / Japan / Nordics:**  
   *Claim:* ‚ÄúNo rhodium mines.‚Äù  
   *Check:* Correct in practice: there is **no material primary rhodium mine production** in these allied regions at present (refining exists, mining doesn‚Äôt). USGS and JM attribute primary rhodium supply overwhelmingly to **South Africa**, plus **Russia and Zimbabwe**, with a small North American contribution. [matthey.com](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)[U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2024/mcs2024-platinum-group.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Global context & South Africa:**  
   *Claim:* ‚ÄúGlobal mine output \~30 t, South Africa \~26.9 t in 2023.‚Äù  
   *Check:* **Partly right, partly wrong.** JM shows **global primary (mine) supply 21.8 t** and **secondary 8.9 t** in 2023, for **\~30.7 t total supply**. But **South Africa‚Äôs primary was 17.4 t**‚Äî**not** \~26.9 t. Your SA figure is overstated by \~55%. (SA‚Äôs share ‚âà80% of primary supply.) [matthey.com](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)

**Verdict:** Revise ‚ÄúUS zero‚Äù ‚Üí **US \~0.4‚Äì0.5 t** (within **NA \~0.6 t**), and revise ‚ÄúSouth Africa 26.9 t‚Äù ‚Üí **\~17‚Äì18 t**.

---

### **US & allies ‚Äì demand to 2030**

* **Magnitude & mix:**  
   Rhodium demand is still dominated by **autocatalysts**, with smaller shares in **chemical (nitric/acetic)**, **glass**, and **electronics**. JM reports **global rhodium demand 34.7 t (2023)** and **33.1 t (2024)**; it expects **another modest deficit** in 2025, with glass demand rebounding somewhat despite lower auto consumption. [matthey.com+1](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)

* **North America signal:**  
   JM explicitly notes **‚Äúimported cars sold in the USA accounted for well over 100,000 oz of rhodium use last year \[2024\]‚Äù**‚Äî**\>3.1 t** **from imports alone**, before counting US‚Äëbuilt vehicles and non‚Äëauto uses. That supports your directional claim that **NA demand is several tonnes per year** and gives context for 2030 ranges. [matthey.com](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM_Market_Report_25.pdf/5f4e4078-8e9a-3c96-d334-9d14da9de094?t=1747159713413)

* **Your 2030 ranges:**  
   Your ‚ÄúNA \~7 t, Europe \~5 t, Japan \~2 t; allies \~10‚Äì15 t‚Äù is **plausible as an order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude scenario**, but it‚Äôs **not sourced to a single forecast** and should be framed as an **illustrative scenario**‚Äîespecially because **BEV penetration, loadings (Euro 7, US Tier 3 completion), and thrifting** could push auto demand **down**, while **glass/chemical cycles** could push **up**. JM‚Äôs latest narrative points to **slightly lower automotive rhodium in 2025** but **glass turning positive**‚Äîit does **not** publish a 2030 rhodium by‚Äëregion forecast in the public report. [matthey.com+1](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Verdict:** Keep the ranges, but mark them as **scenario estimates**, anchored to **JM‚Äôs current totals (‚âà33 t global)** with uncertainty around EV adoption and loadings.

---

### **US & allies ‚Äì supply to 2030**

* **Primary (mined) supply:**  
   With no large new allied PGM mines, **primary allied rhodium output is likely to remain small** (stillwater/East Boulder in the US; Lac des Iles & potential new Canadian projects if they proceed). That said, **‚ÄúNorth America ‚â™0.1 t‚Äù** is **inaccurate**‚Äîwe are already at **\~0.5‚Äì0.6 t** primary. [matthey.com](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)

* **Secondary (recycling):**  
   Your estimate of **global recycling at \~10 t/y** is a bit high; JM has **8.9 t (2023)** and **9.2 t (2024)**. Crucially, **\~43%** of recycled rhodium in 2024 came from **vehicles first sold in North America**, i.e., **‚âà4 t** associated with the NA fleet alone. This single datum means **allied supply (mined+recycled)** will likely **exceed 3‚Äì5 t/y** in any normal scrappage environment. [matthey.com+1](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)

* **Bottom line:**  
   You‚Äôre directionally right that **allies will remain import‚Äëdependent**, but the **best‚Äëcase 3‚Äì5 t/y (mined \+ recycled)** you cite is **too low** against the current recycling base. A more defensible framing is: **primary allied supply \~0.5‚Äì0.7 t/y**, **secondary allied supply ‚Äúseveral tonnes‚Äù (‚âà4‚Äì6 t/y) depending on scrappage and price**, for a **total allied supply plausibly in the mid‚Äësingle‚Äëdigit tonnes**‚Äîstill **well below** a **10‚Äì15 t/y** allied demand scenario. [matthey.com+1](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)

---

### **Technologies (discovery ‚Üí extraction ‚Üí separation ‚Üí remediation)**

* **Exploration (geophysics, geochem, mapping):**  
   Your summary fits standard PGM exploration practice (magnetics+gravity for layered mafic/ultramafic intrusions; geochem and structural mapping in cratons). Provincial surveys (e.g., Manitoba) emphasize these approaches for PGE targets. [blog.gorozen.com](https://blog.gorozen.com/blog/the-hidden-revival-of-platinum-and-palladium?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Extraction/processing:**  
   *Correct:* comminution \+ **flotation** ‚Üí **smelting/converting** ‚Üí hydrometallurgy for PGMs (as at Sibanye‚ÄëStillwater/Columbus). [Sibanye-Stillwater](https://www.sibanyestillwater.com/business/americas/pgm-operations-americas/stillwater-east-boulder/)  
   *Needs correction:* **Marathon** (Ontario) does **not** plan HPAL/POX for PGMs; the FS specifies **conventional Cu‚ÄëPGM flotation** with Cu‚ÄëPGM concentrate off‚Äëtake for smelting/refining. [International Mining](https://im-mining.com/2021/03/03/gen-mining-reports-positive-fs-marathon-palladium-copper-project-including-use-woodgrove-direct-flotation-reactors/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Wheaton Precious Metals](https://www.wheatonpm.com/portfolio/development-projects/marathon/default.aspx?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Separation/refining:**  
   *Accurate in essence.* Industrial routes use **solvent extraction** and **ion exchange** on chloride liquors; **selective precipitation** of **ammonium hexachlororhodate, (NH‚ÇÑ)‚ÇÉ\[RhCl‚ÇÜ\]**, is a classical rhodium step, followed by **calcination/reduction** to metal. Modern reviews and resin vendor literature support the ion‚Äëexchange/SX details you give (Lewatit, etc.). [PMC](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC10342344/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[lanxess.com](https://lanxess.com/en-us/products-and-brands/products/l/lewatit--monoplus-tp-214?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0304386X14002783?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Remediation:**  
   Paste backfill/tailings management and water treatment references are consistent with operator disclosures. Sibanye‚ÄëStillwater states **\~52% of concentrator tailings returned underground at Stillwater**; East Boulder is \~44%. [Sibanye-Stillwater](https://www.sibanyestillwater.com/business/americas/pgm-operations-americas/stillwater-east-boulder/)

---

Also add the JM datapoint that **\>100,000 oz (\~3.1 t) of rhodium were embedded in imported cars sold in the US in 2024**. # Lutetium

## **Bottom‚Äëline assessment of your conclusions**

* **‚ÄúUS/allied primary rhodium supply is tiny and import‚Äëdependent.‚Äù** ‚úîÔ∏è Correct (but quantify NA primary at \~0.5‚Äì0.6 t/y, not ‚Äú‚â™0.1 t‚Äù). [matthey.com](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM-Market-Report-24.pdf)

* **‚ÄúRecycling will be crucial.‚Äù** ‚úîÔ∏è Correct‚Äîand already on the order of **\~4 t/y tied to the NA fleet** today. [matthey.com](https://matthey.com/documents/161599/509428/PGM_Market_Report_25.pdf/5f4e4078-8e9a-3c96-d334-9d14da9de094?t=1747159713413)

* **‚ÄúTech isn‚Äôt the main choke point; it‚Äôs resources & scale.‚Äù** ‚úîÔ∏è Correct. Even with advanced hydromet routes, without a **new, large allied orebody** the allied share of **primary** rhodium won‚Äôt move much; **recycling and imports** bridge the gap.

## **Quick verdict (what‚Äôs most off vs. solid)**

**Most off (needs correction):**

* **U.S. current REO output at Mountain Pass** is far higher than ‚Äúseveral hundred tonnes‚Äù‚ÄîUSGS reports **\~45,000 t REO (concentrate) in 2024**, and Mountain Pass is a **light‚ÄëREE (LREE) bastn√§site** system with **negligible heavy REE (HREE) content** such as lutetium. That means **U.S. primary Lu is effectively \~zero**, not hundreds of tonnes. [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)[USGS](https://www.usgs.gov/publications/complex-carbonate-ore-mineralogy-mountain-pass-carbonatite-rare-earth-element-deposit?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0169136824003871?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Global scale for lutetium** is small. Widely cited technical/industry references put **global Lu‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ output on the order of \~10 t/yr**, not hundreds. EU data show **EU Lu consumption \~5.6 t/yr (metal content)** in 2016‚Äì2020, underscoring that this market is measured in **single‚Äëdigit to tens of tonnes globally**‚Äînot in the hundreds. Your figures of **\~600‚Äì700 t/y** (U.S.) and **100‚Äì150 t/y allied Lu by 2030** are **orders of magnitude too high**. [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lutetium?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Lenntech](https://www.lenntech.com/periodic/elements/lu.htm?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Procurement Resource](https://www.procurementresource.com/reports/lutetium-oxide-manufacturing-plant-project-report?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[scrreen.eu](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf)

* **Medical Lu‚Äë177 demand ‚â† tonnage‚Äëscale Lu feedstock.** Radiopharmaceutical demand is growing quickly, but it is measured in **activity (GBq/Ci) and grams‚Äìkilograms per year**, not tens or hundreds of tonnes of lutetium. Your inference that a multi‚Äëbillion‚Äëdollar Lu‚Äë177 market implies ‚Äútens of tonnes‚Äù of Lu is **not supported**. Technical reviews discuss supply risk and rising capacity, but not tonnage‚Äëscale mass needs. [PMC](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC8241800/)[itm-radiopharma.com](https://www.itm-radiopharma.com/news/press-releases/press-releases-detail/itm-opens-worlds-largest-lutetium-177-production-facility-for-targeted-radionuclide-therapies-against-cancer-644/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Technopolis-group](https://www.technopolis-group.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/technopolis_group_2021_-_study_on_sustainable_and_resilient_supply_of_medical_radioisotopes_in_the_eu_-_therapeutic_radionuclides_final_report.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Largely sound (with nuance):**

* **Midstream bottleneck**: You‚Äôre right that **separation/refining capacity** (especially outside China for HREEs) is the chokepoint. Western projects are being built, but **HREE separation at meaningful scale is still limited**. [Argus Media](https://www.argusmedia.com/en/news-and-insights/latest-market-news/2643665-western-re-refining-projects-attempt-2025-push?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[CSIS](https://www.csis.org/analysis/consequences-chinas-new-rare-earths-export-restrictions?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia and EU projects**: Lynas (Mt Weld), Iluka (Eneabba HREE refinery, 2027), Solvay (France), REEtec (Norway) are real and relevant; timelines are 2025‚Äì2027+ and mostly focused on NdPr/Dy/Tb, with **Lu streams tiny** unless feed has meaningful xenotime. [MarketScreener](https://www.marketscreener.com/quote/stock/LYNAS-RARE-EARTHS-LIMITED-6492543/news/Lynas-Rare-Earths-Annual-Report-FY2024-48046884/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Iluka resources](https://iluka.com/operations-resource-development/resource-development/eneabba/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/companies-forging-rare-earths-industry-eu-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Corrected facts & numbers**

### **US & allied current production of lutetium (2024‚Äì2025)**

* **United States (Mountain Pass, CA)**

  * **Actual REO output**: USGS reports **\~45,000 t REO (mineral concentrates) in 2024**. However, Mountain Pass is a **bastn√§site LREE deposit** (Ce‚ÄìLa‚ÄìNd‚ÄìPr dominant). **HREE (including Lu) are present only in trace amounts** and are **not a meaningful product stream** today. Practical takeaway: **U.S. primary Lu production ‚âà zero**. [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)[USGS](https://www.usgs.gov/publications/complex-carbonate-ore-mineralogy-mountain-pass-carbonatite-rare-earth-element-deposit?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0169136824003871?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia (Lynas Mt Weld; Iluka stockpiles/refinery)**

  * Lynas FY2024 **total REO production was \~10,908 t**, heavily skewed to LREE; historic data show Mt Weld central ore is **LREE‚Äëenriched**, with Dy/Tb already **minor**‚Äîand Lu a **trace** fraction of HREE. Australia‚Äôs **current Lu output is likely at most kilograms to (low) hundreds of kilograms per year**, not 10‚Äì20 t/yr. [MarketScreener](https://www.marketscreener.com/quote/stock/LYNAS-RARE-EARTHS-LIMITED-6492543/news/Lynas-Rare-Earths-Annual-Report-FY2024-48046884/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MDPI](https://www.mdpi.com/2075-163X/13/5/656?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Canada / EU / Norway / Japan**

  * **No primary Lu mining**. The EU has some **separation capacity** (e.g., Solvay France; Neo/Estonia) for certain streams, but **no significant domestic Lu mine output** today. Norway‚Äôs Fen project is exploration‚Äëstage; REEtec targets NdPr first. Japan has **no Lu mining**; seabed trials (Minamitori) are **planned for 2026 pilot**, not production. [Reuters+2Reuters+2](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/companies-forging-rare-earths-industry-eu-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Bottom line:** **Allied primary production of Lu today is negligible**; Lu is recovered mainly as **tiny fractions** within broader RE processing streams, much of which are still processed in or via China.

---

### **US & allied demand by 2030 (order of magnitude)**

* **EU benchmark today:** The EU‚Äôs official CRM factsheet (SCRREEN/EUROSTAT) reports **EU Lu consumption \~5.61 t/yr (metal content)** for 2016‚Äì2020. This is a rare, quantitative anchor point. [scrreen.eu](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf)

* **Global production context:** Commonly cited figures put **global Lu‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ production ‚âà10 t/yr** (order of magnitude). That aligns with the EU figure above (EU \~5‚Äì6 t metal ‚âà \~6‚Äì7 t Lu‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ using \~88% Lu in Lu‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ) and suggests **global totals are single‚Äëdigit to low‚Äëtens of tonnes**‚Äî**not** hundreds. [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lutetium?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Lenntech](https://www.lenntech.com/periodic/elements/lu.htm?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Procurement Resource](https://www.procurementresource.com/reports/lutetium-oxide-manufacturing-plant-project-report?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Medical Lu‚Äë177 growth:** Demand is rising fast (PSMA and NET therapies), but **mass requirements remain grams‚Äìkilograms per year globally**, scaled by reactor capacity and specific activity‚Äînot by bulk lutetium tonnage. Expect **meaningful growth in value**, **modest growth in mass**. [PMC](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC8241800/)[itm-radiopharma.com](https://www.itm-radiopharma.com/news/press-releases/press-releases-detail/itm-opens-worlds-largest-lutetium-177-production-facility-for-targeted-radionuclide-therapies-against-cancer-644/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Corrected 2030 allied demand range:**

* Using the **EU baseline (\~5‚Äì6 t/yr metal content)** and assuming **U.S. \+ UK \+ Japan \+ others** are in the same order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude, a **reasonable allied total** for 2030 is **\~10‚Äì20 t/yr Lu (metal content)**, **not 60‚Äì100 t**. This is deliberately a range because Lu uses outside medicine (e.g., scintillators, optics) are niche and hard to quantify. The **value** of Lu‚Äë177 markets can grow several‚Äëfold without implying large increases in **mass**. [scrreen.eu](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf)

### **US & allied supply by 2030 (order of magnitude)**

* **Mines:** Expect **continued LREE‚Äëheavy output** from Mountain Pass and Mt Weld; neither is a material Lu source absent xenotime‚Äërich feed. New Western projects (e.g., Fen, Norra K√§rr) are **unlikely to contribute Lu at scale by 2030** (per public timelines). [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[leadingedgematerials.com](https://leadingedgematerials.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/NorraKarr_PEA_43-101.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **Iluka Eneabba (WA)**: a **HREE‚Äëcapable refinery** targeting Dy/Tb (and ‚Äúmore‚Äù) from 2027‚Äî**potentially** able to produce small Lu streams **if** feed contains Lu (e.g., xenotime). However, expected Lu volumes remain **very small**. [Iluka resources](https://iluka.com/operations-resource-development/resource-development/eneabba/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **Europe**: **Solvay (France)** to produce NdPr from 2025; **REEtec (Norway)** aims for NdPr first; heavy separation volumes will be limited early on. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/companies-forging-rare-earths-industry-eu-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Argus Media](https://www.argusmedia.com/en/news-and-insights/latest-market-news/2643665-western-re-refining-projects-attempt-2025-push?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **Recycling:** Helps NdPr/Dy/Tb far more than Lu; **Lu recycling by 2030 remains minor**. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/companies-forging-rare-earths-industry-eu-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Corrected 2030 allied Lu supply view:**

* **Primary (mined) Lu in allies:** **‚âà zero to low‚Äëhundreds of kilograms per year** (heavily contingent on xenotime‚Äërich feeds and actual heavy‚Äëseparation operations), not multi‚Äëtonne.

* **Separated Lu from allied refineries (processing imported concentrates)**: possibly **\~1‚Äì5 t/yr** if multiple plants run HREE circuits and can secure xenotime‚Äëbearing feedstock‚Äîstill **uncertain** and **feed‚Äëlimited**.

* **Total allied supply (primary \+ processing of non‚ÄëChinese feed \+ minor recycling):** **low single‚Äëdigit to mid‚Äësingle‚Äëdigit tonnes per year** is a defensible working range for 2030‚Äînot 100‚Äì150 t/yr. (This range is consistent with global totals being in the single‚Äëdigit/low‚Äëtens of tonnes.) [Iluka resources](https://iluka.com/operations-resource-development/resource-development/eneabba/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Argus Media](https://www.argusmedia.com/en/news-and-insights/latest-market-news/2643665-western-re-refining-projects-attempt-2025-push?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **Technology sections (accuracy check)**

* **Exploration (radiometrics, mapping, geochem, hyperspectral)** ‚Äî **Accurate in principle** for REEs. Add the nuance that **Lu** rides with **xenotime (YPO‚ÇÑ)** and other HREE‚Äërich minerals; **radiometrics flag U/Th‚Äëbearing monazite**, whereas **xenotime** may be less radiogenic. Sources on REE exploration and deposit types support your general points. [U.S. Geological Survey Publications](https://pubs.usgs.gov/pp/1802/o/pp1802o.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Processing & separation (flotation; acid/alkali cracking; SX cascades; ion exchange)** ‚Äî **Directionally correct**; SX with **D2EHPA/HEHEHP/Cyanex** variants remains the workhorse to stepwise split REEs; **HREE separations** (down to Ho‚ÄìLu) require many stages and very small product streams. * **Metal production (metallothermic reduction of Lu‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ)** ‚Äî **Plausible** and analogous to other lanthanides, but **commercial Lu metal volumes are extremely small**. I‚Äôd avoid naming specific companies unless you have direct citations. (Keep the mechanism at a high level.)

## **Bottleneck (your conclusion, tightened)**

* Correct: the **chokepoint is midstream**‚Äî**HREE separation and finishing capacity** outside China. Even as Western RE projects ramp, **Lu output will remain constrained by (a) feed mineralogy (xenotime scarcity), and (b) limited heavy‚Äëend separation circuits**. China has historically controlled **\~99% of HREE processing**; Western projects slated for 2025‚Äì2027 (Solvay/REEtec/Iluka) focus first on NdPr/Dy/Tb. **Lu remains a trace product.** [CSIS](https://www.csis.org/analysis/consequences-chinas-new-rare-earths-export-restrictions?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/companies-forging-rare-earths-industry-eu-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Iluka resources](https://iluka.com/operations-resource-development/resource-development/eneabba/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* Treat **Lu** as a **trace, specialty HREE** whose **mass market is tiny** (single‚Äëdigit to tens of tonnes per year globally).

* **U.S. primary Lu ‚âà 0**; **Australia‚Äôs Lu \= trace**; **EU/Norway have separation projects** but **Lu volumes will remain very small** by 2030\.

# Terbium

## **US and Allies Domestic Current Production (tons)**

**United States**

* **‚ö†Ô∏è Output level:** MP Materials‚Äô Mountain Pass is indeed the *only* operating U.S. rare‚Äëearth mine. But your throughput figure is too low. MP reported **41,557 t REO in concentrate in 2023** and **45,455 t in 2024**, not \~13‚Äì14 kt/y. (Your 10,766 t was Q3‚Äëonly.) [MP Materials](https://investors.mpmaterials.com/investor-news/news-details/2024/MP-Materials-Reports-Fourth-Quarter-and-Full-Year-2023-Results/default.aspx?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MP Materials](https://mpmaterials.com/news//mp-materials-reports-fourth-quarter-2023-results/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **‚ùå Tb tonnage:** It‚Äôs not accurate to infer ‚Äúa few hundred tonnes of Tb annually.‚Äù Mountain Pass is a **bastn√§site‚Äëhosted, light‚ÄëREE‚Äërich** deposit with *very low* heavy‚ÄëREE (Dy/Tb) content; DOE notes U.S. ores are **not rich in Dy (and by extension Tb)** and that **heavy REE separation capacity is \~100% in China**, underscoring minimal domestic Tb output. In short, **U.S. mined Tb today is near zero** (trace in the ore and not separated at scale). [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **‚úÖ ‚Äú\<1%‚Äù point:** DoD communications emphasize Tb is **\<1% of rare earth content in most deposits**, consistent with the above. [U.S. Department of Defense](https://www.defense.gov/News/News-Stories/Article/Article/3700059/dod-looks-to-establish-mine-to-magnet-supply-chain-for-rare-earth-materials/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Australia**

* **‚úÖ Producers and scale:** Lynas is the main allied producer; Q1‚Äë2024 REO was **\~2,722 t**, consistent with \~10‚Äì11 kt/y recent run‚Äërates, and Mt Weld is largely LREE. Northern Minerals‚Äô **Browns Range** is a heavy‚ÄëREE (Dy/Tb) project targeting **first production in late 2027** (concentrate), pending FID‚Äîyour timing matches company guidance. [Minedocs](https://minedocs.com/28/Mountain-Pass-TR-10012024.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Company Announcements](https://company-announcements.afr.com/asx/ntu/19cab788-adf2-11ef-9968-32bb3df8972d.pdf)

* **‚ö†Ô∏è Tb share:** Stating Tb as ‚Äú\<1% of REO‚Äù as a generality is fine, but **do not scale Tb tonnage by applying 0.5‚Äì1% to total REO** for LREE‚Äëskewed deposits (Mt Weld, Mountain Pass). The **actual Tb produced today ex‚ÄëChina is very small** and usually **realized only after heavy‚Äëoxide separation**, which outside China remains limited. [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Canada**

* **‚ö†Ô∏è Midstream, not mine:** Canada currently has **no Tb mine production**. Saskatchewan Research Council‚Äôs facility is **a processing/separation & metallization hub**; it has announced capability to produce **\~10 t/month NdPr metal initially, scaling toward \~400 t/y**, but **not Tb** unless heavy‚ÄëREE feed is available. Good to keep this as processing capacity, not mine output. [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/saskatchewan-processing-facility-first-to-produce-rare-earth-metals-in-north-america/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[src.sk.ca](https://www.src.sk.ca/news/src-rare-earth-processing-facility-first-produce-rare-earth-metals-north-america?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Europe (EU/UK/Norway)**

* **‚úÖ Mining:** No current Tb mine output.

* **‚ö†Ô∏è Processing build‚Äëout:** Europe is adding separation (e.g., **Solvay La Rochelle NdPr from 2025**; **REEtec** in Norway 2025), but **heavy‚ÄëREE (Dy/Tb) separation capacity remains small** compared to China. [Argus Media](https://www.argusmedia.com/en/news-and-insights/latest-market-news/2643665-western-re-refining-projects-attempt-2025-push?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/companies-forging-rare-earths-industry-eu-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Iceland/Greenland**

* **‚ùå Status of Kvanefjeld:** The project was **not ‚Äúapproved then halted by referendum.‚Äù** Greenland **banned uranium mining in November 2021**, effectively **halting Kvanefjeld/Kuannersuit**; in 2023 the exploitation licence was **denied**. Current talk of a repeal is speculative; **no production**. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/world/americas/greenland-bans-uranium-mining-halting-rare-earths-project-2021-11-10/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Listcorp](https://www.listcorp.com/asx/etm/energy-transition-minerals-ltd/news/kvanefjeld-rare-earths-project-legal-update-3203653.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Japan**

* **‚úÖ** No primary Tb mining; relies on imported oxides and limited recycling.

**Bottom line on current allied Tb:**

* The U.S. and allies **mine a lot of LREE** (e.g., U.S. \~45 kt REO in 2024), **but virtually no Tb is produced domestically today**; heavy‚Äëoxide separation is the missing step. China still controls **\~100% of heavy‚ÄëREE separation** capacity. **Thus, allied mined Tb output today is best described as *negligible*** (\<\< 10 t/y), not ‚Äúhundreds of tons.‚Äù [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **US and Allies Domestic Demand 2030 (tons)**

* **‚ùå EV/wind Tb per unit:** The statement ‚Äúa 3 MW wind turbine ‚âà2 kg Tb‚Äù and ‚Äúa typical EV ‚âà0.5‚Äì1 kg Tb‚Äù is **orders of magnitude too high**. Modern NdFeB magnets have **sharply reduced heavy‚ÄëREE (Dy/Tb) content** via **grain‚Äëboundary diffusion and microstructure control**; many EV/wind designs now use **little or no Tb at all** (Dy is more commonly used when needed). DOE‚Äôs magnet supply‚Äëchain report documents this shift. [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **‚ö†Ô∏è Demand scale:** A solid, public datapoint: the **EU‚Äôs Tb consumption averaged \~1.6 t/yr (metal equivalent)** in recent years‚Äîthis anchors the order of magnitude. Projecting forward with EV/wind growth and continued thrifting, **allied Tb demand in 2030 is likely in the *tens of tonnes per year*, not ‚Äútens of thousands.‚Äù**

* **‚úÖ Sectors:** Key Tb uses (magnet coercivity at high T, select phosphors, niche ceramics) are right; **magnet demand dominates** among industrial uses.

**Corrected 2030 allied demand view:**

* **Order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude:** **\~10‚Äì40 t/y Tb (metal equivalent)** for the U.S.+EU+Japan combined looks plausible, depending on **magnet chemistry choices** and **continued HRE thrifting** (large uncertainty). The prior numeric example scaling EV units by ‚Äú0.5 kg Tb/EV‚Äù is **not supportable** against observed consumption levels and the EU baseline of \~1.6 t/y. [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **US and Allies Domestic Supply 2030 (tons)**

* **MP Materials (USA):**

  * **‚ö†Ô∏è Capacity framing:** ‚ÄúUpstream 60K‚Äù targets **\~60 kt/y REO** by around 2027‚Äì2029. However, **Mountain Pass ore is LREE‚Äërich and HREE‚Äëpoor**; **assuming 0.5% Tb** to infer **\~300 t/y Tb** is **incorrect**. Any Tb at Mountain Pass is **trace** and domestic **heavy‚Äëoxide separation** is not established at scale. [sec.gov](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1801368/000180136824000014/mp-20231231.htm?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Lynas (Australia/US):**

  * **‚úÖ Expansion:** Lynas is expanding cracking/leach (Kalgoorlie) and U.S. separation (Texas). Still, **Mt Weld is LREE‚Äëskewed**; incremental Tb will be **small** unless feed changes. [Minedocs](https://minedocs.com/28/Mountain-Pass-TR-10012024.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Northern Minerals ‚Äì Browns Range (Australia):**

  * **‚úÖ Timing & nature:** Heavy‚ÄëREE (Dy/Tb‚Äëenriched) concentrate planned; **first production targeted late‚Äë2027**, subject to FID and build. By 2030, **a few t/y of Tb** (oxide equivalent) is a reasonable *project‚Äëlevel* expectation if the flowsheet and offtake proceed. [Company Announcements](https://company-announcements.afr.com/asx/ntu/19cab788-adf2-11ef-9968-32bb3df8972d.pdf)

* **Iluka ‚Äì Eneabba Heavy‚ÄëREE Refinery (Australia):**

  * **‚úÖ Critical midstream:** Firmly funded with a government loan; **commissioning targeted for 2027**. Iluka discloses **\~5.5 kt/y NdPr capacity** and **\~0.75 kt/y Dy+Tb capacity** (combined), processing Iluka and third‚Äëparty concentrates. **This is the key allied heavy‚ÄëREE separation node likely to produce Tb oxide at scale by 2030**, contingent on suitable heavy‚ÄëREE feed (Browns Range and others). [Iluka resources](https://www.iluka.com/media/qx4hjxxd/6dec24-eneabba-rare-earths-positive-outcome-of-funding-discussions-and-updated-economics-presentation.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Iluka resources](https://iluka.com/operations-resource-development/resource-development/eneabba/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Canada (SRC):**

  * **‚ö†Ô∏è Role:** SRC‚Äôs **\~400 t/y NdPr metal** target (once fully operational) helps **LREE** independence but **doesn‚Äôt create Tb** without **HREE‚Äërich feed**; there is **no Canadian Tb mine** slated before 2030\. [src.sk.ca](https://www.src.sk.ca/news/src-rare-earth-processing-facility-first-produce-rare-earth-metals-north-america?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Corrected 2030 allied supply view:**

* **Mining:** U.S. and Australia will deliver **large LREE tonnages**, but **very little Tb** unless HREE‚Äërich deposits (e.g., Browns Range) come onstream.

* **Separation bottleneck:** **Iluka‚Äôs Eneabba** offers the **first meaningful ex‚ÄëChina pathway** to separated Dy/Tb oxides by 2027+, but **actual Tb output** will be **limited by feed availability**.

* **Scale:** A realistic **allied Tb oxide** supply by 2030 looks like **low tens of tonnes per year**, *not* hundreds, assuming successful ramp of **one or two** HREE‚Äërich suppliers into Eneabba (and/or other heavy‚ÄëREE lines). [Iluka resources](https://www.iluka.com/media/qx4hjxxd/6dec24-eneabba-rare-earths-positive-outcome-of-funding-discussions-and-updated-economics-presentation.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **Key Discovery Technologies**

Your list broadly matches industry practice. A few refinements:

* **‚úÖ Radiometrics, magnetics & gravity, hyperspectral, mapping/geochem, drilling/logging**‚Äîall correctly described and relevant for REE targeting (including HREE). [smedg.org.au](https://smedg.org.au/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Hellman%20and%20Duncan%20REE%20Paper_2017.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MDPI](https://www.mdpi.com/2075-163X/13/5/656?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **‚ö†Ô∏è Ion‚Äëadsorption clays:** Where Tb is found with Dy (Browns Range style is hard‚Äërock, but many HREE sources globally include clays), **IP/resistivity and soil/till geochem grids** are indeed useful; keep that nuance. (General practice references as above.)

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **‚úÖ Beneficiation by crushing/grinding \+ flotation** for bastn√§site/monazite; **HMS / magnetic / electrostatic** for mineral sands and xenotime‚Äîaccurate. [Aalborg Universitets forskningsportal](https://vbn.aau.dk/files/782047278/1-s2.0-S004896972501023X-main.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* \*\*‚úÖ ‚ÄúCracking‚Äù (acid roast/leach) and **alkaline** routes‚Äîaccurate for REE concentrates. Lynas‚Äô cracking/leach flow is correctly summarized. [Minedocs](https://minedocs.com/28/Mountain-Pass-TR-10012024.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **‚ö†Ô∏è HPAL/pressure options:** These exist for specific feeds (less common for Tb‚Äërich xenotime but under study). The general framing is fine.

---

## **Key Separation Technologies**

* **‚úÖ Solvent extraction (SX)** remains the **workhorse** for splitting REEs into groups and individuals, incl. Tb later in the train. **Ion exchange** is used for polishing/specialty purity. Good. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0892687513003452?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **‚ö†Ô∏è Novel membranes/ionic liquids:** promising at lab/pilot scale; **not commercial at Tb scale** yet. Your caveat is fine.

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **‚úÖ Oxalate/carbonate precipitation \+ calcination** to high‚Äëpurity oxides, then **metallothermic (Ca/Al) reduction** or **molten‚Äësalt routes** to metal‚Äîaccurate.

* **‚úÖ Zone refining / vacuum melting** for ultra‚Äëhigh purity‚Äîaccurate for niche Tb use.

(For recovery/precipitation from solutions/effluents, **sequential precipitation** and **oxalate routes** are documented; purity depends on feed and conditions‚Äîclaims like ‚Äú\>94% RE purity‚Äù are case‚Äëspecific but directionally reasonable as *process demonstrations*.) [onlinelibrary.wiley.com](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1002/wer.1178?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MDPI](https://www.mdpi.com/2075-163X/11/5/484?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies**

* **‚úÖ Neutralization/precipitation, wetlands/bioreactors, staged precipitation & recovery (e.g., oxalate), tailings stabilization, adsorption/IX, water recycling**‚Äîall standard and well‚Äëdocumented in REE contexts. [onlinelibrary.wiley.com](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1002/wer.1178?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MDPI](https://www.mdpi.com/2075-163X/11/5/484?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **Key Bottleneck technology for US and Allies Domestic Production**

* **‚úÖ Core point (processing):** The chief chokepoint is **midstream separation of heavy REEs (Dy/Tb)**. DOE‚Äôs supply‚Äëchain work shows **near‚Äëtotal reliance on China** for heavy‚Äëoxide separation; this is why even substantial allied mining today yields **almost no domestically separated Tb**. [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **‚úÖ 2030 outlook:** **Iluka‚Äôs Eneabba** (commissioning 2027\) is the **first credible ex‚ÄëChina heavy‚ÄëREE separation hub** likely to produce Tb oxide at useful scale‚Äî**if fed** with HREE‚Äërich concentrates (e.g., Browns Range). Until HREE feed \+ separation **both** exist, allied Tb remains constrained. [Iluka resources](https://www.iluka.com/media/qx4hjxxd/6dec24-eneabba-rare-earths-positive-outcome-of-funding-discussions-and-updated-economics-presentation.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Bottleneck summary (tightened):**  
 Allied Tb supply is limited far more by **heavy‚ÄëREE separation capacity** than by geology. U.S./Australian mines overwhelmingly produce **LREE‚Äërich** concentrates; **Tb is trace** and requires **long SX trains** to isolate. With **heavy separation \~100% in China**, allied Tb output will remain **small** until projects like **Iluka Eneabba** (2027+) and **HREE‚Äërich mines** (e.g., Browns Range) ramp and pair up. [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Iluka resources](https://www.iluka.com/media/qx4hjxxd/6dec24-eneabba-rare-earths-positive-outcome-of-funding-discussions-and-updated-economics-presentation.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

# Dysprosium

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Current Domestic Production (tons)**

**United States.**

* **Mining:** MP Materials‚Äô Mountain Pass (CA) is the only US rare‚Äëearth mine; it produced **\~45,000 t REO** in concentrates in 2024, but the resource and onsite separations are overwhelmingly **light** REE‚Äëskewed (Nd, Pr, La, Ce). Mountain Pass is **not** a material source of heavy REE like Dy today. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf)

* **Separation (pilot‚Äëscale HREE):** In 2025, Energy Fuels began **pilot‚Äëscale** production of **high‚Äëpurity dysprosium oxide** (99.9% Dy‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ) at its White Mesa Mill (UT), initially **\~2 kg/week** (i.e., kilogram‚Äëscale, not yet tons). The company states it could scale to commercial production as early as **Q4‚Äë2026** (subject to feed and a production decision), with **Donald (Australia)** xenotime/monazite concentrate as future feed by **late‚Äë2027**. At a **Phase‚Äë1** Donald concentrate rate of **\~7,100 t/year**, the contained Dy would be **\~92 t/year** (2.15% of TREO), but that is forward‚Äëlooking and contingent. [PR Newswire](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/energy-fuels-successfully-produces-first-kilogram-of-99-9-purity-dysprosium-oxide-at-its-white-mesa-mill-in-utah-on-track-to-commence-terbium-production-in-q4-2025--302535303.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Energy Fuels](https://investors.energyfuels.com/2025-07-17-Energy-Fuels-Now-Producing-Heavy-Rare-Earth-Element-Oxides)

**Australia.**

* Lynas Rare Earths (Mt Weld, WA) remains the largest allied producer of REO but is **light‚ÄëREE dominant**; Tb/Dy are trace fractions in current product mix. (Q1‚Äë2024 output ‚âà2,722 t REO; annualized \~10 kt). Iluka‚Äôs **Eneabba** heavy‚Äërare‚Äëearth **refinery (WA)** under construction is designed for **HREE separation** and shows a **nameplate capacity of \~0.75 kt per year of combined Dy+Tb oxides**‚Äîa critical enabler but still dependent on suitable heavy feedstocks. Northern Minerals‚Äô **Browns Range** (xenotime; Dy/Tb‚Äërich) targets first commercial output in **late‚Äë2027** pending FID. Present Australian **Dy oxide** production remains **immaterial**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Iluka resources](https://www.iluka.com/media/d5gjznmn/iluka-resources-macquarie-australia-conference-may-2025.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Nasdaq](https://www.nasdaq.com/articles/rare-earths-stocks-5-biggest-asx-companies-2025?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Canada, EU/UK/Norway, Japan.**

* No commercial mining of heavy‚ÄëREE yielding **Dy** today. The EU has separation capacity (e.g., Solvay La Rochelle; Neo‚Äôs Silmet) but limited HREE focus; Europe still relies on imported feedstocks and expects to **fall short of 2030 mining/metal targets**. Japan has no primary RE mining. Current allied **Dy** production outside China/Myanmar is therefore **near‚Äëzero to at most single‚Äëdigit tons**, dominated by **pilot** output. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Context‚Äîglobal supply & risk.**  
 Most **Dy** reaching magnets comes from **ionic‚Äëadsorption clays** in **South China and Myanmar**. Conflict and crackdowns in Myanmar have recently **disrupted flows**, tightening HREE (Dy/Tb) supply and spiking prices. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/world/asia-pacific/myanmar-rebels-disrupt-china-rare-earth-trade-sparking-regional-scramble-2025-03-28/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Le Monde.fr](https://www.lemonde.fr/en/environment/article/2024/05/23/rare-earth-mining-in-myanmar-an-extreme-example-of-widespread-destruction_6672433_114.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Demand 2030 (tons)**

**Where Dy is used.** Dysprosium is a **coercivity improver** in Nd‚ÄëFe‚ÄëB magnets for **EV traction motors** and **direct‚Äëdrive wind‚Äëturbine generators** (high‚Äëtemperature stability), plus smaller volumes in electronics, defense and other high‚Äëtech uses. **Grain‚Äëboundary diffusion (GBD)** and hot‚Äëdeformation have **thrifted** Dy per magnet, but not eliminated it in high‚Äëtemp duty cycles. [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Innovate UK Business Connect](https://iuk-business-connect.org.uk/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/IUK-Climate-Magnet-Manufacturing-Report-TW-D4-compressed.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Ideal Magnet Solutions](https://idealmagnetsolutions.com/knowledge-base/grain-boundary-diffusion/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Anchors for a grounded range (not a single point forecast):**

* **EVs:** DOE estimates **\~1‚Äì2 kg of NdFeB magnet per EV**. If allied markets (US+EU+JP+others) sell e.g., **15‚Äì25 million EVs in 2030**, and if average **Dy content** in traction magnets after thrifting is **\~0.3‚Äì1.0 wt%** (range reflects growing adoption of Dy‚Äëlean/GBD designs), implied Dy intensity is **\~3‚Äì20 g/vehicle**, i.e., **45‚Äì500 t Dy/year** for 15‚Äì25M EVs. The wide range reflects real uncertainty about OEM design choices and thrifting. [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Wind:** NREL reports **\~17 kg Dy/MW** for **direct‚Äëdrive** PM generators (and \~**2 kg/MW** for geared DFIG). If allies install, say, **30‚Äì60 GW** of new wind in 2030 with a **25‚Äì50%** share of direct‚Äëdrive, Dy demand falls roughly in the **125‚Äì500 t** range for wind (illustrative; geared/drive mix matters a lot). [NREL Docs](https://docs.nrel.gov/docs/fy23osti/81483.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Other uses (electronics, defense, industrial):** low tens of tons combined. The EU‚Äôs measured **direct consumption** of Dy metal averaged **\~2.3 t/year** in 2016‚Äì2020‚Äîbut that excludes **Dy embedded in imported magnets**, which is substantial; it underscores why ‚Äúapparent consumption‚Äù undercounts end‚Äëuse. [Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf)

**Takeaway.** Depending on **EV/wind trajectories** and **thrifting success**, **allied Dy (oxide) demand in 2030 is plausibly on the order of a few‚Äëhundred tons to \~1,000 t**‚Äîdominated by magnets‚Äî*with a very wide uncertainty band*. Industry analyses consistently flag **Dy/Tb** as the **tightest** magnet REEs later this decade. [Adamas Intelligence](https://www.adamasintel.com/rare-earth-magnet-market-outlook-to-2040/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Green Car Congress](https://www.greencarcongress.com/2023/05/20230506-adamas.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Supply 2030 (tons)**

**What could be online by \~2030 (oxide basis):**

* **Australia (Iluka Eneabba refinery, WA):** **\~750 t/yr Dy+Tb oxide** nameplate separation capacity (mix depends on feed). Realized Dy output depends on Iluka feedstock blend (monazite/xenotime) and third‚Äëparty concentrates. **Key enabler** for non‚ÄëChinese HREE separation. [Iluka resources](https://www.iluka.com/media/d5gjznmn/iluka-resources-macquarie-australia-conference-may-2025.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia (Northern Minerals ‚Äì Browns Range):** Dy/Tb‚Äërich **xenotime** project targeting **first commercial production Q4‚Äë2027** (DFS/FID pending). Earlier pilot work indicated **significant Dy content**; full‚Äëscale output would likely be **tens of tons of Dy/year** if ramped and if separation capacity is available (e.g., Iluka). [Nasdaq](https://www.nasdaq.com/articles/rare-earths-stocks-5-biggest-asx-companies-2025?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Mining Technology](https://www.mining-technology.com/projects/browns-range-rare-earths-project/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **United States (Energy Fuels ‚Äì White Mesa \+ Donald feed):** At **7,100 t/y** Donald concentrate, contained Dy is **\~92 t/y**; Energy Fuels indicates **commercial HREE separation** could start as early as **Q4‚Äë2026‚Äì2027** from available feeds (subject to decisions). That figure is *contained* Dy in concentrate; **realized oxide** depends on recoveries and ramp. [Energy Fuels](https://investors.energyfuels.com/2025-07-17-Energy-Fuels-Now-Producing-Heavy-Rare-Earth-Element-Oxides)

* **United States (Round Top, TX):** USA Rare Earth reported **pilot** production of Dy‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ and plans an integrated mine‚Äëto‚Äëseparation chain, but the project remains **pre‚Äëproduction**; timing and volumes by 2030 are **uncertain**. [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/usa-rare-earth-produces-dysprosium-oxide-at-texas-round-top-mine/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[SEC Database](https://pdf.secdatabase.com/2421/0001213900-25-012473.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Europe (processing):** Solvay and Neo/Silmet are expanding separation/magnet capacity, but **HREE volumes** remain limited; the EU expects to **miss** many 2030 mining/metal targets, with heavier reliance on separation/recycling. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Other allied initiatives (US/Canada/EU recycling):** **HyProMag** (UK/DE) and others will add **secondary NdFeB** supply, recovering some **Dy/Tb** from scrap, but most programs are **early‚Äëstage** and tonnages by 2030 are **modest** relative to primary demand.

**Plausible 2030 allied Dy oxide outcome (order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude):**  
 If **Eneabba** runs near nameplate on Dy+Tb and **Browns Range \+ Donald** deliver significant HREE feed, **allied Dy oxide output** could reach **low‚Äëhundreds of tons per year** by 2030; a **sub‚Äë100 t** outcome is also plausible if projects slip, feed is constrained, or ramp‚Äëups stall. In all scenarios, Dy remains **supply‚Äëconstrained** relative to ambitious magnet targets, with **continuing import reliance**. [Iluka resources](https://www.iluka.com/media/d5gjznmn/iluka-resources-macquarie-australia-conference-may-2025.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Energy Fuels](https://investors.energyfuels.com/2025-07-17-Energy-Fuels-Now-Producing-Heavy-Rare-Earth-Element-Oxides)[Nasdaq](https://www.nasdaq.com/articles/rare-earths-stocks-5-biggest-asx-companies-2025?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Wind Dy intensity:** NREL *Materials Used in U.S. Wind Energy Technologies* ‚Äî **\~17 kg Dy/MW** for **direct‚Äëdrive** turbines (and \~2 kg/MW DFIG). [NREL Docs](https://docs.nrel.gov/docs/fy23osti/81483.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Market tightness:** Adamas Intelligence ‚Äî structural **Dy/Tb undersupply** building through 2030‚Äì2040. [Adamas Intelligence](https://www.adamasintel.com/rare-earth-magnet-market-outlook-to-2040/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Green Car Congress](https://www.greencarcongress.com/2023/05/20230506-adamas.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
