## **Key Discovery Technologies (Dy is typically in xenotime, monazite, or ionic clays)**

* **Radiometrics (airborne/ground Œ≥):** Th/U anomalies flag monazite/xenotime in carbonatites and heavy‚Äëmineral sands‚Äîuseful first‚Äëpass screening. (Well established in REE exploration.) [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Magnetics & Gravity:** Many alkaline complexes/carbonatites have strong density/magnetic contrasts that delineate intrusive bodies and fenite halos; valuable for **xenotime/monazite** targets. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Hyperspectral imaging:** VNIR‚ÄìSWIR mapping helps recognize **REE‚Äëindicator minerals** and alteration patterns; widely used to rank targets before drilling. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Geochemistry (soils/streams):** Pathfinder elements (Y, Th, Zr, Hf) and **Dy‚Äëbearing xenotime** signatures appear in fines; systematic grids vector to buried mineralization. [Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf)

---

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **Hard‚Äërock (xenotime/monazite):** Crush‚Äëgrind ‚ûú gravity/magnetics/electrostatics to concentrate heavy minerals, then **acid digestion** (H‚ÇÇSO‚ÇÑ or HCl) to get mixed REE solution; this is the pathway for projects like **Browns Range** (xenotime‚Äëdominant). [Mining Technology](https://www.mining-technology.com/projects/browns-range-rare-earths-project/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Ionic‚Äëadsorption clays (IAC):** **In‚Äësitu leaching** with **(NH‚ÇÑ)‚ÇÇSO‚ÇÑ** (or other salts) desorbs REE ions from clays, producing a leachate for downstream separation; the main source of **Dy/Tb** historically in South China and **Myanmar**. This method is **low‚Äëgrade but high‚Äëselectivity**‚Äîand highly **environmentally sensitive** when poorly managed. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S2238785422008602?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Wind Watch Docs](https://docs.wind-watch.org/yang2013.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Global Witness](https://www.globalwitness.org/en/campaigns/natural-resource-governance/fuelling-the-future-poisoning-the-present-myanmars-rare-earth-boom/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Separation Technologies**

* **Solvent extraction (SX) cascades:** Workhorse for splitting RE groups sequentially‚ÄîCe/La first, Nd/Pr next, then **middle/heavy REE** (Sm‚ÄìLu). **Hundreds of mixer‚Äësettler stages** and precise pH/redox control are typical to isolate **Dy‚Äëoxide** at \>99.5% purity. Outside China, **HREE SX capacity is scarce** but expanding (e.g., **Iluka Eneabba**). [Iluka resources](https://www.iluka.com/media/d5gjznmn/iluka-resources-macquarie-australia-conference-may-2025.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Ion exchange / chromatography:** Used for polishing or small‚Äëscale separations of heavy REE when ultrapure product is needed. [Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf)

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **Oxalate/carbonate precipitation ‚Üí calcination:** Standard route to **high‚Äëpurity Dy‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ** from purified solutions. [Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf)

* **Metallothermic reduction / molten‚Äësalt electrolysis:** Dy‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ ‚Üí Dy metal via **Ca/Al reduction** or chloride electrolysis; niche demand for metal (most Dy is used as oxide in magnet alloys), and **very few allied plants** are set up for Dy metal. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies (especially relevant to IAC mining)**

* **Neutralization & precipitation:** Treat acidic/ saline leachates by pH control, precipitating Fe/Al and co‚Äëprecipitating REE residuals; oxalate/carbonate steps can recover REE values from effluents. [crimsonpublishers](https://crimsonpublishers.com/amms/pdf/AMMS.000550.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Containment & water management:** Line/cover leach fields; capture and treat runoff; essential to mitigate the severe impacts documented at **Myanmar** operations. [Global Witness](https://www.globalwitness.org/en/campaigns/natural-resource-governance/fuelling-the-future-poisoning-the-present-myanmars-rare-earth-boom/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/world/asia-pacific/armed-group-says-it-takes-control-myanmar-rare-earth-mining-hub-2024-10-23/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Recycling magnets (secondary supply):** **HPMS/HyProMag**‚Äëtype flows recover NdFeB from scrap, allowing **Dy/Tb** recovery; scale remains limited by 2030\.

---

## **Key Bottleneck Technology for US & Allies**

**Mid‚Äëstream HREE separation capacity**‚Äîspecifically, **commercial‚Äëscale SX tailored to heavy REEs (Dy/Tb)**‚Äîis the chokepoint. The U.S. DOE notes **heavy‚ÄëREE separation is concentrated in China**; allied facilities are only now coming online (Iluka Eneabba; Energy Fuels‚Äô ramp; small EU capacity). Even when mines exist, **without HREE SX/refinery capacity** allied producers cannot deliver **battery‚Äëgrade Dy‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ** at scale. Supply risk is compounded by **Myanmar disruptions**. [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Iluka resources](https://www.iluka.com/media/d5gjznmn/iluka-resources-macquarie-australia-conference-may-2025.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/world/asia-pacific/myanmar-rebels-disrupt-china-rare-earth-trade-sparking-regional-scramble-2025-03-28/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

### **Bottleneck summary (2‚Äì4 sentences).**

Allied dysprosium supply is ultimately constrained by **separation** and **feedstock risk**. If Eneabba and White Mesa ramp as planned and Browns Range/Donald feed arrives, the allies can reach **low‚Äëhundreds of tons/year of Dy oxide** by \~2030‚Äîbut schedule, feed quality, and recoveries are genuine risks. Meanwhile, **EV/wind growth** can easily absorb that volume even under aggressive **Dy thrifting**. Absent faster build‚Äëout of **HREE SX capacity** (and robust recycling), allied markets will remain **import‚Äëdependent** for Dy through 2030\. [Iluka resources](https://www.iluka.com/media/d5gjznmn/iluka-resources-macquarie-australia-conference-may-2025.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Energy Fuels](https://investors.energyfuels.com/2025-07-17-Energy-Fuels-Now-Producing-Heavy-Rare-Earth-Element-Oxides)[The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

### **Notes on uncertainty and how to read the ranges**

* Reported **EU ‚Äúconsumption‚Äù** figures (e.g., Dy metal \~2.3 t/y) track **raw material** inflows, not **Dy embedded in imported magnets and devices**, so they **understate real end‚Äëuse**. [Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf)

* The **Energy Fuels Donald** figures are **forward‚Äëlooking** and contingent on investment and execution (the company discloses this clearly). Treat them as **capacity signals**, not guaranteed 2030 output. [Energy Fuels](https://investors.energyfuels.com/2025-07-17-Energy-Fuels-Now-Producing-Heavy-Rare-Earth-Element-Oxides)

* **Demand ranges** hinge on OEM magnet design and **GBD thrifting**; references agree that Dy/Tb remain **critical** for high‚Äëtemp magnets, even as average content per magnet declines. [Innovate UK Business Connect](https://iuk-business-connect.org.uk/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/IUK-Climate-Magnet-Manufacturing-Report-TW-D4-compressed.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

# Gallium

## **US and Allies Domestic Current Production (tons)**

**United States**

* **‚úÖ ‚ÄúNo active gallium mines / no primary production.‚Äù** The US has produced **no primary (low‚Äëpurity) gallium since 1987**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

* **‚ö†Ô∏è ‚ÄúNo commercial‚Äëscale U.S. production exists.‚Äù** Not quite. **One company in New York** *does* **recover and refine high‚Äëpurity gallium** from **imported** low‚Äëpurity gallium and **new scrap**. This is **refining**, not primary production, but it is commercial. US net import reliance remains **100%** for primary gallium. In **2024**, US **reported consumption ‚âà19 t**, with **imports of gallium metal ‚âà11 t** (plus large wafer imports). [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

**Canada**

* **‚úÖ ‚ÄúNo current production.‚Äù**

* **‚úÖ/‚ö†Ô∏è Near‚Äëterm project:** **Rio Tinto \+ Indium Corp** announced **first extraction** (R\&D) and plan **up to 40 t/yr** at Rio‚Äôs **Vaudreuil alumina refinery (Qu√©bec)** **if** the project advances through pilot and scale‚Äëup. Status today is **pre‚Äëcommercial**; target volume is **prospective**, not yet booked. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/rio-tinto-extracts-first-gallium-under-collaboration-with-indium-2025-05-07/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Rio Tinto](https://www.riotinto.com/en/news/releases/2025/rio-tinto-extracts-first-gallium-from-its-alumina-refining-process-with-partner-indium-corporation?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Investing.com](https://www.investing.com/news/stock-market-news/rio-tinto-extracts-first-gallium-under-collaboration-with-indium-4028742?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Australia**

* **‚úÖ ‚ÄúNo primary production.‚Äù** Australia refines alumina at scale (e.g., Worsley), but **does not currently recover gallium**. USGS lists principal *high‚Äëpurity refined* producers as **Canada, China, Japan, Slovakia, and the United States**‚Äînot Australia. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

**European Union (incl. UK/Norway/Iceland)**

* **‚ö†Ô∏è Primary vs refined:** It‚Äôs **correct** that **EU primary output ‚âà0**, but **EU does have high‚Äëpurity refined production** (notably **Slovakia**). The **UK ceased** high‚Äëpurity refined gallium in **2018**. So ‚ÄúEU currently 0 t/yr‚Äù is **too broad**‚Äî**0 for primary**, **non‚Äëzero for refined**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

* **‚úÖ Greece project:** **Metlen Energy & Metals (Agios Nikolaos)** plans **\~50 t/yr** gallium **from 2027‚Äì2028** ramp, integrated with bauxite/alumina operations. This is a leading EU primary project. [AP News+1](https://apnews.com/article/european-union-china-minerals-technology-c99de1a69863092fb40731a08f592e0d?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Mining Weekly](https://www.miningweekly.com/article/metlen-confirms-it-will-build-first-ever-industrial-gallium-plant-in-greece-2025-01-16?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Japan**

* **‚ùå ‚Äú0 t/yr primary output.‚Äù** USGS lists **Japan** among the **few countries still producing *primary* low‚Äëpurity gallium** (\~**3 t/yr** in 2023‚Äì2024, with **\~10 t/yr** primary capacity). Japan is also a **principal high‚Äëpurity refined producer**. Japanese imports of Chinese gallium did fall **\~85%** right after China‚Äôs 2023 controls. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)[Financial Times](https://www.ft.com/content/e679b887-00d8-4937-8a9d-1e2a8dd9c19a?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Allies total (today)**

* **‚ö†Ô∏è Framing:** For **primary** gallium, **China accounts for \~99%**; **Japan and Korea** contribute **small tonnages**; allied primary share is **\<1%**, not literally zero. For **high‚Äëpurity refined** gallium, **US, Canada, Slovakia, Japan** produce some material, but **feedstock** is largely **imported**. **World primary low‚Äëpurity production in 2024 ‚âà760 t**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

**Corrections to insert:** ‚ÄúChina accounted for **\~99%** of worldwide **primary** low‚Äëpurity gallium in 2024 (world total ‚âà**760 t**). Outside China, **small primary** output exists in **Japan (\~3 t)** and **Korea (\~3 t)**; refined production occurs in **US, Canada, Slovakia, Japan** from imported feed and new scrap.‚Äù [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

---

## **US and Allies Domestic Demand 2030 (tons)**

* **‚ö†Ô∏è Baseline today (measured figures):**

  * **United States:** **Reported consumption \~19 t (2024)**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

  * **European Union:** **Processing‚Äëstage consumption \~33 t/yr (2016‚Äì2020 average)**. [Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_GALLIIUM.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **Japan:** **Consumption \~160 t (2022)**‚Äîabout **21%** of world consumption then. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2022/myb1-2022-gallium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **‚úÖ Use pattern:** Electronics dominate use (GaAs/GaN ICs & optoelectronics). USGS shows **ICs \= 79%** of US consumption in 2024; **opto \= 20%**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

* **‚ö†Ô∏è Growth to 2030:** Your global ‚Äú**1,200‚Äì1,500 t/yr**‚Äù scenario assumes **mid‚Äësingle‚Äëdigit to low‚Äëdouble‚Äëdigit** growth. USGS shows **primary capacity \~1,100 t/yr** already (2024), and **refined high‚Äëpurity** output \~**320 t/yr** with **\~340 t/yr** capacity. Demand will depend on **GaN power (EV inverters, fast chargers), RF front‚Äëend (5G/6G), Satcom, radar**. Given today‚Äôs allied baseline (US \~19, EU \~33, JP \~160 t), an **allied 2030** demand **in the low‚Äëto‚Äëmid‚Äëhundreds of tonnes** (order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude **\~250‚Äì400 t**) is a defensible planning range (uncertainty: device mix, yields, scrap recovery). [USGS Publications Warehouse+1](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)[Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_GALLIIUM.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Context on disruption impact:** A **USGS** modeling study estimated a **$3.1B** US GDP hit from a **complete gallium export cutoff** by China, underlining significant **domestic dependence**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/publication/ofr20241057/full?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **US and Allies Domestic Supply 2030 (tons)**

* **Canada (Rio Tinto/Indium, Qu√©bec)** ‚Äî **up to 40 t/yr** if scaled to commercial; **R\&D/pilot now**, next steps to pilot‚Äëscale evaluation before a commercialization decision. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/rio-tinto-extracts-first-gallium-under-collaboration-with-indium-2025-05-07/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Rio Tinto](https://www.riotinto.com/en/news/releases/2025/rio-tinto-extracts-first-gallium-from-its-alumina-refining-process-with-partner-indium-corporation?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **EU ‚Äì Greece (Metlen, Agios Nikolaos)** ‚Äî **\~50 t/yr** targeted; **start 2027**, ramp toward **2028**. [Mining Weekly](https://www.miningweekly.com/article/metlen-confirms-it-will-build-first-ever-industrial-gallium-plant-in-greece-2025-01-16?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **United States** ‚Äî **No announced primary production**. The US **does** have **high‚Äëpurity refining** (one NY facility) using **imported gallium and new scrap**; volumes **not disclosed**, likely **small relative to imports**. A Tennessee zinc‚Äëresidue project has been discussed publicly, but status and tonnage are uncertain. **Summing realistic allied 2030 supply (order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude):**

* **Primary (new):** **Canada \~40 t \+ Greece \~50 t ‚âà 90 t/yr** if both projects commission and ramp.

* **Refined (existing allied facilities):** **small to low‚Äëtens of t/yr** combined (US, Canada, Slovakia, Japan), highly dependent on **imported feed**.

* **Total allied supply in 2030:** **\~90‚Äì120 t/yr** (plausible), still **below** likely allied demand (\~**250‚Äì400 t/yr**), implying **continued import reliance**‚Äî*unless* additional primary recovery lines (more alumina refineries) or major **recycling** capacity are added. ## **Key Discovery Technologies (accuracy check)**

* **‚úÖ Mapping/targeting bauxite & zinc systems** (Ga substitutes into **bauxite** minerals and **sphalerite**), **geochem** of **Bayer liquor/red mud** and **zinc residues**, and **data‚Äëmining of existing Al/Zn plants** are the practical ‚Äúdiscovery‚Äù routes‚Äîsince Ga is **a by‚Äëproduct**, not a primary ore. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

---

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **‚úÖ Bayer‚Äëliquor recovery:** Ga accumulates in **caustic Bayer liquor**; **ion‚Äëexchange** (strong‚Äëbase resins) and **solvent extraction** (e.g., **oxine / organophosphorus**) are standard industry approaches to capture and concentrate Ga from liquor before electro‚Äëwinning. (Chemistry consistent with USGS and literature.) [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

* **‚úÖ Residue leaching:** **Zinc smelter residues / coal ash** can be leached (acid) then treated by **IX/SX**; commercially minor vs. Bayer liquor but technically valid. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0301479724023600?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **‚úÖ Electrowinning to metal** from Ga‚Äërich chloride/sulfate eluates; product then goes to **high‚Äëpurity refining**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

---

## **Key Separation Technologies**

* **‚úÖ Solvent extraction (e.g., oxine / D2EHPA / Cyanex‚Äëtype) and ion‚Äëexchange** to split Ga from Al/Fe and other cations, followed by **precipitation** and **polishing**. This is standard in alumina refineries that install Ga circuits. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **‚úÖ Zone refining (to 6N‚Äì7N), vacuum distillation, re‚Äëelectrolysis**‚Äîestablished routes to high‚Äëpurity gallium metal and to feed GaAs/GaN epitaxy. **US, Canada, Japan, Slovakia** are listed by USGS as principal **high‚Äëpurity refined** producers (not primary). [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies**

* **‚úÖ Red‚Äëmud management (immobilization/beneficiation), waste neutralization, IX/adsorbent polishing of dilute streams, and e‚Äëwaste hydromet recovery** (GaAs/LED scrap) are all consistent with current practice and research trends. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0301479724023600?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Bottleneck technology for US and Allies Domestic Production**

* **‚úÖ Core point stands:** The bottleneck is **installation of gallium‚Äërecovery trains** at alumina (and some zinc) plants‚Äî**not** geology. USGS notes **gallium in bauxite averages \~50 ppm**, and **\<10%** is potentially recoverable with today‚Äôs tech/economics; **China provides \~99%** of primary output because **its plants run the circuits**. The US has **no primary** recovery active; EU will get its **first** at **Metlen**; Canada is **piloting** with Rio/Indium. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-gallium.pdf)

### **Bottleneck summary (tightened)**

Despite abundant gallium in bauxite and zinc streams, **very few allied refineries have Ga recovery lines**, so most Ga **is not captured**. The fix is **capex \+ process integration** (IX/SX \+ electrowinning \+ refining) at alumina plants. Even with **Canada (\~40 t/yr)** and **Greece (\~50 t/yr)** online by \~2027‚Äì2030, **allied supply** will likely trail **allied demand** by a wide margin, keeping **import reliance** high without broader roll‚Äëout. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/rio-tinto-extracts-first-gallium-under-collaboration-with-indium-2025-05-07/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Mining Weekly](https://www.miningweekly.com/article/metlen-confirms-it-will-build-first-ever-industrial-gallium-plant-in-greece-2025-01-16?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

# Germanium

## **US and Allies Domestic Current Production (tons)**

**United States**

* **Primary refinery production:** **None.** USGS lists U.S. primary refinery production as ‚Äú‚Äî‚Äù (zero) in 2020‚Äì2024. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

* **Upstream concentrates:** In **2024**, **zinc concentrates containing germanium** were produced at a mine in **Alaska**; some of this concentrate was exported to **Canada** for germanium recovery. A **Tennessee** zinc mine that previously produced Ge‚Äëbearing concentrates **remained suspended**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

* **Domestic midstream (from imported/recycled feed):** One U.S. company in **St. George, Utah** makes **germanium wafers** (mostly for space solar cells) and one in **Quapaw, Oklahoma** produces **GeCl‚ÇÑ** for fiber optics‚Äî**both from imported and recycled germanium**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

* **Trade baseline (2024):** **Imports ‚âà33 t Ge content** (metal \~20 t \+ dioxide \~13 t); **net import reliance \>50%** of consumption. In **Dec 2024, China banned all exports of germanium to the United States**, underscoring supply risk. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

**Canada**

* **Active producer/refiner:** **Teck Trail (BC)** is one of the world‚Äôs major integrated germanium producers, recovering **GeO‚ÇÇ** and **GeCl‚ÇÑ** from zinc smelting streams. Canada supplied **\~41% of U.S. GeO‚ÇÇ imports (2020‚Äì23)**, indicating significant capacity. [Teck Resources Limited](https://www.teck.com/products/other-metals/germanium?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

**European Union / UK / Norway / Iceland**

* **Belgium (Umicore):** Global leader in **Ge refining/recycling** (GeCl‚ÇÑ, GeO‚ÇÇ, metal) including **optical‚Äëfiber grade GeCl‚ÇÑ**; also expanding germanium feed via **recycling and tailings**. [eom.umicore.com+2eom.umicore.com+2](https://eom.umicore.com/en/germanium-solutions/markets/telecom-optical-fibre/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Germany:** Commercial production/refining is present (Langelsheim; facility operated historically as **PPM**, now **Vital Pure Metal Solutions**). USGS lists **Germany** among countries where Ge was **produced or recycled** in 2024\. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)[VPMS](https://www.vital-pms.de/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **New allied feed:** In **May 2024** Umicore signed a **long‚Äëterm agreement in DRC** (Lubumbashi tailings) to supply Ge concentrates to **Belgium**; test volumes started late 2024 with a ramp‚Äëup planned‚Äîan EU‚Äëaligned source of Ge feed. [umicore.de](https://www.umicore.de/en/media/press-releases/umicore-and-stl-sign-partnership-related-to-germanium-recycling-from-big-hills-mining-waste-materials-in-drc/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Japan**

* **Production:** Not identified by USGS among current producing countries; Japan remains a **major consumer/processor** relying on imports, with strong downstream applications (optics, electronics). [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

**Australia / Norway / Iceland**

* **Primary Ge production:** **None** reported. (Ge occurs as a by‚Äëproduct in certain zinc/alumina systems; no commercial Ge recovery lines are operating.) [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

**Summary (today):** Within the allies, **Canada, Belgium, and Germany** are the meaningful **producers/refiners** of germanium. The **U.S.** produces **Ge‚Äëbearing concentrates** and does **midstream processing from imported/recycled feed**, but **no primary refinery production**. **China remains the leading global producer and exporter**; export **licensing began Aug‚Äë2023** and **exports to the U.S. were banned Dec‚Äë2024**, materially tightening allied supply options. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

## **US and Allies Domestic Demand 2030 (tons)**

* **Measured baselines:**

  * **United States:** USGS continues to estimate **\~30 t/yr** U.S. consumption in recent years (metal \+ compound content). [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/publication/ofr20241057/full?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **EU & Japan:** Official consolidated tonnages are sparse, but both regions host sizable **fiber‚Äëoptic and IR‚Äëoptics** industries (key Ge uses). (EU now adding DRC tailings feed; Japan is a large downstream user.) [umicore.de](https://www.umicore.de/en/media/press-releases/umicore-and-stl-sign-partnership-related-to-germanium-recycling-from-big-hills-mining-waste-materials-in-drc/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Use pattern (global/U.S.):** **Fiber‚Äëoptic glass (GeCl‚ÇÑ/GeO‚ÇÇ)**, **IR optics (Ge lenses/windows)**, **electronics & solar (wafers/SiGe/III‚ÄëV substrates)**, and **PET polymerization catalysts** dominate demand. Independent analysis puts **fiber ‚âà26%**, **IR ‚âà22%**, **PET catalysts ‚âà20%**, **electronics ‚âà12%**, **solar ‚âà10%**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)[RFC Ambrian Limited](https://www.rfcambrian.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/04/rfc-ambrian-germanium-report-april-2025.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **2030 allied demand (planning range):** With continued **fiber‚Äënetwork expansion**, **defense/IR optics**, and **space/solar** demand, a prudent range for **allied** demand by **2030** is on the order of **\~80‚Äì140 t/yr (Ge content)**, anchored by U.S. ‚âà**30 t**, EU and Japan together ‚âà**50‚Äì100 t** (uncertainty depends on fiber build‚Äëout, PET catalyst penetration outside China, and recycling yields). Prices and China‚Äôs export policies will be the main swing factors. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/price-chinas-strategic-germanium-hits-record-high-possible-state-buying-2024-07-18/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **US and Allies Domestic Supply 2030 (tons)**

* **Canada (Teck Trail):** Expect **continued refined Ge output** (GeO‚ÇÇ/GeCl‚ÇÑ), potentially with incremental improvements tied to zinc throughput and process optimization. Canada has been a **top supplier** of GeO‚ÇÇ to the U.S. and will likely remain so through 2030\. [Teck Resources Limited](https://www.teck.com/products/other-metals/germanium?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

* **EU (Belgium \+ Germany):**

  * **Belgium (Umicore):** Ongoing **recycling** and **concentrate/tailings** processing (including **DRC tailings** ramping from late‚Äë2024) should **lift non‚ÄëChina allied supply** marginally by 2030\. [umicore.de](https://www.umicore.de/en/media/press-releases/umicore-and-stl-sign-partnership-related-to-germanium-recycling-from-big-hills-mining-waste-materials-in-drc/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **Germany:** Continued **refining/processing** capability (Vital PMS Langelsheim). [VPMS](https://www.vital-pms.de/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **United States:** **No announced primary refinery** projects. Expect **wafers (UT)** and **GeCl‚ÇÑ (OK)** to persist **from imported/recycled** feed; a 2024 **DPA grant (\~$14.4M)** is aimed at **wafer capacity**, not primary recovery. U.S. upstream **Ge‚Äëbearing zinc concentrates** likely continue (Alaska), but **refining is offshore**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

* **Recycling:** Globally, **\~30%** of germanium consumed has historically been met by **recycled material**; allied gains by 2030 are most likely from **expanded recycling of optics/fiber/wafer scrap** plus increased **closed‚Äëloop capture** at fiber plants. (Quantities vary with price and scrap availability.) [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2020/mcs2020-germanium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude outlook (2030):** Summing **Canada \+ EU** primary/recycled production available to allies, plus U.S. **secondary (recycling) and midstream**, suggests an allied supply envelope on the order of **\~60‚Äì100 t/yr** (Ge content) by 2030‚Äî**still below** the **\~80‚Äì140 t/yr** allied demand range, implying **continued reliance on imports** (non‚ÄëChina where feasible) or further recycling gains. (Global production statistics are opaque‚ÄîUSGS stresses limited verifiability.) [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

## **Key Discovery Technologies**

* **Geochemistry & Mineralogy of Zn deposits:** Germanium substitutes into **sphalerite** (ZnS) in **SEDEX/MVT/VMS** systems. **LA‚ÄëICP‚ÄëMS**, electron‚Äëmicroprobe mapping, and **bulk concentrate assays** identify Ge‚Äërich zones for **zinc mines** that could generate Ge‚Äëbearing concentrates. (USGS Yearbooks summarize the Zn/Ge association and recovery points.) [USGS Publications Warehouse+1](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-germanium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Coal/Lignite & Industrial Residues:** Screening **coal/fly ash** and **historic tailings** for Ge (ICP‚ÄëMS) can add unconventional feed. (USGS notes germanium resources in **lignite** and tailings.) [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

* **Process‚Äëstream analytics at smelters:** In smelting/roasting of Zn concentrates, Ge migrates to **flue dusts** and **leach liquors**; routine **online assay** (AAS/ICP‚ÄëOES) defines recovery potential. (Process flow summarized across USGS Yearbooks/Reviews.) [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-germanium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **Zinc‚Äësmelter route (dominant):** Roast **ZnS** ‚Üí Ge reports to **flue dust**/**acid leach** circuits ‚Üí **precipitation** (e.g., as **GeS‚ÇÇ** or hydroxide) ‚Üí **calcination** to **GeO‚ÇÇ**; part of the stream is chlorinated to **GeCl‚ÇÑ** (fiber‚Äëgrade), then hydrolyzed back to ultra‚Äëpure **GeO‚ÇÇ** where needed. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-germanium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Coal/fly‚Äëash route (minor):** **Acid leach \+ solvent extraction/ion‚Äëexchange** of ash concentrates to yield **GeO‚ÇÇ/GeCl‚ÇÑ** (commercially smaller vs. Zn‚Äëroute but technically proven). [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-germanium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Separation Technologies**

* **Solvent extraction (SX):** Organophosphorus/oxine systems selectively extract Ge(IV) from chloride/sulfate media; **strip** ‚Üí purified Ge solution (precursor to **GeO‚ÇÇ/GeCl‚ÇÑ**). [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-germanium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Ion exchange (IX):** Strong‚Äëbase resins (and specialty chelators) polish Ge from impurity‚Äëladen solutions after SX or precipitation. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-germanium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Chlorination & distillation:** Convert **GeO‚ÇÇ ‚Üí GeCl‚ÇÑ**; **fractional distillation** yields ultra‚Äëpure GeCl‚ÇÑ (fiber dopant), which can be hydrolyzed to very pure **GeO‚ÇÇ** again. [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germanium_tetrachloride?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **Hydrogen reduction & first bars:** **GeO‚ÇÇ \+ H‚ÇÇ ‚Üí Ge metal powder ‚Üí melt to first‚Äëreduction bars**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-germanium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Zone refining (6N‚Äì8N):** Directional solidification removes trace impurities for **detector‚Äëgrade** or **electronic‚Äëgrade** Ge. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-germanium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Crystal growth (CZ/VGF):** **Czochralski** or **vertical‚Äëgradient freeze** for **single‚Äëcrystal germanium** wafers (infrared optics, detectors; satellite solar cell substrates). (US facility in **Utah**; EU in **Belgium**). [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2020/myb1-2020-germanium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies**

* **Jarosite/Residue Management:** Neutralization and **stabilization** of **jarosite/iron residues** from Zn hydrometallurgy to immobilize co‚Äëprecipitated metals. (Generalized from zinc‚Äësmelter environmental practice.) [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-germanium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Effluent treatment & metal capture:** pH adjustment \+ **IX/adsorbents** to capture trace Ge and heavy metals from process waters; return captured Ge streams to recycle loops (common at refineries like Umicore/Teck). [eom.umicore.com](https://eom.umicore.com/en/germanium-solutions/services/recycling-services/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Tailings re‚Äëprocessing:** Leveraging **legacy tailings** (e.g., DRC Big Hill) both **remediates** and **supplies** Ge by extracting residual values with hydromet \+ SX/IX. [umicore.de](https://www.umicore.de/en/media/press-releases/umicore-and-stl-sign-partnership-related-to-germanium-recycling-from-big-hills-mining-waste-materials-in-drc/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Bottleneck Technology for US and Allies Domestic Production**

* **By‚Äëproduct dependency & smelter integration:** Germanium is **not mined as a primary ore**; recovery depends on **zinc smelter** flowsheets (and, to a lesser extent, coal ash). Many allied smelters **do not operate Ge circuits** at scale, so potential Ge in concentrates and residues **is not captured**. [SFA (Oxford)](https://www.sfa-oxford.com/rare-earths-and-minor-metals/minor-metals-and-minerals/germanium-market-and-germanium-price-drivers/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Policy risk from China:** **Export licensing (Aug‚Äë2023)** and **U.S.‚Äëspecific export ban (Dec‚Äë2024)** created acute supply risk and **price spikes**, highlighting the lack of **redundant allied capacity**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/price-chinas-strategic-germanium-hits-record-high-possible-state-buying-2024-07-18/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Data opacity & scale:** USGS notes **limited, non‚Äëtransparent global production data**; capital‚Äëintensive SX/IX and chlorination/distillation circuits have been concentrated in **China** and a few allied facilities (**Belgium, Canada**). Building new allied circuits requires **long‚Äëlead capex, feedstock security,** and **environmental permitting**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

### **Bottleneck summary (2‚Äì4 sentences)**

Germanium supply for allies is constrained less by geology than by **installed recovery capacity at zinc/coal processing hubs**. Because Ge is a **by‚Äëproduct**, allied output cannot quickly scale without **retrofitting smelters** (SX/IX and GeCl‚ÇÑ/GeO‚ÇÇ lines) or expanding **recycling**. China‚Äôs 2023‚Äì2024 controls (including a **Dec‚Äë2024 U.S. ban**) magnified the risk. Near‚Äëterm mitigation lies in **Canada/EU capacity**, **tailings projects (e.g., DRC‚ÜíBelgium)**, and **closed‚Äëloop recycling**, but a structural fix requires **new allied Ge circuits**. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)[umicore.de](https://www.umicore.de/en/media/press-releases/umicore-and-stl-sign-partnership-related-to-germanium-recycling-from-big-hills-mining-waste-materials-in-drc/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

### **Quick edits you can drop into a narrative draft**

* **U.S. current status:** ‚ÄúNo primary refinery production; Alaskan Zn concentrates contain Ge; U.S. imports ‚âà33 t (2024) of Ge metal+dioxide; China **banned** Ge exports to the U.S. in Dec‚Äë2024.‚Äù [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

* **Allied producers today:** ‚Äú**Canada (Teck Trail)**, **Belgium (Umicore)**, and **Germany (Vital PMS)** are the principal allied producers/refiners; **U.S.** handles wafers and GeCl‚ÇÑ from imported/recycled feed.‚Äù [Teck Resources Limited](https://www.teck.com/products/other-metals/germanium?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[eom.umicore.com](https://eom.umicore.com/en/germanium-solutions/markets/telecom-optical-fibre/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[VPMS](https://www.vital-pms.de/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **2030 demand & supply (allies):** ‚ÄúDemand **\~80‚Äì140 t/yr**; plausible allied supply **\~60‚Äì100 t/yr**, assuming Canada/EU maintain or modestly expand and recycling improves; continued **import reliance** likely.‚Äù [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-germanium.pdf)

# Gadolinium

## **US and Allies Domestic Current Production (tons)**

**United States**

* ‚ùå *‚ÄúEssentially all domestic Gd comes from Mountain Pass.‚Äù* Mountain Pass (bastn√§site) produced \~**45,000 t REO (concentrate) in 2024**, but it is **LREE‚Äëdominated (Ce‚ÄìLa‚ÄìNd‚ÄìPr)**; **Gd is a middle/heavy REE and occurs only in trace amounts in this ore**. The U.S. does **not** report production of **separated gadolinium oxide or metal**; any Gd in U.S. use is imported or separated abroad. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* ‚úÖ It is correct that **MP Materials is the only U.S. REE mine**, but using its **total REO tonnage as ‚ÄúGd output‚Äù is inaccurate**‚Äîit says nothing about Gd tonnage. [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Australia**

* ‚ö†Ô∏è *‚ÄúLynas \~3,212 t in Q4 2024 ‚áí \~10‚Äì12 kt/y.‚Äù* That quarterly figure is **REO (all rare earths)**, mostly **LREE**; it **cannot** be read as Gd output. Lynas‚Äô ore and product mix are NdPr/La/Ce‚Äëheavy; **separated Gd from allied producers is very limited and not reported at multi‚Äëhundred‚Äëton scale.** [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/australias-lynas-rare-earths-fourth-quarter-revenue-falls-133-2024-07-22/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Canada**

* ‚ö†Ô∏è Correct that **no primary ‚ÄúGd mine‚Äù** exists. Also correct that **SRC‚Äôs rare‚Äëearth program is a processing/separation initiative** (initial focus NdPr), not a domestic mining source for Gd; **no public data show commercial Gd separation there today.** [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**EU/UK/Norway/Iceland**

* ‚ö†Ô∏è *‚ÄúNorra K√§rr \~5,340 t REO/yr nearing production.‚Äù* Norra K√§rr is **not online** and remains delayed/disputed; it cannot be counted toward current Gd supply. The EU does, however, have **some non‚ÄëChinese separation capacity** (e.g., **Solvay, La Rochelle**) now expanding; public communications emphasize **NdPr for magnets**, but the facility is **capable of processing both light and heavy REEs**‚Äîpotentially including Gd‚Äî**without disclosing per‚Äëelement tonnages.** [Reuters+1](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/solvay-aims-produce-30-eus-needs-critical-components-evs-wind-turbines-2024-07-31/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Japan**

* ‚úÖ No domestic REE mining; **entirely import‚Äëreliant** today. (Japan plans **deep‚Äësea REE mud test mining in 2026** near Minamitori; this is **R\&D/pilot**, not commercial supply yet.) [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/asia/japan-begin-test-mining-rare-earth-mud-seabed-early-2026-2025-07-04/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Bottom line (today):** **Allied ‚ÄúGd production‚Äù is not tens of kilotons**; that figure confuses **total REO** with **Gd**. **Separated gadolinium production within the allies is small and undisclosed**, with **most Gd supply still coming from China**, while **EU facilities (e.g., Solvay) and Australia‚Äôs Iluka refinery (from 2027\) expand non‚ÄëChinese separation routes.** [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/solvay-aims-produce-30-eus-needs-critical-components-evs-wind-turbines-2024-07-31/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Fluor](https://www.fluor.com/projects/iluka-rare-earths?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **US and Allies Domestic Demand 2030 (tons)**

* **Measured baselines:** The **EU consumed \~45 t/yr of gadolinium (metal‚Äëequivalent)** across magnets, lighting, metals and **MRI** on **2016‚Äì2020** averages. Separately, **MRI alone emits \~19 t Gd/yr in Europe and \~21 t/yr in the U.S.** into wastewater‚Äîconsistent with **tens of tonnes per region** already today. [Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[PMC](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC12081572/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **What this means:** A claim that allied demand will be **‚Äú2‚Äì5 kt/yr of Gd‚Äù by 2030** is **not supported** by current usage data. Gd is **not** a mainstream coercivity dopant for EV NdFeB magnets (that role is mainly **Dy/Tb**); Gd‚Äôs largest steady uses are **MRI contrast agents**, **IR/optical/electronics**, and **nuclear fuel/control (Gd‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ as burnable poison)**. [osti.gov](https://www.osti.gov/servlets/purl/1908247?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Planning range for 2030:** Reasonable allied demand is **on the order of \~100‚Äì200 t/yr (metal‚Äëequivalent)** by 2030, assuming **modest growth** in MRI scans, optics/electronics and some industrial uses, and allowing for possible substitution in medical imaging. That range **scales up** from today‚Äôs **EU \~45 t** plus **U.S. MRI \~21 t** (before non‚ÄëMRI uses), plus **Japan and other allies**. (Peer‚Äëreviewed estimates for MRI alone span **\~20‚Äì200 t/yr globally** over the past two decades, depending on year/assumptions.) [Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[PMC](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC11891575/)

---

## **US and Allies Domestic Supply 2030 (tons)**

* **Australia (Iluka Eneabba Refinery, 2027‚Äë):** Designed to **separate both light and heavy REEs**, creating a **non‚ÄëChinese route to separated mid/heavy elements** (Dy/Tb capacity disclosed; Gd not broken out). This plant **enables**‚Äîbut doesn‚Äôt guarantee‚Äî**allied Gd oxide output**, contingent on feed composition and customer pull. [Fluor](https://www.fluor.com/projects/iluka-rare-earths?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Iluka resources](https://www.iluka.com/media/jyzjypkg/erer-fid-presentation-final.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **EU (France):** **Solvay La Rochelle** restarted/expanded rare‚Äëearth separation and **aims to supply \~30% of Europe‚Äôs processed magnet REE demand by 2030**; the plant is **capable of processing heavy REE streams** as supply chains develop. Per‚Äëelement (Gd) tonnages are **not public**. [Reuters+1](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/solvay-launches-rare-earth-processing-expansion-amid-china-restrictions-2025-04-08/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Norway, Estonia, others:** Additional EU/EEA separation capacity (e.g., **REEtec** in Norway, **Neo‚Äôs Silmet** in Estonia) improves **non‚ÄëChina midstream** but is **largely focused on NdPr**; Gd flows depend on available feed. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/western-rare-earths-supply-chain-springs-into-gear-2024-06-17/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **United States/Canada:** No announced U.S. Gd separation line; **Canada‚Äôs** separations are emerging across the RE value chain but **no public Gd tonnage**. (Canadian SRC‚Äôs current milestones center on **NdPr**.) [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Japan:** **Deep‚Äësea mud test mining** begins 2026; **no commercial volumes assured by 2030**. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/asia/japan-begin-test-mining-rare-earth-mud-seabed-early-2026-2025-07-04/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude outlook (2030):** If **Iluka‚Äôs refinery** and **EU facilities** run as planned and feedstocks include Gd‚Äëbearing streams, allied **separated Gd** supply plausibly reaches the **low‚Äëto‚Äëmid‚Äëhundreds of tonnes only in an optimistic case**; a **prudent planning range** is **\~60‚Äì120 t/yr** available to allies by 2030\. This still **straddles or falls short** of the **\~100‚Äì200 t/yr** allied demand range, implying **continued import reliance and/or larger recycling** unless more heavy‚ÄëREE separation is built. (Per‚Äëelement disclosures are scarce; the range reflects facility capabilities, CRMA targets and today‚Äôs consumption anchors.) [Fluor](https://www.fluor.com/projects/iluka-rare-earths?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Reuters+1](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/solvay-aims-produce-30-eus-needs-critical-components-evs-wind-turbines-2024-07-31/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **Key Discovery Technologies (Gd applies as a mid/heavy REE)**

* **Radiometrics \+ Magnetics/Gravity for carbonatites/alkaline intrusions:** Standard REE targeting (U/Th‚Äëbearing monazite/xenotime) still underpins most new REE finds; these tools are **element‚Äëagnostic** (they find the host), but are critical to **any future allied Gd feed.** [USGS Publications Warehouse](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-rare-earths.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Surface geochemistry & pXRF/ICP‚ÄëMS:** Stream/soil surveys and pit mapping to vector in on **MREE/HREE‚Äëenriched zones** within carbonatites or ion‚Äëadsorption clays. [eurare.org](https://www.eurare.org/docs/T1.1.2_Report-final-280217.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Seabed resources (Japan):** **Deep‚Äësea REE‚Äërich mud** near **Minamitori** is confirmed rich in REY, including **Gd**, and entering pilot recovery. [Nature](https://www.nature.com/articles/s41598-018-23948-5?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/asia/japan-begin-test-mining-rare-earth-mud-seabed-early-2026-2025-07-04/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **Conventional mining \+ flotation/physical upgrades:** As at Mountain Pass/Mt Weld (for LREE), and **gravity \+ magnetic** for monazite/xenotime streams that could carry **Gd**. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/australias-lynas-rare-earths-fourth-quarter-revenue-falls-133-2024-07-22/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Acid/alkali digestion to mixed RE leach:** Sulfuric/HCl digestion (monazite/bastn√§site) or caustic cracking ‚Üí **mixed RE chloride/sulfate liquor**. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/australias-lynas-rare-earths-fourth-quarter-revenue-falls-133-2024-07-22/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **For seabed muds:** Pilot flowsheets envisage **slurry lifting \+ beneficiation** then **hydromet**; still at R\&D. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/asia/japan-begin-test-mining-rare-earth-mud-seabed-early-2026-2025-07-04/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Separation Technologies**

* **Solvent extraction (SX) cascades:** Multi‚Äëhundred‚Äëstage **organophosphorus/HEHEHP/Cyanex** flowsheets to split groups, then isolate **Gd**; this is the **industry workhorse** and the **main capability gap** in allies. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Ion exchange (IX) / chromatography:** Smaller‚Äëscale polishing to **nuclear/medical‚Äëgrade Gd‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ/Gd salts**; slower and costlier but used for purity‚Äëcritical streams. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **Precipitation & calcination:** Oxalate/carbonate precipitation ‚Üí **Gd‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ** (battery/optic/medical grade). [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Metal production:** **Metallothermic reduction (e.g., Ca on GdCl‚ÇÉ/GdF‚ÇÉ)** or **molten‚Äësalt electrolysis**; then **vacuum melting/zone‚Äërefining** for high‚Äëpurity Gd metal or alloying feedstocks. (Same families of technologies now being scaled for NdPr at allied plants.) [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies**

* **Neutralization & precipitation of process effluents** (co‚Äëprecipitating REE hydroxides/oxalates; capture radiogenic Th/U where present). [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Closed‚Äëloop water & solvent recycling** in separation plants; end‚Äëof‚Äëlife **recycling of optics/electronics/MRI residues** to recover Gd and cut effluent loads. [Cyclic Materials](https://www.cyclicmaterials.earth/resources/solvay-and-cyclic-materials-sign-supply-agreement-for-recycled-mixed-rare-earth-oxide?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Bottleneck technology for US and Allies Domestic Production**

* **Midstream separation capacity (especially for mid/heavy REE like Gd) remains the chokepoint.** Even as allied mining expands, **few non‚ÄëChinese plants** can economically **split and purify Gd** at scale; this is precisely the **‚Äúmost challenging phase‚Äù** of the REE chain now being re‚Äëcreated in the EU and Australia. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/race-regain-rare-earth-glory-europe-falls-short-mineral-goals-2024-06-27/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Fluor](https://www.fluor.com/projects/iluka-rare-earths?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Policy context:** The **EU CRMA** target to **process 40%** of EU needs by **2030** helps, but allied per‚Äëelement tonnages (incl. Gd) are still **small and undisclosed**; reaching secure **Gd** supply requires **more SX/IX trains and qualified feedstocks**. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/sustainability/climate-energy/eu-picks-13-new-critical-material-projects-including-greenland-2025-06-04/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

### **Key Bottleneck summary (2‚Äì4 sentences)**

Allied **gadolinium** supply is limited by **separation/refining** capacity, not geology. Today‚Äôs non‚ÄëChinese plants are only just scaling, and **element‚Äëspecific (Gd) volumes are modest/undisclosed**. Even with Iluka and Solvay online, a prudent 2030 view is **\~60‚Äì120 t/yr allied Gd supply** versus **\~100‚Äì200 t/yr** demand‚Äî**imports and recycling remain necessary** unless more heavy‚ÄëREE separation comes onstream. [Fluor](https://www.fluor.com/projects/iluka-rare-earths?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/solvay-aims-produce-30-eus-needs-critical-components-evs-wind-turbines-2024-07-31/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_REE-EUROSTAT.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

# Tungsten

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Current Production (tons, tungsten content unless noted)**

**What holds up**

* **United States:** ‚Äú0 t‚Äù mine output is **correct**. The US ‚Äúhas not been mined commercially since 2015.‚Äù US supply is powders/carbides/chemicals produced from **imported concentrates/APT** and scrap by a handful of processors; 7 U.S. companies are capable of converting concentrates/APT/oxides/scrap to powder/carbide.

**Corrections / clarifications**

* **Canada:** ‚Äú0 t‚Äù mine production is correct (Cantung idled; Mactung pre‚Äëproduction). Also note the **updated Mactung resource** (not ‚Äú\~290 kt WO‚ÇÉ‚Äù): **41.5 Mt @ 0.73% WO‚ÇÉ indicated (‚âà303 kt WO‚ÇÉ)** and **12.2 Mt @ 0.59% WO‚ÇÉ inferred (‚âà72 kt WO‚ÇÉ)** (2023 NI 43‚Äë101). [Fireweed Metals+1](https://fireweedmetals.com/fireweed-metals-announces-mineral-resources-for-the-mactung-project-the-largest-high-grade-tungsten-deposit-in-the-world/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia:** Your ‚Äú\~1,000 t (2024)‚Äù is consistent with **USGS**: **1,000 t W** in 2024\. (Good to state explicitly that this is **tungsten content**.)

* **European Union (+UK):** Rather than Nasdaq estimates, use USGS 2024 mine output (tungsten content): **Austria 800 t**, **Spain 700 t**, **Portugal 500 t** (sum ‚âà **2,000 t**). UK Hemerdon **not producing in 2024**.

* **Japan, Norway, Iceland:** No mine production (0 t). Japan‚Äôs tungsten industry focuses on **processing/recycling**, not mining.

* **Omissions:** **Republic of Korea (South Korea)** belongs in ‚Äúallies.‚Äù Current mine output is **0 t** (2024), but the **Sangdong** restart (Almonty) is in construction with Phase‚Äë1 ore‚Äëthroughput \~640,000 t/y; first production targeted H2‚Äë2025 and ramp in 2026‚Äì27 (see ‚Äú2030 supply‚Äù). ## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Demand 2030 (tons, tungsten content)**

**Anchors (measured/structural)**

* **By end‚Äëuse region**, ITIA‚Äôs 2021 split of **final end‚Äëuse**: **China 36%**, **Europe 20%**, **Americas 17%**, **Japan 8%**, **Other Asia 8%**, **RoW 11%**. That puts ‚ÄúUS+EU+Japan+Other Asia allies‚Äù around **45‚Äì50%** of global end‚Äëuse, not ‚Äú\~20% after removing China 80%,‚Äù which mixed up **mine production** share with **consumption**. [ITIA](https://www.itia.info/applications-markets/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Global scale:** World mine production **81,000 t (2024)**. USGS notes non‚ÄëChinese mine share **\<20%**, scrap is significant. Consumption varies with industrial activity. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2024/mcs2024-tungsten.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Reasonable 2030 range (planning level)**  
 Assuming **low‚Äësingle‚Äëdigit growth** in tooling/specialty alloys and sustained defense demand, global consumption by 2030 plausibly sits in the **80‚Äì95 kt** band. Applying **\~45‚Äì50% allied end‚Äëuse share** implies **\~36‚Äì47 kt** tungsten content demanded across **US \+ Europe \+ Japan \+ other allies** by 2030\. This framing is better supported than a back‚Äëof‚Äëenvelope ‚Äúremove China 80% ‚áí \~14 kt‚Äù estimate. [ITIA](https://www.itia.info/applications-markets/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

*(Takeaway: allied demand is in the **tens of thousands of tonnes**, dominated by cemented carbides/hardmetals; defense is material but smaller.)*

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Supply 2030 (tons, tungsten content)**

**What‚Äôs solid today (2024 baseline outside China)**

* **EU (AT/ES/PT)** ‚âà **2,000 t W** combined. **Australia** ‚âà **1,000 t W**. **US/Canada/Japan** mine output: **0**.

**Additions likely by (or around) 2030**

* **South Korea ‚Äî Sangdong (Almonty):** Phase‚Äë1 throughput \~640 kt ore/y, with staged ramp from H2‚Äë2025. Public materials and independent commentary indicate **hundreds of thousands of MTU WO‚ÇÉ per year** at steady‚Äëstate (order **230,000‚Äì332,000 MTU WO‚ÇÉ/y** cited in recent updates), i.e., roughly **1.8‚Äì2.6 kt W/y** on a tungsten‚Äëcontent basis (WO‚ÇÉ√ó0.793). A further Phase‚Äë2 expansion is permitted (to \~1.2 Mt/y ore). Precise steady‚Äëstate tonnage will depend on grade/recovery; funding is advanced. [Discovery Alert](https://discoveryalert.com.au/news/tungsten-mining-strategic-importance-2025-almonty-leads/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Mining Weekly](https://www.miningweekly.com/article/tungsten-west-unveils-restart-plan-for-hemerdon-mine-2025-05-30?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Mining Data Online](https://miningdataonline.com/property/3406/Sangdong-Project.aspx?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **UK ‚Äî Hemerdon (Tungsten West):** **Restart plan** published May 2025; financing pending. Expectation at full ramp: **\~3,320 t/y WO‚ÇÉ‚Äëin‚Äëconcentrate** (\~**2.6 kt W**). Earliest restart \~2026‚Äì27 **if** financing closes. Treat as **upside**, not base case. [Project Blue](https://projectblue.com/blue/news-analysis/1219/tungsten-west-reveals-requirements-for-hemerdon-restart-?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Mining Weekly](https://www.miningweekly.com/article/tungsten-west-unveils-restart-plan-for-hemerdon-mine-2025-05-30?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Canada ‚Äî Mactung (Fireweed):** World‚Äëclass resource (see above); still **pre‚Äëproduction**. Without a completed PFS/FS and build decision, it‚Äôs prudent to treat **material 2030 output as uncertain** (potential post‚Äë2030). [Fireweed Metals](https://fireweedmetals.com/fireweed-metals-announces-mineral-resources-for-the-mactung-project-the-largest-high-grade-tungsten-deposit-in-the-world/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Base‚Äë/Upside scenarios for allied mine supply in 2030 (t W):**

* **Base case (status quo EU+AU, Sangdong Phase‚Äë1):** \~**1,000 (AU) \+ 2,000 (EU) \+ 1,800‚Äì2,600 (ROK)** ‚âà **4.8‚Äì5.6 kt W**.

* **Upside (add Hemerdon restart \+ early Canadian start):** \+**\~2.6 kt W** (UK) **\+?** Canada (unknown) ‚áí **\~7‚Äì8+ kt W** potential by 2030\. [Discovery Alert](https://discoveryalert.com.au/news/tungsten-mining-strategic-importance-2025-almonty-leads/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Project Blue](https://projectblue.com/blue/news-analysis/1219/tungsten-west-reveals-requirements-for-hemerdon-restart-?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Recycling & midstream capacity (important nuance)**

* **Recycled tungsten** routinely supplies **\~30‚Äì35%** of global raw material for powders (ITIA 2021; USGS notes scrap is ‚Äúan important source‚Äù). Europe, Japan, and the US have established **powder/carbide plants** that rely on imported concentrates/APT and scrap. [ITIA](https://www.itia.info/supply-circularity/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-tungsten.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* Contrary to the draft‚Äôs bottleneck statement, there **is** notable Western **APT/powder** capacity: **Global Tungsten & Powders (US, part of Plansee)** processes **tungsten ores and scrap into APT and powders**; **Wolfram Bergbau und H√ºtten (Austria, Sandvik)** operates the Mittersill mine and **refining plant for tungsten carbide/powders**. The constraint is **feedstock access**, not zero capacity. [The Plansee Group](https://plansee-group.com/files/Living.Metals/Pla.LM.2024.25.V4.EN.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[GlobeNewswire](https://www.globenewswire.com/news-release/2009/02/17/15910/0/en/Sandvik-acquires-Austrian-tungsten-producer.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MINING REPORT](https://mining-report.de/english/blog/wolfram-invests-in-a-new-sandvik-processing-plant-in-mittersill/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **Key Bottleneck technology for US & Allies ‚Äî What to change**

**Draft claim (needs correction):**

‚ÄúThe critical bottleneck is downstream processing (APT/powders); virtually all high‚Äëpurity W production is abroad.‚Äù

**What the evidence supports instead:**

* The **primary chokepoints** for allies are (i) **access to non‚ÄëChinese concentrates/APT** (geopolitics: new **export controls on tungsten products**, China \>80% mine output), and (ii) **limited allied mine supply**. **Midstream capacity does exist** in the US/EU (e.g., **GTP (US)**, **Wolfram Austria**, **Kennametal EU/US**), but it is **heavily dependent on imported feed** and scrap. In short, **feedstock availability and policy risk** are the binding constraints; midstream is **not zero**, but needs **expansion** to de‚Äërisk. [Reuters+1](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/what-are-five-new-critical-metal-exports-restricted-by-china-2025-02-04/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[The Plansee Group](https://plansee-group.com/files/Living.Metals/Pla.LM.2024.25.V4.EN.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[GlobeNewswire](https://www.globenewswire.com/news-release/2009/02/17/15910/0/en/Sandvik-acquires-Austrian-tungsten-producer.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**2‚Äì4 sentence bottleneck summary (revised):**  
 China still accounts for **\>80%** of mine output and has imposed new **export controls** on multiple tungsten products, so the most acute allied bottleneck is **securing non‚ÄëChinese feedstock** (concentrates/APT) at scale. The US and EU do have **established powder/carbide plants**, but they depend on imported concentrates and scrap, meaning **feedstock, not basic processing know‚Äëhow, is the governor**. Near‚Äëterm mitigation is **new allied mines (Sangdong, possible Hemerdon) \+ recycling growth**, coupled with **incremental APT/powder debottlenecking**. Without those, allied mine‚Äëto‚Äëmetal volumes will remain well below allied demand by 2030\. [Reuters+1](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/what-are-five-new-critical-metal-exports-restricted-by-china-2025-02-04/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

# Niobium

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Current Production (tons Nb content)**

* **United States:** **0 t** mine production. The U.S. has no active niobium mines; U.S. net import reliance for niobium was **100%** in 2024\.

* **Canada:** **\~7,100 t Nb (2024)** from the **Niobec** underground mine (Qu√©bec) operated by Magris Performance Materials. Canada‚Äôs share was \~6‚Äì7% of world niobium mine output in 2024\.

* **Australia:** **No primary mine production.** Geoscience Australia states there are **no mines producing niobium as a primary product**; any by‚Äëproduct output at lithium/tantalum operations is unreported and small. [Geoscience Australia+1](https://www.ga.gov.au/aimr2024/australias-identified-mineral-resources?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **European Union/UK/Norway/Iceland/Japan:** **No mine production.** (Japan and the EU are major **consumers** and **importers**; Japan also has Nb metal/alloy manufacturing but no domestic ore.) Global mine production in 2024 was **\~110,000 t Nb**, almost **91%** from Brazil, \~6‚Äì7% from Canada; China‚Äôs mine output is minor compared with Brazil.

**Bottom line:** among the U.S. and close allies, **Canada (Niobec) is the only current primary producer** at \~7.1 kt Nb/year; the U.S., EU, Japan and Australia have **zero** primary niobium mine output today. [Geoscience Australia](https://www.ga.gov.au/aimr2024/australias-identified-mineral-resources?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Demand 2030 (tons Nb content)**

**Measured baselines (most recent hard numbers):**

* **United States:** U.S. apparent consumption **\~8,400 t** (2024). Imports for consumption were **\~8,900 t** (Nb content), with 100% net import reliance.

* **European Union:** **FeNb imports 22,064,800 kg (2022)**. At a typical FeNb grade \~65% Nb, that is **\~14,300 t Nb**.

* **Japan:** **FeNb imports 6,003,700 kg (2022)** ‚Üí **\~3,900 t Nb** (65% basis).

**Uses mix:** Niobium demand is dominated by **micro‚Äëalloyed steels** (HSLA) for automotive, pipelines and construction; smaller shares go to superalloys, superconductors (Nb‚ÄëTi/Nb3Sn) and chemical applications.

**Reasonable 2030 planning range:** If allied consumption grows modestly with steel output (‚âà2‚Äì4%/yr) and higher‚Äëvalue uses (e.g., aerospace, some battery/anode R\&D) add incremental pull, a **U.S.+EU+Japan** demand range of **\~30,000‚Äì40,000 t Nb/year by \~2030** is defensible (from a measured \~26‚Äì27 kt combined baseline today). This is a range, not a single point forecast, and hinges mainly on steel volumes (not EV magnets).

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Supply 2030 (tons Nb content)**

* **Canada (Niobec):** Expect **continuation near \~7,000 t Nb/yr** absent a published expansion decision. (USGS shows 6,700 t in 2023; 7,100 t in 2024.)

* **United States (Elk Creek, Nebraska):** **NioCorp**‚Äôs 2022 feasibility study targets **\~7,450 t/yr ferroniobium** (FeNb) once operating (‚âà**\~4,800 t/yr Nb** at 65% Nb). The project has permits and has secured offtakes for much of planned FeNb, but financing and build schedules remain the gating items; 2030 production is **possible but not assured**. [Minedocs](https://minedocs.com/22/Elk_Creek-FS-06282022.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia (ASM Dubbo):** Polymetallic REE‚ÄìZr‚ÄìHf‚ÄìNb project with approvals; company materials indicate potential **niobium oxide** among products, but the 2025 heap‚Äëleach scoping re‚Äëphases toward REE first. **Commercial Nb volumes and timing remain uncommitted**; pre‚Äë2030 output is uncertain. [Australian Strategic Materials Ltd (ASM)+1](https://asm-au.com/mines/the-dubbo-project/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Europe/Japan:** No primary Nb mines. Processing capacity exists to alloy/import FeNb, but **no mine‚Äëderived Nb**.

**Supply outlook (allies):** A **base case** of **\~7 kt (Canada only)**, and an **optimistic case** of **\~10‚Äì12 kt** if Elk Creek (U.S.) enters production before/around 2030 and early Nb from Dubbo materializes. Either way, allied mine‚Äëbased supply remains **well short** of allied demand (‚âà30‚Äì40 kt). Imports‚Äîprimarily **FeNb from Brazil**‚Äîremain indispensable.

## **Key Discovery Technologies (for Nb in carbonatites/alkaline complexes)**

* **Remote sensing & hyperspectral:** Carbonatites and fenites can be mapped using VNIR‚ÄìSWIR hyperspectral; indices for carbonate (‚àº2.30‚Äì2.35‚ÄØ¬µm) and even direct REE absorptions aid target definition (e.g., Epembe, Namibia; Sarfartoq, Greenland). [MDPI+1](https://www.mdpi.com/2072-4292/8/8/620?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[SpringerLink](https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s12303-017-0078-5?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Airborne radiometric \+ gamma‚Äëray \+ ML:** Integrating airborne gamma (Th/U anomalies), hyperspectral and decision‚Äëtree/ML methods has successfully prioritized **Nb‚ÄìREE** targets (Sarfartoq case). [MDPI](https://www.mdpi.com/2813-446X/2/3/8?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Geophysics (magnetic/gravity):** Carbonatite‚Äìalkaline intrusions commonly show **mag/grav** contrasts; surveys map ring complexes, dykes and dense cores that may host pyrochlore. [MDPI](https://www.mdpi.com/2075-163X/10/11/965?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MSU Libraries](https://d.lib.msu.edu/etd/4153/OBJ/download?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Geochemistry & mapping:** Multi‚Äëelement soil/stream (Nb‚ÄëTa‚ÄëREE‚ÄëTh‚ÄëU) anomalies plus field mapping of carbonatite dykes/fenites remain staple targeting tools. [MDPI](https://www.mdpi.com/2075-163X/10/11/965?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Extraction Technologies (mine ‚Üí concentrate)**

* **Mining:** Open‚Äëpit for many carbonatites (e.g., Arax√°/Catal√£o in Brazil) and **underground** at Niobec (Qu√©bec). [Niobium Technology](https://niobium.tech/-/media/niobiumtech/attachments-biblioteca-tecnica/nt_mining-ore-preparation-and-ferroniobium-production-at-cbmm.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Comminution & beneficiation:** Crushing/grinding followed by **gravity/dense‚Äëmedia**, **magnetic separation**, and **flotation** to produce a **pyrochlore** concentrate (typ. 5‚Äì15% Nb‚ÇÇO‚ÇÖ). [ResearchGate](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/272424460_Niobium_oxide_mineral_flotation_A_review_of_relevant_literature_and_the_current_state_of_industrial_operations?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Separation Technologies (concentrate ‚Üí Nb/Ta separation)**

* **Alkaline decomposition:** **NaOH/Na‚ÇÇCO‚ÇÉ roast or fusion** converts Nb minerals to soluble **sodium niobate**, rejecting silicates/Fe; then leach. [Murdoch Research Portal](https://researchportal.murdoch.edu.au/view/pdfCoverPage?download=true&filePid=13136891940007891&instCode=61MUN_INST&utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Acid digestion \+ SX:** Fluoride‚Äëbearing acid media (HF/H‚ÇÇSO‚ÇÑ) followed by **solvent extraction** (e.g., MIBK, TBP, amines) to separate **Nb from Ta** and impurities; counter‚Äëcurrent SX is industry standard. [ORBi](https://orbi.uliege.be/bitstream/2268/251796/1/1-s2.0-S0304386X20308689-main.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Prometia](https://prometia.eu/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/MSP-REFRAM-D2.3-Innovation-potential-recovery-refractory-metals-primary-sources.pdf)

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies (Nb chemicals ‚Üí products)**

* **Niobium pentoxide (Nb‚ÇÇO‚ÇÖ):** Precipitation from purified solution (niobic acid) and calcination to high‚Äëpurity oxide. [ORBi](https://orbi.uliege.be/bitstream/2268/251796/1/1-s2.0-S0304386X20308689-main.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Ferroniobium (FeNb):** **Aluminothermic/thermo‚Äëreduction in electric arc furnaces** is the dominant commercial route (\~65% Nb alloy). Process details published by **CBMM** (Arax√°) and others. [Niobium Technology+1](https://niobium.tech/-/media/niobiumtech/attachments-biblioteca-tecnica/nt_mining-ore-preparation-and-ferroniobium-production-at-cbmm.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[CBMM](https://cbmm.com/assets/infographic/en/index.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **High‚Äëpurity Nb metal:** Electron‚Äëbeam or vacuum melting and specialty electrorefining for niche (superconductor/aerospace) grades. [Scindeks Clanci](https://scindeks-clanci.ceon.rs/data/pdf/1450-5959/2022/1450-59592201001D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies**

* **Water treatment & reuse:** Case study‚Äî**Niobec** uses high‚Äërate ballasted flocculation (Actiflo¬Æ) to meet effluent standards, with broad recycle of process water (illustrates modern tailings‚Äëwater management for Nb concentrators). [Prometia](https://prometia.eu/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/MSP-REFRAM-D2.3-Innovation-potential-recovery-refractory-metals-primary-sources.pdf)

* **HF‚Äëlight flowsheets (R\&D):** Ongoing EU work targets **reduced‚Äëfluoride** digestion/SX to lower hazards and waste‚Äîimportant for new Nb/Ta plants. [Prometia](https://prometia.eu/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/MSP-REFRAM-D2.3-Innovation-potential-recovery-refractory-metals-primary-sources.pdf)

* **Tailings reprocessing:** Secondary recovery (gravity/magnetic re‚Äëtreat) to capture residual pyrochlore while reducing long‚Äëterm liabilities is being studied alongside broader critical‚Äëmetal tailings valorization. [Prometia](https://prometia.eu/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/MSP-REFRAM-D2.3-Innovation-potential-recovery-refractory-metals-primary-sources.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Bottleneck Technology for US & Allies**

**Where the real constraint is:** **Upstream primary supply** within allied borders, not basic metallurgy. With **\~91% of world mine output in Brazil** and **\~6‚Äì7% in Canada**, the U.S., EU, Japan and Australia lack domestic ore. Building a mine+concentrator is the hurdle; ferroniobium smelting is mature and concentrated at a few large plants (e.g., CBMM). Even by 2030, unless **Elk Creek** and at least one other allied project commission, allied mine‚Äëbased supply will likely remain ‚â§**\~10‚Äì12 kt Nb/yr** vs demand of \~30‚Äì40 kt.

### **Bottleneck summary (2‚Äì4 sentences)**

Niobium‚Äôs choke point for the U.S. and close allies is **primary production**: there are **no** operating mines outside Canada within the bloc, and only one (Niobec) today. World supply is overwhelmingly concentrated in Brazil; Canada contributes a small single‚Äëdigit percent. Unless new allied mines (notably Elk Creek) finance and build by decade‚Äôs end, the **supply gap** persists and imports (mainly Brazilian FeNb) remain essential.

---

### **Quick corrections to your draft (for clarity)**

* Canada‚Äôs current production is **\~7.1 kt Nb (2024)** (not a generic 7‚Äì9 kt range without source); Canada is **\~6‚Äì7%** of world output, not 8‚Äì10% in the latest USGS data.

* Demand drivers are **HSLA steel first**; EVs matter indirectly via vehicle steel demand‚Äîniobium is not a mainstream EV battery cathode material today (small R\&D niches exist).

* FeNb import figures for EU/Japan are best anchored to **WITS**; I‚Äôve converted to Nb content at 65% to avoid over‚Äëcounting.

# Magnesium

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Current Production (tons)**

* **United States**

  * **Primary magnesium metal:** *no production in 2023‚Äì2024.* USGS reports the **only U.S. primary smelter (Utah)** halted production in 2022; **capacity (\~64‚ÄØkt/yr)** was **idle throughout 2024**. Reported *primary* production for 2023‚Äì2024 \= **0**. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

  * **Secondary (scrap) magnesium:** about **110‚ÄØkt** recovered in 2024 (86‚ÄØkt new scrap \+ 27‚ÄØkt old scrap). (This is recycled metal, not primary production.) [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

  * **Imports (all magnesium forms, incl. metal, alloys, powders, scrap):** **\~90‚ÄØkt in 2024\.** *(Your draft‚Äôs ‚Äú3.24‚ÄØkt (2022)‚Äù figure is off by two orders of magnitude for the US market.)* [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

* **Canada**

  * **Primary magnesium metal:** **0** (no operating smelters). Canada has magnesite and magnesia activities but **no primary Mg metal production** at present. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2022/myb1-2022-magnesium-metal.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia**

  * **Primary magnesium metal:** **0** in 2023‚Äì2024; Australia mines magnesite and magnesia but **has no operating primary Mg metal plant** today. (Australia is not listed among producing countries in the USGS global magnesium table.) [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

* **European Union/UK/Norway/Iceland**

  * **Primary magnesium metal:** **0**. Europe‚Äôs **last primary Mg plants shut in 2001‚Äì2002**; the EU is ‚Äúalmost totally dependent‚Äù on Chinese supply (‚âà95‚Äì97% of EU imports in recent years). [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/business/energy/europes-magnesium-crunch-poses-another-carbon-conundrum-andy-home-2021-10-26/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[European Commission](https://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/SEPDF/cache/118506.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Eurofer](https://www.eurofer.eu/publications/position-papers/joint-statement-on-magnesium-supply-shortage?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Japan**

  * **Primary magnesium metal:** **0** (no domestic primary production; Japanese demand is met by imports). [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

**Bottom line (today):** Among the U.S. and close allies listed above, **primary Mg production is effectively nil** (U.S. smelter idle since 2022; EU/Australia/Canada/Japan \= 0). The U.S. market relies on **large imports (\~90‚ÄØkt in 2024\)** and **substantial recycling (\~110‚ÄØkt in 2024\)**; the EU is \>95% import‚Äëreliant on China. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)[European Commission](https://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/SEPDF/cache/118506.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Demand 2030 (tons)**

* **Anchors (measured baselines):**

  * **United States:** reported *primary* Mg consumption ‚âà **50‚ÄØkt/yr** in 2024 (note: this excludes secondary metal used in‚Äëhouse). [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

  * **European Union:** press and industry analyses imply EU demand **\~180‚ÄØkt/yr** (inferred because a planned 90‚ÄØkt/yr plant in Romania is described as ‚Äúabout half‚Äù of EU needs). [Financial Times](https://www.ft.com/content/f77bf51f-0cae-42bf-8d9c-c11d24dac906?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **Japan:** import‚Äëdependent; public trade tallies and industry reviews place Japan‚Äôs annual Mg consumption on the order of **\~20‚Äì30‚ÄØkt**. *(Authoritative, consolidated Japanese consumption figures are not published annually by METI; market syntheses and import data point to this range.)* [IndexBox](https://www.indexbox.io/blog/magnesium-world-market-overview-2024/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Use pattern today (U.S.):** **Castings ‚âà65%** of reported primary consumption, **aluminum‚Äëbase alloys ‚âà22%**, **desulfurization ‚âà6%** (remainder other). This corrects the common shorthand that ‚Äúmost Mg goes to Al alloying‚Äù‚Äîthat‚Äôs not current for the U.S. market mix. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

* **Vehicle content correction:** A typical *passenger vehicle* today contains **a few‚Äìto‚Äìlow‚Äëtens of kilograms** of Mg parts (U.S. fleet average was \~3‚Äì12‚ÄØkg per vehicle in recent studies); **EV battery enclosures are predominantly aluminum**, not 60‚ÄØkg of magnesium. (So the ‚Äú\~60‚ÄØkg Mg per EV pack‚Äù claim is not supported.) [Powdermet Inc.](https://powdermetinc.com/the-potential-for-magnesium-forgings-in-automotive/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Reasonable 2030 allied demand range:** Using the measured anchors (EU \~180‚ÄØkt; U.S. \~50‚ÄØkt; Japan \~20‚Äì30‚ÄØkt; plus Canada & Australia industrial demand), a **planning range of \~260‚Äì340‚ÄØkt/yr** for U.S.+EU+Japan by 2030 is defensible, with upside if EV/industrial adoption of Mg castings accelerates. *(Global consumption is \~1.0‚ÄØMt; allied share plausibly sits in the low‚Äëto‚Äëmid‚Äëhundreds of kilotons.)* [Light Metal Age](https://www.lightmetalage.com/news/industry-news/magnesium/global-magnesium-market-supply-demand-and-future-outlook/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)[Financial Times](https://www.ft.com/content/f77bf51f-0cae-42bf-8d9c-c11d24dac906?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
