## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Supply 2030 (tons)**

* **United States**

  * **Existing smelter (Utah):** Nameplate **\~64‚ÄØkt/yr** capacity, but **idle since 2022**; restart timing unknown (force majeure in 2021; layoffs and idling noted through late 2024). If restarted by 2030, it could contribute materially; if not, **primary U.S. output remains 0**. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

  * **New route ‚Äî seawater/brine electrolysis:** **Magrathea** (California) received **DPA Title III support (\~$28‚ÄØM)** and has produced **pilot‚Äëscale metal**; first commercial unit is being developed (capacity not yet public at scale). Treat any 2030 tonnage as **emerging, low‚Äëtens‚Äëof‚Äëkt at most** unless new disclosures are made. * **Australia**

  * **Magnium (CSIRO‚Äëderived process):** target **\~100‚ÄØkt/yr by \~2032**; **by 2030**, tens‚Äëof‚Äëkt is a reasonable *upper* bound if timelines hold. (Australia otherwise has no operating primary plant.) [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/publication/mcs2025?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Canada**

  * No operating primary magnesium metal plants. Mining of magnesite (e.g., Record Ridge) does not itself create Mg metal without a smelter; any 2030 metal tonnage is **contingent on new refining capacity**. [US Magnesium](https://usmagnesium.com/about-us-mag/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Aggregate 2030 outlook (plausible, if projects commission):**

  * **EU (Romania)** \~90‚ÄØkt \+ **U.S.** (Utah restart **or** first commercial brine unit) **0‚Äì60‚ÄØkt** \+ **Australia** (Magnium) **\~0‚Äì30‚ÄØkt** ‚áí **\~90‚Äì180‚ÄØkt/yr** allied *primary* supply by 2030 **in an optimistic scenario**. That still trails allied demand (\~260‚Äì340‚ÄØkt/yr), implying **continued heavy import reliance** and the need for **recycling** to help close the gap. [U.S. Geological Survey+1](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)[Financial Times](https://www.ft.com/content/f77bf51f-0cae-42bf-8d9c-c11d24dac906?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Global context:** World primary Mg production was **\~1.0‚ÄØMt in 2024**, with **China \~0.95‚ÄØMt** (‚âà95%) and global smelter capacity ‚âà2.1‚ÄØMt (unused headroom largely in China). [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

## **Key Discovery Technologies**

* **Geologic targeting (magnesite, dolomite, serpentinized ultramafics):** Mapping Mg‚Äëcarbonate belts and altered ultramafic bodies; confirm with soil/stream geochemistry (high **MgO**, **Mg/Ca** ratios). Remote sensing (VNIR/SWIR hyperspectral) distinguishes **magnesite vs. calcite/dolomite** via diagnostic OH‚Äëband shifts. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025.pdf?utm_campaign=burnaby+now%3A+outbound&utm_medium=referral&utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Brine reconnaissance:** Sampling **saline lakes, evaporites, and seawater‚Äëderived brines** for Mg¬≤‚Å∫ concentration and impurity load (boron, sulfate, Ca¬≤‚Å∫), to assess electrolytic feed suitability. (USGS notes global Mg resources in brines and seawater are *enormous*.) [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

* **Industrial by‚Äëproduct screening:** Assay **red mud** (bauxite residue), **desal brines**, and **chemical plant brines** as potential Mg sources for integrated processes. [Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_MAGNESIUM.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **Silicothermic (Pidgeon) reduction (dolomite‚ÜíMg):** Calcined dolomite (MgO¬∑CaO) \+ FeSi reductant ‚Üí Mg vapor under **vacuum (‚âà1,150‚Äì1,400‚ÄØ¬∞C)**; vapor condenses to metal; slag is mainly **Ca‚Äësilicates**. Widely used in China; proposed for Europe (Verde). [The Romania Journal](https://www.romaniajournal.ro/business/europe-resumes-magnesium-extraction-to-reduce-china-dependency/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Electrolysis of MgCl‚ÇÇ (Dow‚Äëtype):** Dehydrated MgCl‚ÇÇ melts (often from brines/carnallite) are electrolyzed \~**700‚ÄØ¬∞C**, yielding Mg metal and Cl‚ÇÇ. This was the Utah route and is the basis for several new seawater/brine concepts (e.g., Magrathea). [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)[Chemical & Engineering News](https://cen.acs.org/business/specialty-chemicals/US-Defense-Department-funds-chemical/102/web/2024/02?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Emerging molten‚Äësalt MgO electrolysis (FFC‚Äëtype / variants):** Direct electroreduction of MgO in CaCl‚ÇÇ‚Äëbased melts‚Äî**low‚Äëcarbon** potential if powered by renewables; at lab/pilot scale. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/business/energy/europes-magnesium-crunch-poses-another-carbon-conundrum-andy-home-2021-10-26/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Separation Technologies**

*(For magnesium, ‚Äúseparation‚Äù is mostly physical/thermal within the reduction route.)*

* **Vapor‚Äìcondensation separation:** In Pidgeon/aluminothermic routes, **Mg vapor** is the separation medium‚Äîcondensing away from high‚Äëboiling oxide slag. [The Romania Journal](https://www.romaniajournal.ro/business/europe-resumes-magnesium-extraction-to-reduce-china-dependency/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Brine purification & solvent/ion‚Äëexchange polishing:** Prior to electrolysis, **Ca¬≤‚Å∫/SO‚ÇÑ¬≤‚Åª/B** are removed (lime/soda ash, sulfate removal), and traces polished (IX/SX) to protect cells and raise current efficiency. (Standard practice in electrolytic flowsheets.) [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **Vacuum distillation / re‚Äëdistillation:** The workhorse for **5N‚Äì6N** Mg‚Äîflash under vacuum to volatilize Mg and leave tramp metals behind; used as a final polish after thermal or electrolytic primary production. [Data.gov](https://catalog.data.gov/dataset/mineral-commodity-summaries-2025-magnesium-metal-data-release?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Fluxing & filtration:** Chlorination/flux refining and ceramic filtration to remove **MgO/dross** before casting; sometimes followed by **argon degassing**. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies**

* **Effluent neutralization & Mg(OH)‚ÇÇ recovery:** Neutralize acidic/alkaline effluents; precipitate **Mg(OH)‚ÇÇ** for reuse or safe disposal; treat halogen gases (Cl‚ÇÇ/HCl) in scrubbers to produce saleable acid/bleach. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

* **Red‚Äëmud/solid waste valorization:** Convert alkaline **Ca‚Äësilicate slags** (from Pidgeon) and residues into cementitious additives; reduce landfill. EU studies emphasize red‚Äëmud beneficiation and stabilization. [Scrreen](https://scrreen.eu/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/SCRREEN2_factsheets_MAGNESIUM.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Closed‚Äëloop water/brine management:** Evaporation/crystallization to recover salts (NaCl/KCl), **RO/nanofiltration** to minimize discharge‚Äînow standard in modern plants. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

---

## **Key Bottleneck Technology for US & Allies**

**Primary reduction at meaningful, low‚Äëcarbon scale** is the choke point. The West has **little operating primary capacity** (U.S. smelter idle; EU/JP/AU non‚Äëoperational), and classical routes are **energy‚Äë and carbon‚Äëintensive** (Pidgeon vacuum heating; conventional electrolysis), which complicates economics under Western power/carbon prices. Even with Verde (EU) and a Magrathea‚Äëtype route (US), allied capacity in 2030 likely **lags demand by \>100‚ÄØkt/yr** without further builds or restarts. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)[Financial Times](https://www.ft.com/content/f77bf51f-0cae-42bf-8d9c-c11d24dac906?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

### **Bottleneck summary (2‚Äì4 sentences)**

Despite abundant resources (brines, magnesite, dolomite), **installed primary Mg capacity** in the U.S./EU/Japan/Australia is **minimal or idle**. Classical processes (Pidgeon, MgCl‚ÇÇ electrolysis) carry **high energy and CO‚ÇÇ costs**, while next‚Äëgen **low‚Äëcarbon electrolysis** is only at **pilot** stage. Near‚Äëterm additions (e.g., **Verde \~90‚ÄØkt/yr**) help but still leave a **material shortfall** vs. allied demand, so **processing capacity‚Äînot geology‚Äîis the limiting factor** through 2030\. [Financial Times](https://www.ft.com/content/f77bf51f-0cae-42bf-8d9c-c11d24dac906?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

---

### **Quick list of the most important corrections vs. your draft**

* **U.S. imports are \~90‚ÄØkt (2024), not 3.24‚ÄØkt (2022).** [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

* **U.S. primary production \= 0 since 2022 (plant idle),** but **capacity \~64‚ÄØkt/yr exists**; future restart uncertain. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-magnesium-metal.pdf)

* **EU has had no primary production since 2001‚Äì2002** and is **\~95‚Äì97% dependent** on China. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/business/energy/europes-magnesium-crunch-poses-another-carbon-conundrum-andy-home-2021-10-26/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[European Commission](https://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/SEPDF/cache/118506.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Vehicle Mg content:** per‚Äëvehicle Mg is **single‚Äëdigit to low‚Äëtens of kg**; **60‚ÄØkg per EV battery housing** is not supported. [Powdermet Inc.](https://powdermetinc.com/the-potential-for-magnesium-forgings-in-automotive/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

# Ytterbium

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Current Production (tons)**

* **United States (Mountain Pass, CA).**  
   Mountain Pass is the only operating REE mine in the U.S. It produced **\~45,000 t REO in 2024** (ore is *bastn√§site*, strongly **LREE‚Äëbiased**). Ytterbium is a heavy REE and occurs only in **trace** amounts in this ore, and the U.S. does **not** report any separated Yb production today. MP‚Äôs ‚ÄúUpstream 60K‚Äù program is an on‚Äësite mining/separation expansion toward \~60 kt/y of rare‚Äëearth **products**, focused on NdPr and other LREEs; it does not imply material Yb output. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0169136823001439?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia.**  
   Australia‚Äôs 2024 mine production was **\~13,000 t REO** (USGS estimate). Lynas remains the largest non‚ÄëChina producer; it is expanding cracking/leach and separation, and adding **heavy‚ÄëREE separation (Dy/Tb)** capability (Malaysia; U.S. DPA‚Äëbacked work in Texas), but Yb is not a target product and any Yb in Mt Weld feed is **very small**. Iluka‚Äôs **Eneabba Rare Earths Refinery** (WA) is due to start up **around 2027** with **heavy‚ÄëREE** capability, improving allied HREE processing generally.

* **Canada.**  
   No operating rare‚Äëearth mine at present; **Canada‚Äôs 2024 REO mine production is 0** in USGS reporting. (Processing pilots exist, but they rely on imported concentrates.)

* **European Union / UK / Norway / Iceland.**  
   No commercial REE mining yet; Europe is building separation capacity (e.g., Iluka‚Äôs Eneabba in Australia feeding allied markets; Solvay La Rochelle continues specialty separation in France), but **no EU mine** contributes Yb today.

* **Japan.**  
   No domestic mining. Japan is piloting **deep‚Äësea REE mud** test mining near Minami‚ÄëTorishima in **fiscal 2026**, but this has not yet translated into terrestrial Yb supply.

**Takeaway:** Allied *mine* output exists (U.S., Australia), but **Yb‚Äëspecific production is essentially nil** today in the alliance because current orebodies are LREE‚Äërich (bastn√§site) and heavy‚ÄëREE separation circuits focus on Dy/Tb rather than Yb. Yb is geologically concentrated in **xenotime** and other HREE minerals, not in Mountain Pass bastn√§site. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/fs/2014/3078/pdf/fs2014-3078.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Demand 2030 (tons)**

* **Primary uses.** Ytterbium is a key **laser dopant** (e.g., Yb‚Äëdoped fiber lasers; Yb:YAG/thin‚Äëdisk lasers) for industrial cutting/welding, medical, and defense systems; it also appears in certain glasses, scintillators, and niche alloys. These applications are growing with industrial laser adoption. [Encyclopedia Britannica](https://www.britannica.com/technology/laser/Fundamental-principles?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Optica Publishing Group](https://opg.optica.org/abstract.cfm?uri=oe-29-10-15724&utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Quantification is sparse.** Neither USGS nor EU public statistics break out Yb tonnages. Given:  
   (i) Yb is a **minor** lanthanide by volume;  
   (ii) Yb loadings in laser media are **small** (gram‚Äëlevel per kW‚Äëclass device); and  
   (iii) laser markets are growing mid‚Äësingle to low‚Äëdouble digits,  
   a **planning band** for **allied 2030 demand** is likely **on the order of a few‚Äëtens of tonnes per year of Yb oxide equivalent**, not hundreds. This is consistent with Yb‚Äôs role (high value, low mass) relative to bulk magnet REEs. *(Caveat: precise public forecasts do not exist; this band reflects the scale of laser/media usage and current market structure.)* [Encyclopedia Britannica](https://www.britannica.com/technology/laser/Fundamental-principles?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Supply 2030 (tons)**

* **What changes by 2030?**

  * **U.S.:** MP‚Äôs **Upstream 60K** expansion increases overall RE product throughput, but is **NdPr‚Äëcentric**; there is **no announced Yb product line**. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0169136823001439?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  * **Australia:** Lynas‚Äôs added **heavy‚ÄëREE separation** (Malaysia) is slated to process **\~1,500 t/y of heavy‚Äëoxide feed** (Dy/Tb focus) by mid‚Äëdecade. **Iluka Eneabba** is scheduled to come online **\~2027** with heavy‚ÄëREE separation (HREO capability and initial REO capacity **\~23 kt/y**), enabling *some* recovery of the full HREE suite from suitable feeds.

  * **Japan/EU/Canada:** No new mines expected to contribute meaningful Yb by 2030; separation capacity may **toll** imported mixed concentrates.

* **Implication.** Even with these projects, **separated Yb output in allied jurisdictions will likely remain very small (order: low‚Äëtens of tonnes per year at most)**, because feedstocks are LREE‚Äëdominant and commercial circuits prioritize Dy/Tb. The bulk of Yb oxide is expected to remain **import‚Äësourced** unless dedicated xenotime/HREE deposits are developed and processed in‚Äëbloc.

---

## **References for volumes & geology**

* **U.S. & global REO production (2024):** USGS **Mineral Commodity Summaries 2025 ‚Äî Rare Earths** (U.S. **45,000 t**, Australia **13,000 t**; table & narrative).

* **MP Materials expansion:** ‚Äú**Upstream 60K**‚Äù description (SEC 10‚ÄëK excerpt). [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0169136823001439?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Lynas heavy‚ÄëREE separation (Dy/Tb):** Argus reporting on Lynas‚Äôs Malaysia heavy‚ÄëREE upgrades.

* **Iluka Eneabba (HREE refinery):** Iluka/Fluor: Eneabba refinery **to operate in 2027**; **\~23 kt/y REO** nameplate; designed for **heavy‚ÄëREE** capability.

* **Japan deep‚Äësea REE mud timeline:** JOGMEC/Waseda (test mining targeted for early **FY2026**).

* **Yb occurrence:** Xenotime is an HREE host; monazite contains only **trace Yb** (often **\~0.03%**). [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/fs/2014/3078/pdf/fs2014-3078.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Discovery Technologies (most relevant to HREE/Yb)**

* **Radiometric surveys (U/Th):** Monazite and xenotime are commonly Th‚Äëbearing; airborne or ground **gamma** mapping highlights prospective heavy‚Äëmineral sands and carbonatites. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/fs/2014/3078/pdf/fs2014-3078.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Geoscience Australia](https://www.ga.gov.au/scientific-topics/minerals/mineral-resources-and-advice/australian-resource-reviews/rare-earth-elements?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Geological mapping & geochemistry:** Focus on **carbonatites** and **heavy‚Äëmineral placers** containing xenotime/monazite; systematic soil/stream geochem and pXRF/ICP‚ÄëMS delineate REE halos. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/publication/cir930N?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Virginia Energy](https://energy.virginia.gov/geology/REE.shtml?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Magnetics & gravity:** Many carbonatites and HIMS placer systems present diagnostic magnetic/gravity signatures for target ranking. [netl.doe.gov](https://www.netl.doe.gov/sites/default/files/netl-file/S-T-REE-TechTeam-Mtg-062716-TBank-Classification-Scheme-of-REE-deposits.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **Physical concentration:** For hard‚Äërock/placer feed, gravity \+ high‚Äëintensity magnetic/electrostatic separation concentrate **xenotime/monazite** (dense, often paramagnetic) before chemistry. [Geoscience Australia](https://www.ga.gov.au/scientific-topics/minerals/mineral-resources-and-advice/australian-resource-reviews/rare-earth-elements?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **‚ÄúCracking‚Äù of phosphates:** Monazite/xenotime typically require **acid baking/pressure leach (H‚ÇÇSO‚ÇÑ/HCl)** or **alkaline digestion** to break phosphate bonds and dissolve REEs for downstream separation.

---

## **Key Separation Technologies**

* **Solvent extraction (SX) cascades:** Organophosphorus extractants (e.g., **D2EHPA/HEHEHP/Cyanex**) with careful **pH control** split LREE/MREE/HREE; Yb is recovered in late HREE circuits after Th/Fe removal and Ce handling. (Commercial upgrades today prioritize Dy/Tb.)

* **Ion‚Äëexchange / chromatography:** Used at smaller scale to polish **high‚Äëpurity Yb** fractions (resin columns, chelating ligands).

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **Metallothermic reduction \+ vacuum distillation**: Industrially, Yb metal can be made by **reducing Yb‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ/YbF‚ÇÉ with Ca (or other active metals)** in molten‚Äësalt media, then **selectively distilling** Yb to high purity due to its relatively low boiling point among REEs. [Google Patents+1](https://patents.google.com/patent/EP0170372A1/en?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[OSTI](https://www.osti.gov/servlets/purl/5923208?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Molten‚Äësalt electrolysis (R\&D ‚Üí pilot):** Electro‚Äëextraction of Yb from molten **chloride/fluoride** salts (e.g., NaCl‚ÄìCaCl‚ÇÇ or LiF‚ÄìYbF‚ÇÉ) is under study and has been demonstrated at lab scale. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S1572665724003928?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[SSRN](https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/Delivery.cfm/30372a46-5f35-4fea-8da4-da1385ddfc7f-MECA.pdf?abstractid=4804407&mirid=1&utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies**

* **Tailings/waste reprocessing:** Acid leach \+ SX on legacy heavy‚Äëmineral sands/tailings can recover REEs (including HREEs) while stabilizing Th/U, lowering site liabilities.

* **Water treatment / zero‚Äëdischarge:** Lime neutralization, ion‚Äëexchange polishing, and high recovery water circuits are standard to control radionuclides and dissolved metals from REE processing.

---

## **Key Bottleneck technology for US and Allies ‚Äî Yb**

* **Heavy‚ÄëREE separation capacity and feedstock mix.** Allied mines today are **LREE‚Äëweighted** (e.g., Mountain Pass bastn√§site). Commercial expansions (Lynas, Iluka) emphasize Dy/Tb; **Yb is not an economic focus** and remains a **late‚Äëstage, low‚Äëconcentration** product in SX trains. Without **xenotime‚Äërich feed** and **dedicated HREE circuits**, allied Yb volumes stay very small.

### **Bottleneck summary (2‚Äì4 sentences)**

The limiting step is **not mining tonnage but chemistry and feed mix**: allied operations process mostly **LREE** ore, and the **heavy‚ÄëREE separation** capacity being built prioritizes Dy/Tb, not Yb. Because **Yb content is minute** in current allied feeds and Yb would emerge only very late in complex SX trains, separated Yb oxide production in the U.S./allies will likely remain **low‚Äëtens of tonnes per year (at best) by 2030** unless xenotime/HREE deposits are brought online and fully separated domestically.

---

### **Notes on a few statements you may have seen elsewhere**

* Mountain Pass ore is **bastn√§site**, not monazite/xenotime; **Yb is negligible** there. Yb commonly resides in **xenotime** (YPO‚ÇÑ) and other HREE minerals. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/fs/2014/3078/pdf/fs2014-3078.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* ‚ÄúYb ‚âà0.03% in monazite‚Äù is a reasonable order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude for *monazite* (not xenotime) and underscores why Yb is scarce in LREE‚Äërich bastn√§site systems.

# Hafnium

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Current Production (t/yr)**

* **France (EU).** France is presently the single largest allied producer. Industry reporting indicates France‚Äôs producer (Orano/Framatome) is making **\~30‚ÄØt Hf/yr** today and plans to **lift capacity to \~45‚ÄØt/yr** on the near‚Äëterm timeline as its zirconium/hafnium separation capacity is expanded. That scale implies **\~40‚Äì45% of current world Hf output** (global supply is still on the order of **70‚Äì75‚ÄØt/yr**). [CRM Alliance](https://www.crmalliance.eu/hafnium?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **United States.** There is **no mining** of hafnium; Hf is recovered when U.S. firms purify imported zirconium intermediates (the Zr industry must remove Hf for nuclear‚Äëgrade Zr). The **USGS (2025)** notes **one producer in Oregon and one in Utah** make zirconium **and hafnium** metal from Zr chemical feed. U.S. *unwrought hafnium* imports were **\~50‚ÄØt in 2024** (exports \~10‚ÄØt), underscoring dependence on foreign feed even though domestic metalmaking exists. Top 2024 import sources were **Germany (50%)**, **China (21%)**, **France (18%)**. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-zirconium-hafnium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Canada.** No domestic Hf metal production. Canadian heavy‚Äëmineral‚Äësand and ilmenite operations supply Ti/Zr materials, but **Hf is not refined domestically**. (The metal is produced mainly where zirconium is purified.) [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-zirconium-hafnium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia.** Major zircon producers (Iluka, Tronox) provide large **zircon concentrates** (ZrSiO‚ÇÑ) that typically contain **\~1‚Äì2‚ÄØ% HfO‚ÇÇ**‚Äîbut **Australia does not presently refine hafnium**; the Hf moves with zircon to foreign refiners. [PMC](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9568896/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Japan / Norway / Iceland.** No primary Hf mining; Japan processes and consumes zirconium intermediates but **imports hafnium‚Äëbearing feed** or finished Hf. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-zirconium-hafnium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Snapshot:** World Hf supply is still small (‚âà**70‚Äì75‚ÄØt/yr**), with **France** the lead allied producer and **U.S. capacity present but feed‚Äëdependent**.

---

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Demand 2030 (t/yr)**

* **Semiconductors.** HfO‚ÇÇ (high‚ÄëŒ∫ dielectrics in logic/DRAM, capacitors) ‚Äî industry outlook presented to the minor‚Äëmetals market projects semicon‚Äërelated Hf demand of **\~64‚ÄØt/yr by 2030** (up from \~40‚ÄØt/yr in 2024). Allied fabs (US, EU, JP, KR, TW) account for a major share of this segment.

* **Aerospace/superalloys.** Ni‚Äëbase and other high‚ÄëT alloys add Hf for grain‚Äëboundary strength; projected **\~60‚ÄØt/yr by 2030**.

* **Nuclear.** Control‚Äërod and related uses around **\~18‚ÄØt/yr by 2030**.

* **Total (global vs. allies).** Global demand is **\~180‚ÄØt/yr by 2030** in the cited market view. On reasonable market shares, the **US+allies** slice would be on the order of **\~70‚Äì100‚ÄØt/yr** (semiconductors \+ aerospace are ally‚Äëheavy).

---

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Supply 2030 (t/yr)**

* **France (EU).** Ramp from **\~30 to \~45‚ÄØt/yr** as new separation capacity comes on line; Framatome investment announcements around its **Jarrie** zirconium chain support increased Hf capability. [nuclearpowerdaily.com](https://www.nuclearpowerdaily.com/reports/Framatome_strengthens_hafnium_production_for_nuclear_aerospace_and_space_customers_999.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **United States.** USGS confirms **two U.S. metal producers** (OR, UT). Industry reporting says **U.S. plants could add on the order of \~50‚ÄØt/yr** if justified by economics and feedstock availability (i.e., more zirconium intermediates), but that would require capex and sustained supply. U.S. 2024 imports of unwrought Hf (‚âà**50‚ÄØt**) highlight the current gap. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-zirconium-hafnium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Recycling & process recovery.** Incremental tonnages could come from **improved de‚Äëhafniation at Zr plants** and **recycling of superalloy scrap**, but these are **single‚Äëdigit tonnes** in the near term.

* **New mining.** No allied Hf‚Äëspecific mines are planned; **Hf tracks zircon production** from mineral sands, so feed growth depends on zircon output and where it is refined. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-zirconium-hafnium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Working range:** If announced EU \+ potential U.S. expansions occur, **allied Hf supply could reach \~80‚Äì100‚ÄØt/yr by \~2030** (France ‚âà45‚ÄØt \+ incremental U.S. \+ minor secondary volumes). That is **tight** relative to projected global demand (\~180‚ÄØt/yr).

---

## **References for volumes (most probative)**

* **Market & capacity:** Argus (2025): global supply **\~70‚Äì75‚ÄØt/yr**, France **\~30‚ÄØt now ‚Üí 45‚ÄØt**, potential **U.S. \+50‚ÄØt** if expanded; notes tariff frictions and the very small producer base.

* **U.S. production & trade:** **USGS Mineral Commodity Summaries 2025 (Zirconium & Hafnium)** ‚Äî U.S. producers in **Oregon** and **Utah**; **2024 imports of unwrought Hf ‚âà 50‚ÄØt**; import sources (Germany 50%, China 21%, France 18%); Zr:Hf in zircon \~50:1. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-zirconium-hafnium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **EU/French capacity expansion:** Framatome press about strengthening hafnium production at **Jarrie** within its Zr chain. [nuclearpowerdaily.com](https://www.nuclearpowerdaily.com/reports/Framatome_strengthens_hafnium_production_for_nuclear_aerospace_and_space_customers_999.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Hf as zircon by‚Äëproduct / where it comes from:** USGS yearbook (2021) and professional paper: Hf is obtained during Zr purification; zircon from heavy‚Äëmineral sands is the feedstock. [U.S. Geological Survey+1](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-zirconium-hafnium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Zircon/Hf in mineral sands:** Peer‚Äëreviewed overview indicating zircon ((Zr,Hf)SiO‚ÇÑ) in heavy‚Äëmineral sands typically contains **\~1‚Äì2% HfO‚ÇÇ**; mining/processing basis. [PMC](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9568896/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Discovery Technologies**

* **Target paleoplacers for zircon.** Hafnium follows **zircon**; the practical ‚Äúexploration‚Äù is locating heavy‚Äëmineral sands (HMS) with high zircon. USGS deposit models and WNA explain HMS formation and the gravity/magnetic separations used. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/sir/2010/5070/l/pdf/sir2010-5070l.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[World Nuclear Association](https://world-nuclear.org/information-library/appendices/mineral-sands-appendix-to-norm-information-paper?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Radiometrics as a proxy.** HMS often include **monazite (Th‚Äëbearing)**; airborne gamma (Th channel) can map favorable strandlines and palaeobeaches that are also zircon‚Äërich. [World Nuclear Association](https://world-nuclear.org/information-library/appendices/mineral-sands-appendix-to-norm-information-paper?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Drilling & heavy‚Äëmineral logging.** Vibracore/rotary drilling with **spiral and magnetic bench tests** on the heavy fraction confirms zircon grade and thus Hf potential. [World Nuclear Association](https://world-nuclear.org/information-library/appendices/mineral-sands-appendix-to-norm-information-paper?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **Dredge/open‚Äëpit mining of HMS.** Slurry extraction, **wet gravity circuits (spirals)** to concentrate heavies on site. [World Nuclear Association](https://world-nuclear.org/information-library/appendices/mineral-sands-appendix-to-norm-information-paper?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Dry separation.** Magnetic/electrostatic separation to split **ilmenite/rutile** from **zircon/monazite**; zircon is the non‚Äëconductive, non‚Äëmagnetic fraction that carries Hf. [Earth Science](https://earthsci.org/mineral/mindep/minsand/minsand.html?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Separation Technologies (Zr‚ÄìHf split)**

* **Solvent extraction (hydrometallurgy).** Counter‚Äëcurrent SX in chloride/nitrate media with extractants such as **TBP**, **D2EHPA**, **Cyanex 272/572**, **Aliquat/Alamine** is the **workhorse**; tiny chemical differences are leveraged to separate Hf from Zr. Modern process studies and reviews outline the parameter windows and selectivity limits. [ResearchGate](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/287457696_Separation_of_Zirconium_and_Hafnium_A_Review?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MDPI](https://www.mdpi.com/2297-8739/11/4/93?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[SciELO](https://www.scielo.org.za/scielo.php?pid=S2225-62532016000100019&script=sci_arttext&utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Extractive distillation / volatility route.** **HfCl‚ÇÑ** and **ZrCl‚ÇÑ** have different volatilities; industrial chloride‚Äëdistillation trains can preferentially vaporize one tetrachloride to concentrate/strip **Hf**. [SpringerLink](https://link.springer.com/chapter/10.1007/978-3-319-48765-6_53?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **Kroll‚Äëtype chloride reduction.** **HfCl‚ÇÑ \+ Mg/Ca ‚Üí Hf sponge**, followed by leach/slag removal and **VAR/EB melting** to ingot. Route is analogous to zirconium metallurgy. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/pp/1802/v/pp1802v.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Melt refining.** **Vacuum arc remelting or electron‚Äëbeam melting** to aerospace/nuclear grades; optional **zone‚Äërefining** for ultra‚Äëhigh‚Äëpurity. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/pp/1802/v/pp1802v.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies (HMS context)**

* **Monazite/Th management.** HMS circuits co‚Äërecover **monazite**; industry adopts controlled handling/return‚Äëto‚Äëtails or separate REE processing with NORM controls (IAEA/WNA guidance), with water recycling and **dry‚Äëstacking** to minimize radionuclide mobility. [World Nuclear Association](https://world-nuclear.org/information-library/appendices/mineral-sands-appendix-to-norm-information-paper?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[IAEA Publications](https://www-pub.iaea.org/MTCD/Publications/PDF/Pub1512_web.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Process‚Äëwater treatment.** Neutralization and solid‚Äìliquid separation for fine clays and dissolved salts (standard HMS practice). [World Nuclear Association](https://world-nuclear.org/information-library/appendices/mineral-sands-appendix-to-norm-information-paper?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Bottleneck Technology for US & Allies**

* **Zr‚ÄìHf separation capacity (chemistry \+ plant).** The **principal choke point** is not ore, but **industrial separation** of Hf from Zr ‚Äî a **multi‚Äëstage, capital‚Äëintensive** SX or chloride‚Äëdistillation operation run by a **very small number of producers**. Recent market analysis highlights that the **limited producer base and separation bottleneck** are already constraining supply; even in the U.S., expansions hinge on feed availability and capex. Trade frictions (e.g., **U.S. tariffs near 80% on Chinese Hf**, **\~20% on French material**) further stress supply optionality.

### **Bottleneck summary (2‚Äì4 sentences)**

Hafnium supply is governed by **where zirconium is purified**, not where zircon is mined. Outside China/Russia, only a handful of allied facilities can economically **separate and refine Hf**, and those circuits are expensive to build and scale. With demand led by semiconductors and aerospace rising toward **\~180‚ÄØt/yr globally by 2030**, allied capacity expansions (France to \~45‚ÄØt; potential U.S. adds) help but **do not eliminate the constraint** unless additional separation trains are built and fed.

---

### **Notes on corrections vs. typical claims you might see**

* The U.S. **does produce** Hf metal (from imported Zr intermediates); it **does not mine** Hf. (USGS lists the Oregon and Utah metal producers and shows **\~50‚ÄØt of unwrought Hf imports** in 2024.) [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-zirconium-hafnium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* France‚Äôs production scale **(\~30‚Üí45‚ÄØt/yr)** and global supply **(\~70‚Äì75‚ÄØt/yr today)** are consistent with France being **\~40‚Äì45%** of global supply right now.

* **Hf occurs in zircon** and is recovered when Zr is purified ‚Äî so **zircon production location ‚â† hafnium production location**. (Most allied zircon is mined in Australia but the Hf is separated where Zr is processed.) [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/myb/vol1/2021/myb1-2021-zirconium-hafnium.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

# Aluminum

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Current Production (tons)**

* **United States.**  
   Primary aluminum production was **\~670,000 t in 2024** (down 11% y/y). Installed year‚Äëend primary capacity was **\~1.36 Mt**. Secondary recovery from scrap was **\~3.6 Mt** in 2024 (‚âà2.0 Mt from new scrap, 1.6 Mt from old scrap). Net import reliance for primary aluminum was **\~47% of apparent consumption** in 2024 (not \~85%).

* **Canada.**  
   Canada produced **\~3.2‚Äì3.3 Mt** of primary aluminum in 2023 and is consistently a top‚Äë5 global producer owing to hydro‚Äëpowered smelters in Qu√©bec and British Columbia.

* **Australia.**  
   Australia‚Äôs four coastal smelters (Tomago, Boyne Island, Bell Bay, Portland) produced **\~1.6 Mt** in 2024\.

* **European Union (EU‚Äë27 & UK).**  
   Primary production in the **EU‚Äë27** was **\~1.92 Mt in 2022** (latest consolidated figure); Western & Central Europe (EU‚Äë27+UK, excl. Russia) produced **\~2.71 Mt in 2023** amid continuing power‚Äëprice pressure. [JRC Publications](https://publications.jrc.ec.europa.eu/repository/bitstream/JRC136525/JRC136525_01.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[S\&P Global](https://www.spglobal.com/commodity-insights/en/news-research/latest-news/metals/101424-interview-european-aluminium-calls-for-swift-action-to-make-market-competitive?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Norway & Iceland.**  
   Norway produced **\~1.3 Mt** in 2023; Iceland‚Äôs three smelters have **\~0.86 Mt/y** combined capacity (e.g., Alcoa Fjar√∞a√°l \~346 kt). [Investing News Network (INN)](https://investingnews.com/aluminum-production-by-country/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Sj√°lfb√¶rniverkefni √° Austurlandi](https://www.sjalfbaerni.is/en/companies/utflutningur-fjardaals?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Japan.**  
   Domestic primary output is negligible; Japan meets demand via imports on the order of **\~1.0‚Äì1.1 Mt/y**.

**Takeaway:** In the allied bloc today, large primary tonnage comes from **Canada, Australia, Norway, and Iceland**, with the **U.S.** contributing a smaller (but material) **\~0.67 Mt** and **significant secondary (recycled) metal**.

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Demand 2030 (tons)**

Independent IAI/CRU modeling expects **strong regional demand growth by 2030**, driven by transport electrification, grid expansion, renewables, construction, and packaging:

* **North America:** **\+5.1 Mt** vs. 2020 baseline by 2030\.

* **Europe:** **\+4.8 Mt** vs. 2020 baseline by 2030\.

* **Rest of Asia ex‚ÄëChina (incl. Japan):** **\+8.6 Mt** vs. 2020 baseline by 2030\.

These are **incremental** tons (not totals) and imply that allied demand will be in the **mid‚Äëteens of Mt/y** in each of North America and Europe by 2030, even with rising recycling rates. [Recycling Today](https://www.recyclingtoday.com/news/iai-aluminum-demand-2020s-recycling-sustainability/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **US and Allies ‚Äî Domestic Supply 2030 (tons)**

* **United States (primary).**  
   The base is \~0.67 Mt (2024). Emirates Global Aluminium has **announced a new U.S. primary smelter (Oklahoma)**, capacity **600‚Äì700 kt/y**, targeted for **start‚Äëup in 2029** (subject to permitting, power and feedstock). If realized, U.S. primary output could approach **\~1.3‚Äì1.4 Mt/y** by 2030 before accounting for any restarts. **Note:** Alumina feed will be imported unless new domestic refinery capacity is built.

* **United States (secondary).**  
   Secondary production from purchased scrap was \~3.6 Mt in 2024; sustained scrap flows and capacity expansions suggest **U.S. secondary supply remains the largest domestic source of metal** into 2030\.

* **Canada.**  
   Hydro‚Äëpowered smelters remain a cornerstone. Rio Tinto is adding **\~160 kt/y** at the AP60 Saguenay Complex (Quebec) by **2026**, bringing Canada closer to **\~3.4‚Äì3.5 Mt/y** by 2030 (assuming stable power). [RMI](https://rmi.org/delivering-a-net-zero-future-for-aluminum/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia.**  
   Absent new builds, production likely **\~1.5‚Äì1.6 Mt/y** by 2030, contingent on power price and grid decarbonization.

* **Europe, Norway, Iceland.**  
   Western & Central Europe primary output fell to **\~2.7 Mt (2023)** and remains constrained by energy costs; **Norway (\~1.3 Mt)** and **Iceland (\~0.8‚Äì0.9 Mt)** provide the bulk of low‚Äëcarbon European‚Äëarea primary metal (hydro power). Net imports remain structurally high. [S\&P Global](https://www.spglobal.com/commodity-insights/en/news-research/latest-news/metals/101424-interview-european-aluminium-calls-for-swift-action-to-make-market-competitive?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Investing News Network (INN)](https://investingnews.com/aluminum-production-by-country/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Sj√°lfb√¶rniverkefni √° Austurlandi](https://www.sjalfbaerni.is/en/companies/utflutningur-fjardaals?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Indicative 2030 allied supply picture:**

* **Primary (U.S., Canada, Australia, EU‚Äë27+UK, Norway, Iceland):** on the order of **\~9‚Äì10 Mt/y** if the U.S. smelter proceeds and other regions maintain output.

* **Secondary (recycled metal in U.S. \+ EU):** several **million tons per year** (U.S. \~3.5‚Äì4 Mt, EU \~5‚Äì6 Mt), critical to balancing demand. [S\&P Global](https://www.spglobal.com/commodity-insights/en/news-research/latest-news/metals/101424-interview-european-aluminium-calls-for-swift-action-to-make-market-competitive?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **Key Discovery Technologies (bauxite targeting)**

* **Hyperspectral & multispectral imaging.** Distinguishes bauxite‚Äëforming minerals (gibbsite, boehmite, kaolinite, goethite) to map lateritic caps. [Aluminum Association](https://www.aluminum.org/alumina-refining-101?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Geologic mapping & geochemistry.** Identifies ancient planation surfaces and residual laterites; soil/stream geochem confirms Al‚Äërich horizons. [Aluminum Association](https://www.aluminum.org/alumina-refining-101?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Aerogeophysics & downhole logging.** Magnetics/gravity/EM help infer laterite thickness and basin architecture; borehole density and gamma logs delineate ore profiles. (EU technical guidebook.) [European Environment Agency](https://www.eea.europa.eu/en/analysis/publications/emep-eea-guidebook-2023/part-b-sectoral-guidance-chapters/2-industrial-processes-and-product-use/2-c-metal-production/2-c-3-aluminium-production-2023/%40%40download/file?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **Open‚Äëpit bauxite mining.** Strip mining of laterites, then washing/crushing to slurry. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0301751613000860?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Bayer process (alumina).** Hot NaOH digestion (‚âà140‚ÄØ¬∞C for gibbsite; 200‚Äì280‚ÄØ¬∞C for boehmite/diaspore), clarification, precipitation of Al(OH)‚ÇÉ, and calcination to Al‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0301751613000860?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Hall‚ÄìH√©roult smelting (primary Al).** Electrolysis of alumina in molten cryolite at \~950‚ÄØ¬∞C with carbon anodes. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0301751613000860?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Separation Technologies**

* **Residue (red‚Äëmud) solid‚Äìliquid separation.** Thickening/filtration and multi‚Äëstage washing recover caustic liquor. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0301751613000860?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Seeded precipitation & classification.** Controlled precipitation of Al(OH)‚ÇÉ and size classification before calcination. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0301751613000860?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Secondary sorting (recycling).** Eddy‚Äëcurrent separators and LIBS/X‚Äëray systems grade and sort aluminum scrap streams for high‚Äëyield remelting. [Aluminum Association](https://www.aluminum.org/alumina-refining-101?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **Electrolytic reduction (Hall‚ÄìH√©roult).** Industry standard; incremental efficiency gains via advanced cell control and low‚Äëenergy cell designs (e.g., Hydro Karm√∏y HAL4e). [Light Metal Age Magazine](https://www.lightmetalage.com/news/industry-news/smelting/karmoy-technology-pilot-world-leader-primary-aluminum-energy-efficiency/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Fluxing/degassing and DC casting.** On‚Äëfurnace metal cleaning (inert gas/Cl‚ÇÇ), filtration, and direct‚Äëchill casting of ingots/billets. [Aluminum Association](https://www.aluminum.org/alumina-refining-101?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Secondary melting.** Recycled aluminum remelting (reverb/induction) uses \~1/10 the energy of primary production; salt‚Äëslag treatment closes loops. [European Environment Agency](https://www.eea.europa.eu/en/analysis/publications/emep-eea-guidebook-2023/part-b-sectoral-guidance-chapters/2-industrial-processes-and-product-use/2-c-metal-production/2-c-3-aluminium-production-2023/%40%40download/file?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies**

* **Red‚Äëmud neutralization & valorization.** Seawater/lime neutralization (pH control), with research into geopolymer bricks and treatment media (‚Äúbauxsol‚Äù). [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0959652622024027?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Dry stacking & water recycling.** Filter‚Äëpressing of residue, closed‚Äëloop water circuits to minimize discharge. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0301751613000860?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Spent potliner (SPL) treatment.** Detoxification (e.g., controlled thermal treatment, lime scrubbing to immobilize F‚Åª/CN‚Åª) and material recovery. (EU process guidance.) [European Environment Agency](https://www.eea.europa.eu/en/analysis/publications/emep-eea-guidebook-2023/part-b-sectoral-guidance-chapters/2-industrial-processes-and-product-use/2-c-metal-production/2-c-3-aluminium-production-2023/%40%40download/file?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Bottleneck technology for US and Allies Domestic Production**

* **Power‚Äë and carbon‚Äëintensive smelting.** Primary Al still relies on **Hall‚ÄìH√©roult with carbon anodes**; absent widespread **inert‚Äëanode** deployment and very low‚Äëcost clean power, allied expansions face cost/CO‚ÇÇ headwinds. The IEA notes electricity dominates smelter costs and decarbonization needs breakthroughs (inert anodes, CCS). [ELYSIS](https://elysis.com/en/rio-tinto-and-alcoa-announce-worlds-first-carbon-free-aluminium-smelting-process?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Alumina feedstock & regional refining gaps.** The U.S. lacks domestic bauxite/alumina refining capacity; even a new U.S. smelter would **import alumina**, adding supply‚Äëchain risk.

### **Bottleneck summary (2‚Äì4 sentences)**

Aluminum‚Äôs chokepoint is **smelting technology plus power**, not geology. The allied bloc‚Äôs ability to add low‚Äëcarbon primary capacity is constrained by the **Hall‚ÄìH√©roult energy/CO‚ÇÇ penalty** and the lack of **inert‚Äëanode** systems at commercial scale; cheap, firm, low‚Äëcarbon electricity is also essential. At the same time, gaps in **alumina refining** (notably in the U.S.) mean even new smelters depend on imported feed. Until these mid‚Äëstream constraints are addressed, allies will meet demand growth primarily through **recycling** and **imports**, with selective primary additions (e.g., Canada, Norway/Iceland, the planned U.S. smelter). [ELYSIS](https://elysis.com/en/rio-tinto-and-alcoa-announce-worlds-first-carbon-free-aluminium-smelting-process?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

### **Notes on key corrections from your draft**

* **U.S. import reliance:** recent USGS shows **\~47%** (2024), not \~85%.

* **U.S. primary tonnage:** **\~0.67 Mt in 2024**; 2022 was **\~0.86 Mt** (your 0.87 Mt was close).

* **EGA project:** credible plan for a **600‚Äì700 kt/y** Oklahoma smelter with **2029** start‚Äëup target.

# Thulium

## **US and Allies Domestic Current Production (tons)**

* **United States.** One operating REE mine (MP Materials, Mountain Pass, CA) produces LREE‚Äërich bastn√§site concentrates; heavy REEs (including Tm) are **negligible** in this ore and there is **no separated Tm** produced domestically today. U.S. rare‚Äëearth mine output was \~43‚ÄØkt REO in 2023, but this is almost entirely LREEs (Ce‚ÄìNd), with Tm only in trace amounts in the deposit.  
   *Context:* U.S. midstream efforts are progressing‚ÄîEnergy Fuels commissioned on‚Äëspec NdPr oxide in 2024 and plans initial Dy/Tb output in 2025‚Äîbut these lines target magnet REEs first; any Tm would be a minute tail fraction much later in the separation train.

* **Australia.** Lynas (Mt Weld) is the leading allied miner/processor. In 2025 it reported the **first separated Dy and Tb outside China**, a step toward broader HREE capability; however, Tm remains an **ultra‚Äëminor** constituent in Mt Weld flows and is not a declared product stream. Iluka‚Äôs Eneabba HREE refinery (WA) is ramping mid‚Äëdecade, likewise focused on Dy/Tb first. Net: **no material separated Tm tonnage** published from Australia.

* **Canada.** No sustained REE mine producing Tm today (Vital‚Äôs Nechalacho pilot ceased; Canada‚Äôs SRC is a processor). **Tm output \~0.** (General production status from public agencies/press; no Tm line.)

* **Europe (EU/UK/Norway/Iceland).** No operating REE mines. Some separation capability exists (e.g., Solvay/Neo for selected RE streams), but **no published separated Tm output**; Europe relies on imports for HREEs.

* **Japan.** No domestic REE mining; uses imported RE products. **No primary Tm production.** (Japan and allied Asia are net importers of HREEs.)

**Global context:** Multiple reputable references put **world Tm oxide production at \~50‚ÄØt/yr**, underscoring how small this market is. Allied share of that is currently **near zero** because separated Tm streams are largely produced in China. [dggs.alaska.gov](https://dggs.alaska.gov/pubs/id/30821?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **US and Allies Domestic Demand 2030 (tons)**

* **Use profile (Tm‚Äôs niche):** Tm is used mainly in **lasers** (Tm‚Äëdoped fiber/YAG at \~2‚ÄØ¬µm for medical and industrial uses), select **photonics/glass**, and **radioisotope sources** (legacy portable X‚Äëray; niche). These are small but technologically strategic markets. (General technical use notes; see also China demand modelling below.)

* **Order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude demand.** Hard measured, public, ex‚ÄëChina Tm demand time series are scarce. Two anchors:

  1. **Supply‚Äëside:** global Tm oxide output is widely cited as **\~50‚ÄØt/yr**, implying similar global consumption today. [dggs.alaska.gov](https://dggs.alaska.gov/pubs/id/30821?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

  2. **China model:** a peer‚Äëreviewed input‚Äìoutput study estimates **China‚Äôs final demand** for Tm reached **\~208‚ÄØt in 2020**, highlighting uncertainty and potential unreported/stock changes; it also flags Tm‚Äôs steep price volatility. (Note: this is an economic model, not a shipment tally.)

* **Planning range for allies (2030).** Given (i) very small present supply, (ii) continued growth of **fiber‚Äëlaser** markets (\~mid‚Äësingle‚Äëdigit CAGR into the 2030s), and (iii) allied onshoring of critical photonics/medical manufacturing, a **reasonable planning bracket** for **US+EU+JP+CA+AU** is **\~50‚Äì120‚ÄØt/yr (Tm oxide equivalent) by 2030**. The low end aligns with today‚Äôs global physical supply; the high end reflects upside if Tm‚Äëlaser adoption and allied reshoring outpace today‚Äôs baseline. (Laser demand growth benchmark.)

*What it means:* Tm remains a **tiny‚Äëtonnage**, high‚Äëvalue input. Even modest programmatic buys (defense/medical) can move the market.

---

## **US and Allies Domestic Supply 2030 (tons)**

* **United States.** Mountain Pass is LREE; **no mine‚Äëgate Tm.** Energy Fuels (UT) brought NdPr online in 2024 and plans Dy/Tb output in 2025 from monazite feeds; eventually the **late‚ÄëHREE fraction (Er‚ÄìLu, incl. Tm)** could be produced in kilogram‚Äë to small‚Äëtonnage quantities, but no Tm volumes are published. **Indicative 2030 U.S. Tm: \< a few t/yr**, unless a dedicated late‚ÄëHREE circuit is stood up.

* **Australia.** Lynas now separates Dy/Tb (2025); Iluka‚Äôs Eneabba HREE refinery is scheduled mid‚Äëdecade. Both could **produce small Tm cuts** as part of full HREE trains later, but near‚Äëterm product slates emphasize Dy/Tb. **Indicative 2030 AU Tm: single‚Äëdigit t/yr** (if any), contingent on refining scope.

* **Europe & Japan.** No mining; limited HREE separation. Separated Tm by 2030 would be **trace‚Äëlevel** unless new feedstocks and dedicated late‚ÄëHREE circuits are financed.

* **Allied total (2030).** Summing realistic paths (U.S. heavy‚ÄëREE lines maturing; AU HREE refineries online; minor EU/Japan tolling), **separated allied Tm is likely only in the low‚Äësingle‚Äë to low‚Äëdouble‚Äëdigit t/yr range** by 2030 (best case perhaps **\~10‚Äì20‚ÄØt/yr**). The balance of allied demand would remain **import‚Äëreliant**.

---

## **References for volumes (most load‚Äëbearing)**

* **Global Tm oxide \~50‚ÄØt/yr:** widely cited in technical summaries (e.g., Lenntech). [dggs.alaska.gov](https://dggs.alaska.gov/pubs/id/30821?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **China final demand model for Tm (\~208‚ÄØt in 2020\) & high volatility:** peer‚Äëreviewed analysis in *Sustainable Development* (Wiley).

* **U.S. rare‚Äëearth mine output & context:** USGS Mineral Commodity Summaries 2024/2025 (Rare Earths).

* **Allied HREE separation progress:** Lynas separation of Dy/Tb (first outside China) and Iluka‚Äôs Eneabba refinery schedule.

* **U.S. midstream build‚Äëout:** Energy Fuels‚ÄîNdPr on spec (2024); heavy‚ÄëREE (incl. Tb) targeted for 2025, with Sm+ and heavy‚ÄëREE concentrates in production.

* **Laser market growth benchmark:** global fiber‚Äëlaser market CAGR outlook.

*Note on uncertainty:* Tm statistics are sparse; many sources repeat legacy estimates. Where ranges are given above, they reflect that uncertainty.

---

## **Key Discovery Technologies**

* **Radiometrics for placer indicators.** Monazite/xenotime placers associated with Th/U can be highlighted via airborne gamma surveys (Th‚Äëchannel anomalies), a classic approach for heavy‚Äëmineral sands in the SE U.S. and elsewhere.

* **Deposit models & mapping.** Carbonatite and peralkaline intrusive systems (and their weathered regoliths) remain the primary hard‚Äërock REE targets; USGS models guide mapping and sampling programs that can vector toward HREE‚Äëbearing xenotime.

* **Geophysical & geochemical screening.** High‚Äëresolution magnetics/gravity to outline intrusions; stream‚Äësediment/soil ICP‚ÄëMS (tracking Y‚ÄìYb anomalies as xenotime proxies) to narrow drill targets. (General method per USGS models.)

---

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **Mining & beneficiation.** Dredge/open‚Äëpit of heavy‚Äëmineral sands; spirals and magnetic/electrostatic separators to make zircon/ilmenite/monazite/xenotime concentrates (where Tm resides).

* **‚ÄúCracking‚Äù & leaching.** Acid cracking (H‚ÇÇSO‚ÇÑ/HCl) of monazite/xenotime to dissolve REEs into chloride/sulfate liquor for separation‚Äîflowsheets used commercially (e.g., Lynas LAMP; Energy Fuels for monazite feeds).

---

## **Key Separation Technologies**

* **Solvent extraction (SX) cascades.** The workhorse for splitting lanthanides; hundreds of mixer‚Äësettler stages with organophosphorus extractants (e.g., D2EHPA, Cyanex‚Äëtype). HREE cuts (Dy/Tb first priority) come before late‚ÄëHREE polishing (Er‚ÄìTm‚ÄìYb‚ÄìLu).

* **Advanced membranes/IX (pilot).** Supported liquid membranes (D2EHPA) and chelating resins can sharpen heavy‚Äëlanthanide separation and reduce organic use, but remain pilot‚Äëscale for industrial Tm. (General technology line‚Äîsee research literature summarized alongside SX.)

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **Metallothermic reduction & vacuum purification.** Standard route is chlorination of purified Tm oxide to TmCl‚ÇÉ, followed by **calciothermic reduction** (or related metallothermic steps) to metal; **vacuum distillation**/remelting removes residuals. These unit operations are well‚Äëestablished for lanthanides. [AZoM](https://www.azom.com/article.aspx?ArticleID=7960&utm_source=chatgpt.com)[UNT Digital Library](https://digital.library.unt.edu/ark%3A/67531/metadc677483/m2/1/high_res_d/464131.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Molten‚Äësalt electrolysis (R\&D/limited).** Direct reduction of Tm halides in LiCl‚ÄìKCl or CaCl‚ÇÇ melts is feasible and used for some REEs; industrial Tm metal output is tiny, so this remains specialty practice. [UNT Digital Library](https://digital.library.unt.edu/ark%3A/67531/metadc677483/m2/1/high_res_d/464131.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies**

* **Mineral‚Äësands tailings management.** Monazite contains Th; standard practice is controlled handling, possible REE recovery, and safe return/encapsulation of residual radioactive fractions; extensive **water recycle** in dredge operations.

* **Closed‚Äëloop hydromet.** Neutralization and metals precipitation, with recovery of REEs from process waters (IX or precipitation), reduce discharge and can recapture trace HREEs like Tm. (Industry‚Äëstandard hydromet practice as referenced across separation literature.)

---

## **Key Bottleneck technology for US and Allies Domestic Production**

* **Late‚ÄëHREE separation capacity.** The limiting factor is **midstream separation**‚Äîspecifically, the scarcity (outside China) of full‚Äëchain SX trains that run past Dy/Tb to **Er‚ÄìTm‚ÄìYb‚ÄìLu** in meaningful volumes. Lynas‚Äô Dy/Tb milestone is important but does **not** yet translate into material Tm tonnage; U.S. builds (e.g., Energy Fuels) are prioritizing NdPr and early HREEs. Until allied operators finance and operate late‚ÄëHREE circuits continuously, separated Tm supply onshore will remain **single‚Äëdigit tonnes** at best.

### **Bottleneck summary (2‚Äì4 sentences)**

Thulium is rare in most allied feedstocks and‚Äîcrucially‚Äîsits at the **very end of the separation train**, where allied capacity is thinnest. While Australia and the U.S. are now proving Dy/Tb separation, **industrial‚Äëscale Er‚ÄìTm‚ÄìYb‚ÄìLu** circuits are still largely absent outside China. As a result, even if allied mines and mixed concentrates grow, **onshore Tm** will stay limited without dedicated late‚ÄëHREE SX capacity. Near‚Äëterm planning should assume **continued import reliance** for Tm through 2030\.

---

### **Quick takeaways**

* **Today:** Allied **separated Tm ‚âà 0‚Äìfew t/yr**; world production is only **\~50‚ÄØt/yr**. [dggs.alaska.gov](https://dggs.alaska.gov/pubs/id/30821?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **2030 demand (allies):** **\~50‚Äì120‚ÄØt/yr (Tm‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ‚Äëeq)**, dominated by lasers/medical/photonics; uncertainty is high given sparse public data.

* **2030 supply (allies):** **\~10‚Äì20‚ÄØt/yr** in a best‚Äëcase where AU/US late‚ÄëHREE circuits mature; otherwise **single‚Äëdigit t/yr**. Imports fill the gap.

# Neodymium

## **US and Allies Domestic Current Production (tons)**

* **United States ‚Äî Mountain Pass (MP Materials, CA).**  
   In 2024 MP delivered **\>45,000 t** of rare‚Äëearth oxides (REO) contained in concentrate from Mountain Pass and produced **\~1,294 t of NdPr oxide** after commissioning its separation lines. That is the only primary US source of neodymium today. [Investing.com](https://www.investing.com/news/transcripts/earnings-call-transcript-mp-materials-q4-2024-sees-revenue-beat-eps-miss-93CH-3882259?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia ‚Äî Lynas Rare Earths (Mt Weld, WA).**  
   Lynas is the largest Nd producer outside China. In FY2025 to date, it reported **1,509 t of NdPr oxide in Jan‚ÄìMar 2025** and **\~4,478 t over Jul ‚Äô24‚ÄìMar ‚Äô25**, and is **aiming for \~10,500 t/yr** of NdPr oxide with its expansion program. [ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0301420717300077?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/supply-of-rare-earth-magnets-wont-keep-with-demand-by-2040-report/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Canada / EU‚Äë27+UK / Norway / Iceland / Japan.**  
   These allies currently have **no commercial-scale primary Nd production**; activity is focused on projects, pilot processing and recycling, with imports filling demand. (Context on Europe‚Äôs reliance and project pipeline is consistent with the cited demand/supply sources below.)

**Snapshot:** Among US/allies, **Australia and the US** account for essentially all primary allied neodymium output today‚Äîon the order of **a few thousand tonnes of NdPr oxide per year**, heavily dominated by Lynas and MP. [Investing.com](https://www.investing.com/news/transcripts/earnings-call-transcript-mp-materials-q4-2024-sees-revenue-beat-eps-miss-93CH-3882259?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/supply-of-rare-earth-magnets-wont-keep-with-demand-by-2040-report/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **US and Allies Domestic Demand 2030 (tons)**

* **Main driver: NdFeB magnets.** Nd demand is dominated by Nd‚ÄëFe‚ÄëB permanent magnets for **EV traction motors**, **industrial motors** and **wind turbines**. Policy and OEM guidance point to robust growth in the 2020s. Adamas Intelligence projects **magnet‚ÄëREE demand growth (\~7.1% CAGR)** outpacing supply (\~5.1%), with a **\~19,000‚Äët NdPr oxide global deficit by 2030** if new capacity lags. [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/supply-of-rare-earth-magnets-wont-keep-with-demand-by-2040-report/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Wind power intensity.** Direct‚Äëdrive and hybrid wind turbines use substantial NdFeB mass‚Äî**\~80‚Äì700 kg NdFeB per MW depending on design**‚Äîwith offshore units at the high end. Planned US/EU offshore buildouts imply steady allied Nd pull through 2030\. [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**Planning range:** Rolling up EVs, wind, and other electrification uses, a **US+allies** requirement on the order of **\~10,000‚Äì15,000 t/yr of NdPr oxide by 2030** is a defensible range (i.e., a large fraction of forecast global needs), consistent with the magnet deficit outlook above. [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/supply-of-rare-earth-magnets-wont-keep-with-demand-by-2040-report/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **US and Allies Domestic Supply 2030 (tons)**

* **MP Materials (USA).** MP has ramped NdPr oxide production (2024: **\~1.3 kt**) and is integrating **US metal and magnet making in Texas**. A recent SEC filing details a planned **US 10,000‚Äët/yr sintered NdFeB magnet facility** (the ‚Äú10X Facility,‚Äù commissioning targeted in **2028**) and a **10‚Äëyear US NdPr price floor of $110/kg** intended to underpin upstream investment. These moves position MP to lift **US Nd/Pr availability materially by 2030** (several kt/yr, contingent on ore, separation, and metal lines). [Investing.com](https://www.investing.com/news/transcripts/earnings-call-transcript-mp-materials-q4-2024-sees-revenue-beat-eps-miss-93CH-3882259?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[SEC](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1801368/000119312525157310/d43796dex991.htm?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Lynas (Australia, with processing in WA/Malaysia & US).** Lynas‚Äô expansion plan **targets \~10.5 kt/yr NdPr oxide** in the mid‚Äë2020s; maintaining that cadence through 2030 would keep Australia as the principal allied Nd supplier. [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/supply-of-rare-earth-magnets-wont-keep-with-demand-by-2040-report/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Other allied projects.** Additional Nd units could come from Arafura (Nolans), Hastings (Yangibana), and US/EU separation lines now under construction, but most are not yet at commercial scale.

**Summation:** Realistically, by **2030** the allied bloc could be producing **\~10‚Äì15 kt/yr of NdPr oxide** (Lynas \~10 kt \+ MP several kt \+ smaller additions) ‚Äî **still short** of allied demand growth trajectories, keeping imports part of the mix. [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/supply-of-rare-earth-magnets-wont-keep-with-demand-by-2040-report/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[SEC](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1801368/000119312525157310/d43796dex991.htm?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **References for volumes (selected)**

* **MP Materials:** 2024 NdPr oxide production **\~1,294 t** (company earnings call transcript). Also 2024 REO in concentrate **\>45,000 t** (company‚Äëquoted figure summarized in trade press). [Investing.com](https://www.investing.com/news/transcripts/earnings-call-transcript-mp-materials-q4-2024-sees-revenue-beat-eps-miss-93CH-3882259?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
