[ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0301420717300077?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/supply-of-rare-earth-magnets-wont-keep-with-demand-by-2040-report/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Global balance:** Adamas Intelligence forecast of a **\~19,000‚Äët NdPr oxide deficit by 2030** (magnet‚ÄëREE demand vs. supply). [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/supply-of-rare-earth-magnets-wont-keep-with-demand-by-2040-report/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Wind magnet intensity:** **\~80‚Äì700 kg NdFeB/MW** (design‚Äëdependent) used for demand attribution. [The Department of Energy's Energy.gov](https://www.energy.gov/sites/default/files/2024-12/Neodymium%2520Magnets%2520Supply%2520Chain%2520Report%2520-%2520Final%5B1%5D.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **US magnetization build‚Äëout:** SEC exhibit describing **US 10,000‚Äët/yr NdFeB** magnet capacity plan and **$110/kg NdPr** price‚Äësupport mechanism. [SEC](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1801368/000119312525157310/d43796dex991.htm?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Discovery Technologies**

* **Airborne radiometrics (Th/U),** **soil/stream geochemistry** and **high‚Äëresolution magnetics/gravity** to vector carbonatites/alkaline intrusions and monazite/bastn√§site systems (pre‚Äëdrill targeting for deposits like Mountain Pass and Mt Weld). [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_Pass_Rare_Earth_Mine?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Mineralogy‚Äëled targeting (bastn√§site/monazite/xenotime)** confirmed by petrography and XRD/SEM on core; these dictate downstream processing choices. [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bastn%C3%A4site?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **Open‚Äëpit hard‚Äërock mining** (drill‚Äëblast, load‚Äëhaul) for carbonatite ores;

* **Physical beneficiation**: crushing/milling ‚Üí **flotation** of bastn√§site/monazite ‚Üí gravity/magnetic cleanup to yield \~**concentrate**;

* **Thermo‚Äë/hydrometallurgy**: calcination (drive off CO‚ÇÇ/alter Ce valence) then **acid leach (HCl/H‚ÇÇSO‚ÇÑ)** to dissolve REEs into solution. [Wikipedia+1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_Pass_Rare_Earth_Mine?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Separation Technologies**

* **Solvent extraction (SX)** cascades (organophosphorus extractants, staged pH control) to split light‚ÄëREEs and isolate an **Nd/Pr stream**, often preceded by **selective oxidation** and removal of Ce(IV).

* **Ion‚Äëexchange / chromatographic polishing** for high purity;

* **Precipitation** (oxalate/carbonate) and calcination to **Nd‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ / NdPr oxide** saleable specs. [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bastn%C3%A4site?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **Metallothermic reduction** (e.g., Ca‚Äëreduction of NdCl‚ÇÉ/NdF‚ÇÉ) to Nd metal;

* **Vacuum refining/distillation** to remove residual Mg/Ca and volatiles;

* **Alloying & magnet fabrication**: melt Nd/Pr with Fe‚ÄìB (and coercivity dopants where needed), powderize, align, sinter, and finish to NdFeB magnets. (US lines now being built to onshore this step.) [SEC](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1801368/000119312525157310/d43796dex991.htm?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies**

* **Acid neutralization & co‚Äëprecipitation** to remove Th/U and REEs from process liquors (lime/alkali).

* **Water ‚Äúpolishing‚Äù** (adsorbents/IX) to very low REE levels before discharge;

* **Tailings re‚Äëtreatment** (re‚Äëleach \+ SX) to recover residual REEs while shrinking legacy footprints‚Äîturning waste into feedstock. (These flows mirror established REE practice around bastn√§site/monazite circuits.) [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bastn%C3%A4site?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

---

## **Key Bottleneck technology for US and Allies Domestic Production**

* **Mid‚Äëstream separation and magnetization capacity.** The chokepoint is not geology but **chemical separation (SX) and downstream metal/magnet manufacturing** at scale. Forecasts show **NdPr demand outpacing supply** toward 2030; allied efforts (US/AU) are adding separation and **10,000‚Äët/yr US magnet** capacity, but the sector still needs multiple parallel SX trains and metalization lines to balance demand. [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/supply-of-rare-earth-magnets-wont-keep-with-demand-by-2040-report/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[SEC](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1801368/000119312525157310/d43796dex991.htm?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

### **Key Bottleneck summary (2‚Äì4 sentences)**

Allied ore supply exists, but converting concentrates into **separated Nd/Pr oxide** and then into **metal/magnets** remains the rate‚Äëlimiter. Even with MP/Lynas expansions, **processing/magnet capacity** must scale faster than mine output to close the projected **NdPr shortfall by 2030**. Build‚Äëout of SX, metal reduction and sintered magnet lines‚Äîplus recycling‚Äîwill determine how much of allied demand can be met domestically. [MINING.COM](https://www.mining.com/supply-of-rare-earth-magnets-wont-keep-with-demand-by-2040-report/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[SEC](https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1801368/000119312525157310/d43796dex991.htm?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

# Silicon

# Antimony

## **US and Allies Domestic Current Production (tons)**

* **United States ‚Äî primary mine output: 0 t.** The U.S. has no active antimony mines today; apparent U.S. consumption in 2024 was \~**24,000 t** and net import reliance \~**85%**. The USGS also notes China imposed export licensing on Sb in Aug‚Äë2024 and, in Dec‚Äë2024, **banned exports of antimony to the U.S.**, underscoring supply risk. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)  
   *Note:* United States Antimony (Montana) refines imported concentrates but does not change the ‚Äú0 t‚Äù mine figure. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

* **Canada ‚Äî primary: \~0 t.** No active Sb mines; historic Beaver Brook (NL) has been largely inactive in recent years. Canada depends on imports/recycling. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

* **Australia ‚Äî small, but non‚Äëzero.** Mandalay Resources‚Äô **Costerfield** mine (VIC) produces gold‚ÄØ+‚ÄØantimony; in **Q2‚Äë2024 it produced \~359 t Sb**, implying **\~1,000‚Äì1,400 t/y** if sustained. In parallel, **Nyrstar/Trafigura‚Äôs Port Pirie** complex received **A$135‚ÄØm** government support (Aug‚Äë2025) and plans an **antimony pilot plant**, shifting some Sb production on‚Äëshore as a **by‚Äëproduct** of imported lead concentrates. [Alkane Resources](https://mandalayresources.com/site/assets/files/3895/mnd_press_release_q1_2025_production_sales_final.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Nyrstar](https://www.nyrstar.com/resource-center/press-releases/transitionary-funding-secured-for-nyrstar-australias-critical-metals-processing)

* **European Union / Norway / Iceland ‚Äî primary: \~0 t.** No operating Sb mines; the bloc remains import‚Äëdependent. (Some secondary recovery from smelters/recycling exists but is small.) [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

* **Japan ‚Äî primary: 0 t.** Japan has no Sb mines; demand is met via imports. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

**Global context.** World mine production in 2024 was about **100,000 t**, with **China \~48%** and the rest mostly Russia and Tajikistan‚Äîleaving allies structurally short of primary supply. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

---

## **US and Allies Domestic Demand 2030 (tons)**

* **Use profile.** In the U.S. (a good proxy for allied usage), 2024 end‚Äëuses were **\~39% flame retardants**, **\~40% metal products** (chiefly antimonial lead for batteries & ammunition), and **\~21% non‚Äëmetal products** (glass, catalysts, chemicals). [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

* **Growth drivers (to 2030).**

  * **Flame retardants** (electronics, building materials) remain the largest sink; regulation‚Äëdriven FR formulations sustain demand. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

  * **Batteries & metals.** Lead‚Äëacid remains ubiquitous for start‚Äëstop vehicles, backup/industrial power; antimonial lead persists despite EV growth. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

  * **Solar/PV glass & specialty chemicals** add steady incremental use in the U.S. and EU. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

* **Order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude demand (allies, 2030).** Starting from the U.S. **\~24 kt** in 2024 and assuming modest growth plus EU/Japan/other allied needs, a **planning range of \~30‚Äì45 kt/y** for combined U.S.+allies by 2030 is defensible (EV transition does not eliminate lead‚Äëacid; FR and PV glass expand; defense steadies). China‚Äôs licensing/ban episodes in 2024 also point to precautionary **stockpiling**, which can raise near‚Äëterm pull. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

---

## **US and Allies Domestic Supply 2030 (tons)**

* **United States (Perpetua/Stibnite, Idaho).** The **Stibnite** project obtained its key federal Record of Decision; Perpetua says the mine could meet **‚Äúmore than 35% of U.S. antimony demand‚Äù** at steady state‚Äîequivalent to **\~8‚Äì9 kt/y** on today‚Äôs consumption base. First production is guided for the **late 2020s**. [Invalid URL](https://chatgpt.com/)

* **United States Antimony (Montana).** Smelting/refining of imported concentrates is ongoing, with potential throughput expansions by decade‚Äôs end (scale not disclosed publicly). [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

* **Australia (two streams).**

  1. **Costerfield**: on current run‚Äërates, **\~1‚Äì1.4 kt/y** Sb. 2\) **Port Pirie**: government‚Äëbacked studies target **Sb by‚Äëproduct** output (pilot first, with scope to scale). Combined Australian allied supply could reach **\~1.5‚Äì3 kt/y** by early‚Äë2030s if both sustain. [Alkane Resources](https://mandalayresources.com/site/assets/files/3895/mnd_press_release_q1_2025_production_sales_final.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Nyrstar](https://www.nyrstar.com/resource-center/press-releases/transitionary-funding-secured-for-nyrstar-australias-critical-metals-processing)

* **EU / Norway / Iceland.** No mines expected online by 2030; **recycling and by‚Äëproduct recovery** might contribute **‚â§1 kt/y**. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

* **Japan.** No primary production; refining changes would be marginal. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

**Summing a realistic allied picture (2030):** U.S. **Stibnite \~8‚Äì9 kt/y** \+ U.S. Antimony (small, imported feed) \+ Australia **\~1.5‚Äì3 kt/y** \+ EU recycling **‚â§1 kt/y** ‚áí **\~10‚Äì15 kt/y** allied supply if projects deliver‚Äî**still below projected allied demand (\~30‚Äì45 kt/y)**, implying continued import reliance and/or stockpiling. [Invalid URL](https://chatgpt.com/)[Nyrstar](https://www.nyrstar.com/resource-center/press-releases/transitionary-funding-secured-for-nyrstar-australias-critical-metals-processing)[U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

---

## **References for volumes**

* **USGS Mineral Commodity Summaries 2025 ‚Äî Antimony.** U.S. 2024 apparent consumption **24 kt**, leading uses **FR 39% / metal products 40% / non‚Äëmetal 21%**, world mine production **100 kt**, China‚Äôs 2024 **export licensing** (Aug) and **ban on Sb exports to the U.S.** (Dec). [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

* **Perpetua/Stibnite (Reuters).** Mine permitted; **\>35% of U.S. demand** potential; DoD backing. [Invalid URL](https://chatgpt.com/)

* **Australia ‚Äî Costerfield (Mandalay) production.** Q2‚Äë2024 **\~359 t Sb**, indicating \~1‚Äì1.4 kt/y scale. [Alkane Resources](https://mandalayresources.com/site/assets/files/3895/mnd_press_release_q1_2025_production_sales_final.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Australia ‚Äî Port Pirie (Nyrstar/Trafigura).** **A$135 m** transitionary funding; **antimony pilot plant** planned. [Nyrstar](https://www.nyrstar.com/resource-center/press-releases/transitionary-funding-secured-for-nyrstar-australias-critical-metals-processing)

---

## **Key Discovery Technologies**

* **Geological mapping & geochemistry (Sb‚ÄëAu epithermal systems).** Field mapping of quartz‚Äìsulfide veins plus soil/stream‚Äësediment geochemistry for **Sb, As, Tl, Au** pathfinders remains the primary discovery workhorse in districts like Idaho‚Äôs Stibnite. [Invalid URL](https://chatgpt.com/)

* **Induced‚Äëpolarization (IP) & resistivity.** Sulfide‚Äërich stibnite veins create **high‚Äëchargeability** anomalies that help trace blind ore shoots beneath cover.

* **Hyperspectral/alteration mapping.** Kaolinite/sericite/iron oxide alteration halos around Sb veins can be mapped by multispectral/hyperspectral imagery to vector drilling.

* **Data integration.** Combining structural models with geochemistry/geophysics (ML‚Äëassisted targeting) shortens drill campaigns in mature terranes.

---

## **Key Extraction Technologies**

* **Mining.** Narrow, steep **stibnite (Sb‚ÇÇS‚ÇÉ)** veins are mined by underground methods (decline access, cut‚Äëand‚Äëfill or long‚Äëhole stoping). Bulk tonnage is rare; selective mining reduces dilution.

* **Physical beneficiation.** **Gravity** (jigs/tables) to pre‚Äëconcentrate dense stibnite, followed by **flotation** (xanthate/sulfide collectors) to concentrate Sb sulfide.

* **Roasting to oxide.** Fluidized‚Äëbed or multiple‚Äëhearth **oxidation roasting** converts Sb‚ÇÇS‚ÇÉ ‚Üí **Sb‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ** (antimony trioxide) and produces a saleable FR‚Äëgrade oxide or an intermediate for metal reduction; **SO‚ÇÇ** is captured in acid plants.

* **(Alt.) Pressure leach.** Autoclave **chloride/sulfate** leaching of fine concentrates can solubilize Sb (and co‚Äërecovered Au), enabling hydromet flows where smelting is constrained.

---

## **Key Separation Technologies**

* **Roast ‚Üí oxide route.** Controlled oxidation produces **Sb‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ** (FR feedstock).

* **Pyromet reduction to metal.** **Sb‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ \+ 3Fe ‚Üí 2Sb \+ 3FeO** (or using coke/Fe‚ÄìSi in shaft/electric furnaces) yields **antimony metal** typically 99‚Äì99.5%.

* **Electro‚Äërefining (select cases).** Chloride or alkaline electrolytes refine crude Sb to high purity; used where ultra‚Äëlow impurities are required.

* **Vacuum distillation/zone refining.** High‚Äëpurity Sb (99.95%+) via staged evaporation and re‚Äëcondensation; zone‚Äëmelting for semiconductor grades.

---

## **Key Purification & Refinement Technologies**

* **Hydro‚Äëpyro hybrids.** Pressure‚Äëleach to solution ‚Üí precipitation/solvent extraction ‚Üí calcine to **Sb‚ÇÇO‚ÇÉ** ‚Üí pyromet reduction to metal.

* **Alloying & decanting.** Molten Sb‚ÄìPb alloys can be fractionated by controlled cooling; largely superseded by direct roast/reduction but still relevant in legacy circuits.

* **High‚Äëpurity finishing.** Multi‚Äëpass **vacuum distillation** or **zone refining** to semiconductor/battery grades.

---

## **Key Remediation Technologies**

* **AMD control & metals precipitation.** **Lime/alkali** neutralization precipitates Fe‚Äëoxyhydroxides that co‚Äësorb **Sb**; sludge is dewatered/contained.

* **Constructed wetlands.** Passive polishing of Sb‚Äëbearing drainage using iron‚Äërich substrates and microbial processes to immobilize antimonate/antimonite species.

* **Adsorptive polishing.** **Granular ferric hydroxide, modified biochar, mesoporous alumina** beds to capture dissolved Sb before discharge.

* **Tailings covers & revegetation.** Sulfide‚Äëbearing Sb tailings require water covers or engineered caps plus **phytostabilization** to curb erosion and dust.

---

## **References for mining technologies**

* **USGS MCS 2025 (Antimony)** ‚Äî end‚Äëuse shares, U.S. consumption, supply posture, and China‚Äôs 2024 export licensing/ban events. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

* **Reuters (Perpetua/Stibnite)** ‚Äî ROD granted; mine could meet **\>35%** of U.S. demand. [Invalid URL](https://chatgpt.com/)

* **Mandalay (Costerfield)** ‚Äî Q2‚Äë2024 **359 t Sb** production; demonstrates active Australian Sb output. [Alkane Resources](https://mandalayresources.com/site/assets/files/3895/mnd_press_release_q1_2025_production_sales_final.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Nyrstar/Port Pirie** ‚Äî **A$135 m** transitionary government support; aim to **pilot antimony** production at Port Pirie. [Nyrstar](https://www.nyrstar.com/resource-center/press-releases/transitionary-funding-secured-for-nyrstar-australias-critical-metals-processing)

---

## **Key Bottleneck technology for US and Allies Domestic Production**

* **Smelting & refining capacity (and know‚Äëhow).** The chokepoint is not geology but **midstream processing**: large‚Äëscale roasters, oxide plants and metal refineries are sparse outside China. China also tightened **technology controls** (e.g., export‚Äëcontrol on **‚Äúgold‚Äëantimony smelting and separation‚Äù** know‚Äëhow), making replication harder/faster in the West. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/what-is-antimony-why-is-china-curbing-its-exports-2024-08-16/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Knock‚Äëon constraints.** Environmental permitting for SO‚ÇÇ/particulate controls, scarce specialized equipment (roasters, high‚Äëtemp fuming furnaces, vacuum distillation), and skilled operators all slow capacity build‚Äëout. Result: even with new ore (e.g., Stibnite), **domestic conversion to Sb metal/oxide** is the critical gap. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)

### **Key Bottleneck summary (2‚Äì4 sentences)**

Allied antimony supply is constrained primarily by **processing capacity**, not ore. With no U.S./EU mine base and few Western **roast/reduction** complexes, concentrates depend on foreign smelters. China‚Äôs 2024 licensing and the **Dec‚Äë2024 ban on Sb exports to the U.S.** exposed that vulnerability, while export‚Äëcontrol on antimony smelting technology further complicates catch‚Äëup. Unless allies add integrated **roaster ‚Üí oxide ‚Üí metal** capacity, even marquee mines like Stibnite will not fully close the allied supply gap. [U.S. Geological Survey](https://pubs.usgs.gov/periodicals/mcs2025/mcs2025-antimony.pdf)[Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/what-is-antimony-why-is-china-curbing-its-exports-2024-08-16/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **1\) US & allies ‚Äì current production (2024)**

   USGS‚Äôs final 2024 **mine production (lithium content)** shows **Australia 88,000 t** and **world total (ex‚ÄëUS) 240,000 t**, putting Australia near **37%** (not 60‚Äì70%). Australia is still the largest single producer.

   *Ownership note:* **Mt Marion** is **Mineral Resources (50%) / Ganfeng (50%)**, not Albemarle/Tianqi. **Greenbushes** is operated by Talison and owned **51% by Tianqi/IGO JV and 49% by Albemarle**. [Mineral Resources](https://www.mineralresources.com.au/our-business/lithium/mt-marion/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Talison Lithium](https://www.talisonlithium.com/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

[Investing News Network (INN)](https://investingnews.com/daily/resource-investing/battery-metals-investing/lithium-investing/lithium-production-by-country/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **2\) US & allies ‚Äì 2030 demand**

* **Your text:** ‚ÄúAlbemarle projects global demand \~3.3 Mt LCE by 2030‚Ä¶ US & allies at \~30‚Äì50% implies \~1‚Äì1.7 Mt LCE (\~190‚Äì320 kt Li) per year by 2030\. For example, reaching 50% EV market share in the US & EU would consume \~100‚Äì200 kt Li‚ÇÇCO‚ÇÉ annually.‚Äù

* **Verdict:** **Mixed.**  
   **Global 2030 demand at \~3.3 Mt LCE** from Albemarle is **correct** per **FT** coverage.  
   **The US/EU ‚Äúexample‚Äù (100‚Äì200 kt Li‚ÇÇCO‚ÇÉ at 50% EV share)** is **too low by several‚Äëfold.** A simple check: in **2023**, **battery demand for lithium** was already **\~140 kt Li (content)** globally (‚âà **745 kt LCE**), before any 50% EV share in US/EU. By 2030, if US and EU together sold \~14 million EVs/year (50% of \~28M light‚Äëvehicle sales), and each EV averaged \~30‚Äì40 kg **LCE** (‚âà60 kWh pack √ó \~0.5‚Äì0.6 kg LCE/kWh), that alone implies **\~420‚Äì560 kt LCE** just for new EVs in US+EU‚Äî**well above 100‚Äì200 kt LCE.** [IEA](https://www.iea.org/reports/global-ev-outlook-2024/trends-in-electric-vehicle-batteries?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0921344921003712?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

**What to change:** Keep Albemarle‚Äôs **3.3 Mt LCE (2030)**, but drop/replace the 100‚Äì200 kt LCE example. A defensible 2030 order‚Äëof‚Äëmagnitude for **US+EU combined** is **several hundred thousand tonnes LCE/yr** for EVs alone, plus grid storage. [IEA](https://www.iea.org/reports/global-ev-outlook-2024/trends-in-electric-vehicle-batteries?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **5\) Key discovery technologies (geophysics & mapping)**

* **MT/CSAMT for brines:** Reasonable; MT can image conductive brine systems in closed basins. (Case studies available from Abitibi Geophysics.) [ageophysics.com](https://www.ageophysics.com/en/useful-resources/case-studies-and-news?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Gravity for pegmatites:** **Revise the density statement.** Spodumene‚Äëbearing **pegmatites are typically *less dense*** than common **mafic** hosts (e.g., amphibolite), so they appear as **gravity lows**; gravity can still help where contrasts are favorable. Your sentence says ‚Äúoften higher density,‚Äù which is generally the opposite of what‚Äôs used in practice. [ResearchGate](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/362600400_Application_of_Microgravity_Survey_in_the_Exploration_of_Rare-metal_Bearing_Pegmatites_-_A_Case_Study_from_Marlagalla_Mandya_District_Karnataka?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[MDPI](https://www.mdpi.com/2075-163X/12/12/1498?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Magnetics/UAV‚Äëmag:** Fair with caveats‚Äîpegmatites themselves are often weakly magnetic; magnetics help via **structure/host** contrasts rather than a strong intrinsic pegmatite signature. (GREENPEG & recent reviews discuss the limits.) [Lyell Collection](https://www.lyellcollection.org/doi/10.1144/SP526-2021-189?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Geologic mapping/geochem; remote sensing:** Directionally fine.

## **7\) Separation & refining technologies**

* **Ion exchange / adsorption:** Fine; widely piloted (e.g., Lilac, Standard Lithium). [Standard Lithium Ltd.](https://www.standardlithium.com/investors/news-events/press-releases/detail/186/smackover-lithium-successfully-completes-derisking-of-dle?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Membranes & electrodialysis:**  
   Your claim that **bipolar‚Äëmembrane electrodialysis (BMED/EEDBM) converts LiCl to LiOH** is supported by peer‚Äëreviewed work; **commercial use remains limited**. Cite scientific sources rather than vendor generalities. [MDPI](https://www.mdpi.com/2297-8739/11/5/146?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[PMC](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9963233/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

Replace the Fluence/MOF sentence with peer‚Äëreviewed examples of **Li/Mg‚Äëselective membranes** (e.g., **Nature Communications 2024**). [Nature](https://www.nature.com/articles/s41467-024-46887-4?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[fluencecorp.com](https://www.fluencecorp.com/using-membranes-to-recover-lithium-from-wastewater/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Spodumene conversion:** The sequence **Œ±‚ÜíŒ≤ conversion (\~1000‚Äì1100‚ÄØ¬∞C) ‚Üí acid roast (H‚ÇÇSO‚ÇÑ) ‚Üí water leach ‚Üí precipitation** is standard; citing a technical review would strengthen this. [Valmet](https://www.valmet.com/globalassets/sharepoint/imported/2911_03_06en.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[ScienceDirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S2096519223008601?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **8\) Remediation & byproducts**

* **Membrane‚Äëbased water treatment:** Keep Fluence as an **RO/NF provider** for mining water, but **do not attribute MOF membranes or specific Li‚Å∫ selectivity figures to Fluence**. [fluencecorp.com+1](https://www.fluencecorp.com/nirobox/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

* **Fluidized‚Äëbed Li‚ÇÉPO‚ÇÑ granulation / co‚Äëprecipitation / bio approaches:** These remain **early‚Äëstage**; cite peer‚Äëreviewed pilot studies where possible (I didn‚Äôt see your exact MDPI Li‚ÇÉPO‚ÇÑ paper, but the concept is plausible as research).

* **Site‚Äëspecific examples (e.g., epsomite at Thacker Pass):** The **Thacker Pass** flowsheet clearly features **sulfuric acid leach** and extensive **lime/soda ash** use; be careful not to over‚Äëspecify polishing/side reactions beyond what‚Äôs in the technical report summaries. [Q4 Capital](https://s203.q4cdn.com/835901927/files/doc_presentations/2025/01/Technical-Report-December-2024.pdf)

## **9\) Bottlenecks**

* **Your thesis:** ‚ÄúScaling refined lithium output and proving DLE; Western refineries delayed; Albemarle shelved SC refinery.‚Äù

* **Verdict:** **Well founded, needs precise citations and dates.**  
   Albemarle **paused/deferred** the **$1.3‚ÄØbn South Carolina** LiOH project, citing economics amid price slump; the CEO reiterated in **May‚ÄØ2025** that the ‚Äúmath doesn‚Äôt work‚Äù without support. This is a solid example of the **refining bottleneck** in the West. [Reuters+1](https://www.reuters.com/markets/commodities/lithium-producer-albemarle-cut-workforce-lower-spending-2024-2024-01-17/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **Suggested text edits (targeted)**

1. **U.S. production:** replace with

    *United States:* **Non‚Äëzero** ‚Äì commercial production from Albemarle‚Äôs **Silver Peak** brine operation in Nevada; USGS withholds the exact volume, but confirms U.S. mine production exists.

2. **Australia share:** replace ‚Äú60‚Äì70%‚Äù with

    **\~37% of 2024 world mine output (Li content)**; Australia \= **88 kt Li**, world total (ex‚ÄëUS) \= **240 kt Li**.

3. **Canada projects:** replace producing sites with

    2024 production mainly from **North American Lithium (Sayona‚ÄìPiedmont JV)** in Qu√©bec and **Tanco** (Sinomine) in Manitoba; **Whabouchi** and **Moblan** are **not yet producing**. [Sayona Mining](https://sayonamining.com.au/projects/nal-project/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)[Tancomine](https://tancomine.com/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

4. **EU:** replace ‚Äúessentially zero‚Äù with

    **Small but non‚Äëzero.** **Portugal** produced **\~380 t Li** in 2024; **AMG Lithium** opened Europe‚Äôs **first battery‚Äëgrade LiOH refinery** in Germany (20 kt/y module). [electrive.com](https://www.electrive.com/2024/09/18/amg-lithium-opens-first-lithium-refinery-in-europe/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

5. **Thacker Pass:**

    **Claystone project** with **Phase 1 \~40 kt/y Li‚ÇÇCO‚ÇÉ**, ultimate plan up to **160 kt/y** over phases; first production shown **post‚Äë2027** in company timeline. [Q4 Capital](https://s203.q4cdn.com/835901927/files/doc_presentations/2025/01/Technical-Report-December-2024.pdf)

6. **Hard‚Äërock grades:**

    **Ore** grades typically **\~1‚Äì3% Li‚ÇÇO** (e.g., Greenbushes 2023‚Äì24 feed \~2.2% Li‚ÇÇO). **SC6** (\~6% Li‚ÇÇO) is **concentrate**, not ore. [IGO Limited+1](https://www.igo.com.au/site/pdf/483721a4-afe7-4723-a907-6efce0c66748/Greenbushes-CY23-Resources-and-Reserves.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

7. **2030 demand example:**

    Replace the 100‚Äì200 kt LCE figure with **several hundred kt LCE** for US+EU EVs alone at 50% share; globally **\~3.3 Mt LCE** demand in 2030 (Albemarle). [IEA](https://www.iea.org/reports/global-ev-outlook-2024/trends-in-electric-vehicle-batteries?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

8. **Membranes:**

    Attribute high Li/Mg selectivity claims to **peer‚Äëreviewed studies** (e.g., **Nature Communications 2024**), not to Fluence. [Nature](https://www.nature.com/articles/s41467-024-46887-4?utm_source=chatgpt.com)

## **Bottom line on conclusions**

* **Core conclusion (supply shortfall without more refining/DLE):** Directionally **right**. Western **refining** capacity and **commercial‚Äëscale DLE** remain the weak links; multiple projects paused or staged (e.g., Albemarle SC refinery). **But** your numeric comparison badly **understates allied mine supply** if Australia is included and **understates US/EU demand** at a 50% EV share. Tightening those numbers strengthens, not weakens, your argument. [Reuters](https://www.reuters.com/business/energy/albemarle-ceo-says-math-doesnt-work-us-lithium-refinery-project-2025-05-01/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
